    第一卷

    　　吴封翁
    　　霅溪吴封翁，富而好德。生二子先后举孝廉，亦佐乃翁济急扶危，以成善事。乾隆丁未岁饥，二子皆出助赈。翁无所事，止息于园庭以养静。因山林空旷，以防宵小。
    　　除夕，请翁入宴。二婢执烛前导，翁仰见树端伏人，即止不进。嘱二婢曰：「汝等留烛于亭，归告太夫人，我守静已久，不愿赴热闹场，可移樽独酌，以适我意。」太夫人知翁性情，不敢拂，命仆移筵就之。翁屏退家人，仰树呼曰：「树上君子，此间已无外人，曷来一叙耶？」树上人闻之，战栗几坠。翁曰：「老夫岂执汝哉？毋恐。」其人下，叩首称死罪。翁视之，邻人某也。邀入亭中，曰：「现备酒肴，先酌三杯，以御严寒。姑告所需几何，助汝可也。

    First Volume

    Wu Fongong
    Wu Fongong of Zhe River, wealthy and virtuous. He had two sons who successively passed the examination for filial piety and integrity. They also assisted their father in helping the needy and alleviating crises, thus completing good deeds. In the year of Dingwei during the Qianlong era, when there was a famine, both sons went out to assist in relief efforts. With nothing to do, Wu Fongong rested in the garden to cultivate tranquility. Due to the vastness of the mountains and forests, he took precautions against mischievous people.
    On New Year's Eve, he was invited to a banquet. Two maids carried candles ahead to guide him. Looking up, Wu Fongong saw someone crouching at the top of a tree and stopped, not advancing. He instructed the maids, saying, "You can leave the candles in the pavilion and return to inform my wife. I have been in seclusion for a long time and do not wish to attend a noisy gathering. You can move the wine to here for me to drink alone, as it suits my mood." Knowing Wu Fongong's temperament, his wife did not dare to dissuade him and ordered the servants to move the banquet to the pavilion. Wu Fongong dismissed his family and called out to the tree, saying, "Gentleman on the tree, there are no outsiders here. Why don't you come down and talk?" The person on the tree, upon hearing this, trembled and almost fell. Wu Fongong said, "Old man, I would not detain you. Do not be afraid." The person came down, knelt and confessed his grave offense. Wu Fongong looked at him and recognized him as a neighbor. He invited him into the pavilion and said, "We have prepared food and wine. Let us drink three cups first to ward off the cold. Please tell me what you need, and I will help you."

    3

    」邻人泣对曰：「小人有母，不幸遇荒年，无以卒岁。素稔翁家富有，故行此不肖事耳。」翁曰：「不能周济邻居，以至为非，老夫之过也。汝其饱餐，当以二十金畀汝，卒岁之余，小作贸易，足以度日矣。切勿再为此事，他人不汝恕也。一成盗名，则为捕役鱼肉，没齿不能掩盖。且陷老母于不义。其奈之何？」邻人益感泣，叩首无算。翁乃予银，并布裹食物，送之墙下，曰：「归遗尔母。汝仍出此，勿使我家人知，以留汝颜面。」邻人缘墙而去。方唤家人，见杯盘狼藉，翁忽有兼人之量，且疑且喜。

    Explanation

    3

    The neighbor wept and replied, "I have a mother, and unfortunately, we have encountered a famine year. I have no means to survive the rest of the year. I always knew the old man's family was wealthy, so I did this despicable thing." The old man said, "Unable to help the neighbor, leading to wrongdoing, it is the old man's fault. You should eat your fill. I will give you twenty taels of silver. With the remainder of the year, do some small trade, which will be sufficient to get by. Do not do this again; others will not forgive you. If you gain a reputation as a thief, you will be prey to the constables, and you will not be able to hide it for the rest of your life. And you will involve your mother in wrongdoing. What can be done about it?" The neighbor wept even more and knocked his head against the ground countless times. The old man then gave him the silver and wrapped some food in cloth, sending it down to him under the wall, saying, "Take it and give it to your mother. You still climb over this wall, do not let my family know, to preserve your dignity." The neighbor climbed over the wall and left. Just as he was calling his family, he saw the tableware in disarray. The old man suddenly had an extra-large capacity, both suspicious and pleased.

    4

    后十余年，长公子发甲，官至大中丞。次公子亦入词林，提督学院。翁受二品封而卒。会葬之日，戚友以千计。忽有灵隐寺方丈大和尚来，侍者云从，祭品丰洁。俯伏柩前，哭之恸甚。中丞慰谢之，而不知是何交情。和尚造膝密告曰：「僧本邻居，前曾为盗，蒙老大人不责其罪，反以廿金为助，藉以奉母。母卒，弃去为僧，苦志虔修。今入方丈，称大禅师，皆老大人之德有以成之。僧不敢忘，谨以实告。」吴氏乃知其事云。

    Explanation

    4

    More than ten years later, the elder son, having passed the imperial examinations, reached the position of Grand Censor. The younger son also entered the Hanlin Academy and served as the supervisor of the imperial academy. The elder master received a second-rank imperial title and then passed away. On the day of the funeral, relatives and friends numbered in the thousands. Suddenly, the abbot of Lingyin Temple, a senior monk, arrived with his attendants. The sacrificial offerings were abundant and clean. He knelt before the coffin and cried with great sorrow. The Grand Censor comforted and thanked him, but did not understand the reason for his deep emotion. The abbot whispered confidentially, saying, "I was once a neighbor of the elder master. Before, I had committed theft, but the elder master did not punish me. Instead, he gave me twenty gold coins as assistance to support my mother. After my mother's death, I left to become a monk, striving diligently and practicing sincerely. Now, I have become the abbot and am called Great Zen Master, all due to the virtue of the elder master. I will never forget this, and I carefully and truthfully tell you this." The Wu family then learned of his story.

    5

    芗厈曰：此不难于济助，难于惟恐人知。谆谆告诫，俾改行从善，是为阴德。
    　　
    　　难女
    　　余舅金氏，以上海之洋行为业。自置洋船五，在东西两洋贸易。每船必有标客以御盗贼。甲子春，船将开行，大宴标客。招优演剧，甚盛设也。标客自然首座，傲睨一切。余舅命其子侄陪宴，皆少年好事之辈。见客倨甚，切切私议，欲试其能。半酣小歇，肃客入园散步，坚请试其技。客左右顾，见道旁有卧柳，曰：「此碍步，请为公子去之。」迅以掌劈柳本，截然中断，如斧劈者。众皆咋舌。

    Explanation

    5

    Xiang Yan said: It is not difficult to help someone, but it is difficult to do so without being noticed. Repeatedly advising and encouraging someone to change their ways and become good is considered an act of hidden virtue.

    The Difficult Woman

    My maternal uncle, Mr. Jin, is engaged in maritime trade in Shanghai. He owns five foreign ships and conducts trade in both the East and West Oceans. Each ship must have a guard to protect against thieves. In the spring of the year 1844 (Jiashen year), the ship was about to set sail, and a grand banquet was held for the guards. Entertainers were invited to perform, and the banquet was very elaborate. The guards naturally took the first seats and looked down on everything and everyone else. My uncle ordered his nephews and nieces to accompany him to the banquet. They were all young and eager to try their skills. Seeing the guards' arrogance, they whispered and discussed among themselves, wanting to test their abilities. During the banquet, they took a short break and invited the guests to take a walk in the garden. They insisted on testing their skills. The guard looked around and saw a lying willow by the path. He said, "This obstructs the way, please allow me to remove it for the young master." He quickly chopped the base of the willow with his hand, and it was cut cleanly in half, like it was cut with an axe. Everyone was amazed and gasped.

    6

    当其时，有淮阳难民过境，沿肆乞钱。内有处女，矫矫不群，亦随众募化。至洋行，轻薄之伙以一钱投之，女怒叱曰：「视汝姑为何如人，而以一钱为戏耶？今日罚汝千钱，不然吾不行矣。」随坐大门坎以阻人出入。时脚夫运糖包至，每包约重百七八十觔，皆壮而多力者，肩之疾趋。至大门，见女碍路，喝之起。女故张其肱阻之。脚夫怒，作失手势，以糖包压之。女接而投掷，不甚费力。群夫大哗，佥以糖包共压女。女无惧色，左抵右抛如弄丸然，纷纷飞出市头，反将群夫击退。

    Explanation

    6

    At that time, refugees from Huaiyang were passing through, begging for money along the streets. Among them was a young woman who stood out for her proud and independent nature, and she also joined in the begging. When they reached the foreign trading company, a group of disrespectful men threw a single coin at her. The woman angrily rebuked them, saying, "What kind of people are you, treating a coin as a joke? Today, I will fine you a thousand coins, or I will not let you pass." She then sat at the entrance to block people from entering and exiting. At that moment, porters carrying heavy sugar packets arrived; each packet weighed about one hundred and seventy to eighty pounds, and all were strong and powerful, rushing forward with great speed. Upon reaching the entrance, they saw the woman blocking the way and shouted at her to move aside. The woman deliberately extended her arms to block them. The porters became angry and, in a threatening gesture, tried to use the sugar packets to push her aside. The woman caught the packets and threw them back with little effort. The porters became agitated and, in unison, tried to use the sugar packets to overwhelm her. But the woman showed no fear, skillfully deflecting and throwing the packets to the sides as if they were balls, sending them flying out of the market. In the end, she successfully repelled the porters.

    7

    女大怒曰：「汝曹欺压孤女，使之内伤。罪在不赦，非多给钱养伤，事不能已矣。」时吆喝之声达于内，主人止戏，客亦出观。少年共议曰：可以观客之长矣。随激客曰：「我等观此女之力，恐无敌于世。客能退之否？」客视女弱甚，曰：「吾以二指提之出矣。」攘臂而前，女以一掌拍客胸，跌去数丈，入柜内如菩萨座。内外哗然，老主人出，命仆扶客入。以千钱赠女，好言劝之去。方叱少年滋事。入视标客，已从后户遁矣。少年兄弟密议曰：若得此女保标，谅海洋无敌手。其兄欲买以为妾。

    Explanation

    7

    The woman became very angry and said, "You all bullied the orphan girl, causing her internal injury. The crime is unforgivable, unless you pay more money for her medical treatment, the matter cannot be settled." The shouting reached inside, and the host stopped the play. The guests also came out to watch. The young men discussed and said, "It can be seen how the guest is skilled." They then provoked the guest by saying, "We have seen the strength of this woman. She might be unmatched in the world. Can the guest make her retreat?" The guest looked at the woman and thought she was very weak. He said, "I can lift her out with just two fingers." He advanced with his arms raised. The woman struck the guest's chest with one hand, and he fell back several feet, falling into the cabinet as if sitting on a Buddha's seat. There was a commotion inside and outside. The old host came out, ordered the servant to help the guest inside, gave the woman a thousand coins, and spoke kindly to her to leave. He then scolded the young men for causing trouble. He went inside to see the guest, but the guest had already fled through the back door. The young men and their brothers secretly discussed and said, "If we get this woman to protect our bet, we can be sure there is no match in the world." His brother wanted to buy her as a concubine.

    8

    次日闻官以舟与资，将护送难民出境。少年兄弟访至马头，挨舟觅女，见舱中坐一叟，衣冠虽破，冠蓝顶冠。女侍其侧，方絮絮教训，女俯首垂泪。少年登舟拜之，叟喝女退。出迎，肃客入坐。少年曰：「叟居何职，因何窘迫至是？」叟曰：「老夫淮之山阳人，忝为都阃，以老致仕。不意今夏雨甚河决，田庐皆没，不能不随众觅食。老夫无子，只有一女，年方及笄。昨因乞钱，用泰山压顶势伤一标客。女子何可逞强，擅动煞手，败人衣食。老夫正训斥之。」少年极誉女能，问将焉往。叟曰：「老夫亲家为渐军水师提督，婿亦开府矣，将送女完姻。而老夫依以终身也。」少年诺诺而退。

    Explanation

    8

    The next day, the official provided boats and funds to escort the refugees out of the country. The young brothers visited the boat landing and searched through the boats for the girl. They saw an old man sitting in a cabin, his clothes and hat though worn, he was wearing a blue-topped hat. The girl was standing by his side, and he was repeatedly teaching her, while she bowed her head and tears streamed down her face. The young brother boarded the boat and bowed to him. The old man ordered the girl to step back. He came out to greet the young brother and invited him to sit down. The young brother asked, "What position does the old man hold, and why is he in such a difficult situation?" The old man replied, "I am from Huai's Shanyang, humbly holding the position of a military officer, and I retired due to old age. Unfortunately, this summer there was heavy rain and the river overflowed, submerging all my fields and houses, so I could not help but follow the crowd to seek food. I have no sons, only one daughter, who is just coming of age. Yesterday, because she was begging for money, she used the force of a falling mountain to injure a traveler. How can a woman show off strength, arbitrarily use deadly force, and ruin someone's livelihood? I am scolding her now." The young brother highly praised the girl's ability and asked where they were going. The old man said, "My relative is a naval commander of the Jian Army, and my son-in-law has also established his own office. We are sending the girl to complete her marriage. And I will rely on her for the rest of my life." The young brother nodded affirmatively and withdrew.

    9

    芗厈曰：女子之强者，功胜于男子，何也？其心专也。昔闻献县来一绳伎，有姿首。方开场作剧，有武举能开十四石弓者，以元恶霸一方，纵淫，无敢与较。见此女投所好，强欲留宿。班主曰：「我等卖艺不卖身。客何犯我规耶？」武举怒，拳击班主伏地。众皆曰：「此武举官人也，良家妇女尚不敢抗。尔等既卖伎，何敢拂之，自取苦恼耶？」女子乃笑，迎武举而慰解之曰：「官人果与妾有情，请以夜持五十金来。否则，不能承也。」武举哂曰：「五十金非难事，果处子亦不为费。」

    Explanation

    9

    Xiang Yan said: Strong women outperform men in their achievements. Why is this so? It is because their minds are focused. Once, I heard of a rope performer from Xian County who was exceptionally beautiful. Just as they were starting their performance, there was a martial arts champion who could draw a bow of fourteen stones, a notorious villain who dominated a region and indulged in licentious behavior, and no one dared to challenge him. Seeing this woman catering to his preferences, he forcibly wanted to stay overnight. The master of the troupe said, "We sell our performances, not ourselves. Why do you break our rules?" The martial arts champion became angry and punched the master of the troupe to the ground. Everyone said, "This is the martial arts champion, even respectable women would not dare to resist. You all are selling your performances, so why do you dare to defy him, causing yourselves trouble?" The woman then smiled and greeted the martial arts champion, trying to pacify him, saying, "If the official truly has feelings for me, please bring fifty taels of gold at night. Otherwise, I cannot comply." The martial arts champion sneered, "Fifty taels of gold is not a difficult matter, even if she is a virgin, it will not be a waste."

    10

    入夜至女室，置五十金案头曰：「可以共卧矣。」女曰：「妾请先睡，官人能犯妾，任意为之。如其不能，请留金而送客。」武举曰：「汝不过欲盖羞耳。何有于是？」女子乃闭门，去衣俯伏炕上。武举腾身上，以两手翻其躯，竟如铁铸，莫动分毫。随作开弓势，尽平生之力劈分两股。力尽而股不稍移。武举怒击其臀，坚如石。遍击首背，皆然，拳反作疼，乃伏其背，以柔情动之，闻女子酣呼睡熟。播弄终夕，无可如何。迟明，女子跃起曰：「官人既不伤妾，妾亦无伤于官人，请留金而退可也。」武举从此力脱而死。嗟乎，色与力不可并用，并用必内伤自毙。彼武举何坠女子之术中而不悟，此为恶之报也。吁，可戒矣！

    Explanation

    10

    At night, the martial candidate entered the woman's room and placed fifty gold coins on the table, saying, "We can sleep together now." The woman replied, "I will sleep first. If you can do anything to me, go ahead. If you cannot, please leave the gold and send me away." The martial candidate said, "You are just trying to cover up your shame. What's there to it?" The woman then closed the door, took off her clothes, and lay down on the kang. The martial candidate jumped onto her and tried to turn her body, but she was as hard as iron, not moving an inch. He then made a bowing gesture and used all his strength to split her legs. Exhausted but her legs did not move. The martial candidate hit her buttocks angrily, which were as hard as stone. He hit her head and back, all the same, and his fists hurt instead. He then lay on her back and tried to move her with gentle affection, hearing the woman snoring deeply, asleep. He played with her all night, unable to do anything. By late morning, the woman leapt up and said, "Since you did not harm me, I will also not harm you. Please leave the gold and go away." The martial candidate died of exhaustion from that point on. Alas, lust and strength cannot be used together; using them together will cause internal injury and death. Why did that martial candidate fall into the woman's trap without realizing it? This is the punishment for evil. Alas, it is a warning.

    11

    语怪(七则)
    　　怪者，圣人所不语也。而商羊萍实载在《家语》，何也？有理可明，虽怪犹常；若无情理，徒骇人听闻，斯圣人不语。然同一怪事，有理无理，庸愚所不能明。姑志之以俟达者。
    　　粤东臬署二堂后院有榕树一株，其本三人合抱，其末高七八丈，扶疏广荫。树有神甚灵，故建庙立碑。凡臬使必以礼虔祀，朔望演剧，则安然无事。若稍有懈怠，神即显形，绯袍乌帽，据坐公案，必有殃咎。是以无敢渎者。道光壬寅，乔廉访在任，有僮溺树侧，立即疯狂，操刀飞舞，砍尽书院芭蕉数十本。主人缚僮谢罪而后已。有仆不信其事，故溺之。神情顿迷，入房抽剑插胸，数刃透背。人见之惊喊，仆曰：「无伤也。」自拔出剑，而血不流，惟前后红痕一线而已。不言痛，亦不变色，饮食如常。主人虑其有变。资遣回籍。

    Explanation

    11

    Strange Tales (Seven Cases)

    Strange things are not spoken of by sages. Yet, the stories of Shang Yang and Ping Shi are recorded in the Family Instructions (Jia Yu), why is that? If there is a rational explanation, even strange things can be considered normal; if there is no reason or logic, they are merely shocking, and thus sages do not speak of them. However, for the same strange event, whether it has reason or not, ordinary people may not understand. Let us record it and wait for someone wise to understand.

    In the rear courtyard of the second hall of the judicial office in Guangdong, there is a banyan tree. Its trunk is so large that three people can embrace it, and its branches reach seven or eight zhang high, providing lush and expansive shade. The tree is said to have a spirit that is very powerful, so a temple was built and a stele erected. All magistrates must worship it with reverence and ritual, performing plays during the full moon and new moon, and everything will be peaceful. If there is any neglect, the spirit will manifest, appearing in a red robe and black hat, sitting on the public bench, and there will be misfortune. Therefore, no one dares to show disrespect. During the Renyin year of the Daoguang era, Qiao, the magistrate, was in office. One of his servants urinated near the tree and immediately went mad, wielding a knife and dancing, cutting down dozens of banana plants in the academy. The master tied the servant up and apologized, and the servant calmed down. Another servant did not believe the story and urinated near the tree. He suddenly became confused, entered the room, drew a sword and stabbed his chest, the blade piercing through his back. People saw this and shouted in alarm, but the servant said, "It's not hurt." He pulled out the sword, and blood did not flow, only a thin red line remained. He did not complain of pain, nor did his complexion change, and he ate and drank as usual. The master feared something might happen and provided funds to send him back to his hometown.

    12

    又前任公子当署宴客，爱树阴清凉，移席其下。无云而雨，着菜上，皆臭秽不可食，宾主败兴而散。
    　　又前使族人，昼寝于榕树堂侧室，忽睹云雾中一蟒奔床前，惊骇逸出。觅得鸟枪，实贮火药，将往击之。或问其故，其人以前事告，或往觇之，毫无形迹。其人指蟒卧案下，遂携枪执火，潜入帐内。觉又奔之，即燃枪轰击，响震远近，其人昏迷伏地矣。众皆聚观，见窗纸尽裂，鸟枪断折。其人尚昏迷未觉，而两手如截，连腕脱去。遍觅之，不见枪筒与手所在。乃救其人醒，问之，曰：「枪鸣时，即震惊而毙，不觉手之脱，与枪之折也。」噫，此更异矣。凡鸟枪贮药过多则裂，尚有情理可言。然不能销熔铁筒与人之手也。或曰其人曾亵树神，故有此怪事。

    12

    Again, the former nobleman was hosting a banquet and loved the cool shade of the trees, so he moved the seating area under them. Suddenly, rain fell without clouds, spoiling the vegetables on the table, making them foul-smelling and inedible. The guests and hosts left in disappointment.

    Again, a family member was taking a daytime nap in a side room of the banyan tree hall when they suddenly saw a python rushing towards the bed in the mist. They fled in terror. Finding a bird gun and loading it with gunpowder, they prepared to confront the snake. Someone asked the reason, and the person explained the previous incident, with no trace remaining. Sneaking into the tent, they felt the snake rush again and immediately fired the gun, causing the sound to echo far and wide. The person fainted and fell to the ground. The window paper was all torn, and the bird gun broke. The hands were cut off, along with the wrists. Searching everywhere, they did not find the gun barrel or the hands. Then, they saved the person and woke them up. Asking about the incident, the person said, "When the gun fired, I was shocked and fainted, not realizing my hands were cut off and the gun was broken." Ah, this is even more strange. Generally, if a bird gun is loaded with too much gunpowder, it will explode, but it cannot melt the iron barrel or the person's hands. Some say the person had disrespected the tree deity, leading to this strange event.

    13

    吾乡有朱氏翁，年周甲，为米市伙。其为人也，严以正己，和以接物，故人皆亲之。每出行，遇有碍足之物，必去净而后已。见棺椁之暴露者，必为掩盖。一日索逋至野，见破冢内有巨瓮，白镪满中。翁恐目迷，方捡阅间，冢旁农人觏之，奔而前曰：「此我祖父墓也，方因雨破。汝徘徊其间，毋盗是墓中物耶？」翁谢过曰：「原物归君，我未动毫厘也。」农人识翁，故挥之去。而呼其兄弟子侄来曰：「冢中不知谁氏物，露我目中，天其富我乎，盍共取之。」众皆合力起出，视瓮中盘旋蠕动，皆毒蛇也。农人恚曰：「翁先见此，而曰原物，戏我实甚，我其还戏之。」众曰诺。共舁瓮至翁宅后，俟其寝息，升屋拨瓦而倾之。翁夫妇跃起曰：「天雨金矣，姑趋避之。」候雨定而后捡较，得数千金，家以是富。彼农人倾毕，负空瓮归，方自以为得计也。

    Explanation

    13

    In my hometown, there lived an elderly man surnamed Zhu, who had reached the age of sixty and worked in the rice market. He was strict in self-discipline and gentle in dealing with others, so people all loved him. Whenever he went out, he would remove any obstacles that hindered his path until they were cleared. If he saw exposed coffins, he would cover them up. One day, while collecting debts in the countryside, he found a large jar in a broken tomb, filled with silver coins. Fearing he might lose his way, he began to examine the contents when a farmer from the nearby area saw him and ran up, saying, "This is my grandfather's grave, which was damaged by rain. Are you wandering here, not stealing the contents of the tomb?" The old man apologized and said, "The original owner should get their property back; I have not touched a single coin." The farmer recognized the old man and dismissed him, then called his brothers, nephews, and cousins, saying, "The contents of the tomb are unknown, but they have appeared before my eyes. Heaven is bestowing wealth upon us, so let us all take it." They all worked together to lift the jar out, and upon looking inside, they saw venomous snakes writhing and moving. The farmer became angry and said, "The old man saw this first and said it was the original owner's, playing a trick on me. I will play a trick on him in return." They all agreed. They carried the jar to the old man's house, waited until he and his wife were asleep, climbed onto the roof, and tipped the jar over. The old man and his wife jumped up, saying, "Heaven is raining gold, let us quickly move away." After waiting for the "rain" to stop, they counted the treasure and found several thousand silver coins, which made their family wealthy. The farmer, after tipping the jar, carried the empty jar back home, thinking he had gained an advantage.

    14

    或曰：金银之气，上属青龙。蛇，龙类也，故变幻及之。凡南方人家，蛇多者必富，殊不然也。昔某家有婢，闻空室叮当之声，趋视之，梁上一翠色四足蛇，方吐钱着地。婢奔告主母，偕往观之，蛇去钱存，仅十余枚耳。异日，又闻房中铮铮然，婢探之。见翠蛇据床顶上，吐钱盈席矣。又报主妇走观，则蛇不见，捡得时钱千余文。妇以告主。其家本小康，意谓神欲益其富，盛设祭祀。自此蛇不复来，而家随中落。

    Explanation

    14

    Someone said: "The qi (vital energy) of gold and silver rises to the Azure Dragon. The snake, being a kind of dragon, is thus affected by transformation." It is said that households in the south with many snakes will become wealthy, but this is quite not so. In a certain household, a servant heard a clinking sound in an empty room and hurried to see what it was. On the beam, she saw a green four-legged snake that was spitting coins onto the ground. The servant ran to tell the mistress, who went with her to see it. When they arrived, the snake was gone, but the coins remained, only about ten or so. Later, the servant heard again a clinking sound in the room and investigated it. She saw a green snake perched on the top of the bed, spitting coins all over the mat. She reported this to the mistress, who went to see it. By the time the mistress arrived, the snake was not there, but they collected at that time over a thousand coins. The mistress told the master. The family was originally modestly well-off and thought that the god wanted to increase their wealth, so they held a grand sacrifice. From then on, the snake did not come back, and the family subsequently declined.

    15

    浙有诸生某，名宿也。久困场屋，在闱中，艺毕诗成，吟诵间，四鼓人静，忽见青面撩牙，凹胸凸肚，一怪当面，生胆素壮，不甚惧。徐问曰：「汝来何为？」怪曰：「吾得一佳作，欲助有福者抡元，遍觅闱中，惟汝可。」生曰：「试诵之。」怪曰：「香油煎鲞香，豆油炒千张。二语不甚佳乎？」生曰：「此孩童急口令也，若以为文，笑死万人，且玷我声名实甚。」举砚欲击之。怪出朱笔点其额，不觉首肯，竟录其词作破，怪大笑而没。以下皆己作也，录毕缴卷，若忘其事者。二三场悉尽心为之，受卷所不贴。誊录照缮而入。是科座主，系名公卿，卷落一同考官处，乃以翰林散馆出为令者，亦自命不凡，阅此卷破题，不觉大笑，致颔颏振脱，张口不能言。仆扶入室，卧不起。座主与考官有年谊，往候其疾。

    15

    A certain scholar from Zhejiang, a renowned scholar, had long been trapped in the examination halls. While in the examination room, having finished his essay and composed a poem, he was reciting it when, at the fourth drum, when people were quiet, he suddenly saw a grotesque creature with a green face, fanged mouth, sunken chest, and protruding belly standing before him. The scholar, who was known for his courage, was not overly frightened. He asked calmly, "What brings you here?" The creature replied, "I have obtained a fine piece of work and wish to help someone with good fortune win first place. I have searched throughout the examination hall, and only you are suitable." The scholar said, "Try reciting it." The creature recited, "Cooked fish with sesame oil is fragrant, fried tofu with soybean oil is delicious. Are these two lines not somewhat good?" The scholar replied, "This is a tongue twister for children. If you take it as a literary work, it would laugh to death a thousand people, and it would greatly tarnish my reputation." He lifted the inkstone to strike the creature. The creature took out a red pen and marked his forehead. Unconsciously, the scholar nodded in agreement, and the creature finally recorded the words as the solution. The creature laughed loudly and disappeared. The following were all his own works. After recording, he submitted the exam paper, as if he had forgotten the matter. In the second and third exams, he put his heart into it, but the examiner did not stick to the exam paper. The copy was neatly transcribed and submitted. The chief examiner of this session was a famous high-ranking official. The exam paper fell into the hands of one of the examiners, who was someone demoted from the Hanlin Academy to become a magistrate and considered himself extraordinary. When reading this exam paper's opening, he could not help but laugh, causing his chin to shake off. He opened his mouth but could not speak. His servant helped him into the room, and he lay down and did not get up. The chief examiner had a long-standing friendship with the examiner and went to visit his illness.

    16

    曰：「老年兄素称康强，何忽患此恙？」房官以手指案上卷，笑容可掬。座主检阅数过，不觉钦佩，曰：「老年兄得此佳卷，何虞不入彀耶？我将与副总裁共赏之。」遂携卷去。两主司皆朗诵健羡，谓无出其右者，竟定解元。榜放，同考官之疾自愈，闻此卷发解，忍笑往见座主曰：「大人与职，声名从此扫地矣。是何言也，而可作解首耶？」座主曰：「文实佳甚，岂出老年兄门下，过作谦词乎？」房官曰：「无论下文如何，观其一破，概可知矣。」主司共读之，不觉狂笑曰：「我等皆自开讲阅起，未及详观承破，至有此失，奈何？」考官方全诵之，曰：「文实高超，大人所取允当。无已，请召此生问明其故，易卷可也。」监临速召生来共鞠。生始悟场中之事，以实对。考官曰：「必魁星欲为是科光，故作此戏。不然走马看花之际，恐遗珠耳。」众皆曰然。

    Explanation

    16

    "Sir, you have always been known for your health and strength. How could you suddenly fall ill?" The examiner pointed to a scroll on the table, smiling broadly. The chief examiner reviewed it several times, admiring it, and said, "Sir, with such a fine scroll, why should we worry about it not being selected? I will share in appreciating it with the deputy chief examiner." He then took the scroll away. Both the chief and deputy examiners read it aloud with admiration, agreeing that none surpassed it, and finally decided on the first-place winner. When the results were announced, the co-examiner's illness healed itself. Hearing that this scroll had been selected, he forced a smile and went to see the chief examiner, saying, "Your reputation will be ruined from now on. What do you mean by selecting this as the top scorer?" The chief examiner replied, "The text is indeed very good. Is this an excessive modesty, claiming it is not from the elder brother's hand?" The co-examiner said, "Regardless of what follows in the text, by looking at the first part, one can generally know it." The chief and deputy examiners read it together, unable to contain their laughter, saying, "We all started reading from the opening, did not have time to carefully examine the subsequent parts, and thus made this mistake. What to do?" The chief examiner then read it in full, saying, "The text is indeed highly skilled. The choice made by the chief examiner is appropriate. If there is no other way, please call this student to clarify the reason, and it can be changed." The supervisor quickly called the student to come and explain. The student then realized what happened in the examination hall and answered truthfully. The chief examiner said, "It must be that the God of Literature wanted to shine in this examination, so he played this trick. Otherwise, while looking at things superficially, perhaps out of fear of overlooking a gem." Everyone agreed.

    17

    豫西沈孝廉，名士也。以文会友，卓卓一时。忽患时症，头疼身热。医以生军下之，所下皆白膏。病痊而愚甚。至一丁不识。向之朋友来，议论纵横，孝廉殊愦愦，自亦不知其故。或曰：人能记忆，一切皆在脑，所下白膏，脑脂也。脑减则忘其所有，信如斯言。药补其脑，当能复原矣。何以沈孝廉终身不复也？
    　　
    　　某官保
    　　某宫保未达时，寒士也，卖卜浙之吴山。有鹾商某，武林巨富，生平喜风鉴，书无不览。遇能者，俯首降心，专诚求教，故其术甚精。生一女，自视之合封一品夫人，凡议婚者，必面相攸曰：「非吾女匹。」延至廿余年，无当意者，戚友皆非笑之。时商行香，至庙遇雨，舆不得行，在庙闲玩，过卖卜处，见公骨格非凡，又睹其旋焉而返，足迹印地者皆中满，商大悦，确信为大贵人也。询姓名年庚籍贯，知为旧族，已游泮而未婚，齿又与女相若，曰：「先生步君平后尘，亦属韵事，但不如教学有相长之益。

    Explanation

    17

    A Scholar-Official from Western Henan, known as a man of letters, was renowned for his literary gatherings and his outstanding reputation at the time. Suddenly, he fell ill with a seasonal fever, experiencing headaches and body aches. The physician treated him with a purgative called "Sheng Jun," and what was expelled were all white, greasy substances. Although his illness was cured, he became extremely foolish, unable to recognize even the simplest characters. When his former friends visited and engaged in lively discussions, he was completely confused and did not understand the reason for his condition. Someone said: "Memory lies in the brain, and everything is stored there. The white substance expelled was brain fat. When the brain is reduced, one forgets everything. If this is true, then medicines that replenish the brain should restore one's faculties. Why did Scholar-Official Shen never recover?"

    A High-Ranking Official

    When the official was not yet prominent, he was a poor scholar who sold fortunes in the Wu Mountain area of Zhejiang. There was a wealthy salt merchant in Hangzhou who had a great interest in fortune-telling and had read extensively. He would humbly and sincerely seek guidance from those who were skilled, which made his abilities very refined. He had a daughter who believed she was destined to marry a high-ranking official's wife. Whenever someone proposed marriage, she would look at them and say, "You are not worthy of my daughter." Over twenty years, no suitable match was found, and family and friends mocked her. Once, while the merchant was visiting a temple and it rained, his carriage could not move forward, and he was idly playing in the temple. He passed by a place where fortunes were sold and saw the official, who had an extraordinary appearance and demeanor. He noticed that the official turned around and left, leaving footprints that were deeply imprinted in the ground. The merchant was greatly pleased and firmly believed that the official was destined for greatness. He inquired about the official's name, birth year, and background, learning that he was from an old family, had passed the local examination, and was unmarried, and that his age was similar to his daughter's. He said, "Sir, following in the footsteps of Zi Junping (Zeng Yi), a famous fortune-teller, is also a charming pursuit, but it is better to focus on mutual learning and growth."

    18

    」公曰：「某异乡人，此间无人相识，谁作曹邱者？」商曰：「先生果有意乎？我即主人，请以训我子何如？」公欣诺。商返，具衣冠什物延公，使二幼子受业。阅半载，见其性情通达，学问书法俱佳，遂遣媒纳为赘婿。未几商卒，长子袭父业，渺视公而戏弄之，且不使诸弟入学，曰：「何学丐为？」公读闺中，其夫人讥之曰：「丈夫不能身自振发，而依亲戚为事，妾亦何颜？」公怒欲去，夫人曰：「妾奉严命，相随终身，岂有他志？然不得不劝夫子自立也。今夫子舍妾而去，将焉往？」公曰：「寒苦，我命也，不能仰人鼻息。还我故人，任我所之。」夫人苦留之，不可，竞脱华服，衣故衣，不名一钱，携来时笔砚而去。

    Explanation

    18

    The stranger replied, "I am a stranger from afar, unknown here. Who could act as an introducer?" The merchant said, "If you truly intend to help, I shall be your host and ask if it would be acceptable to teach my children?" The stranger agreed. The merchant returned, prepared clothing, utensils, and other necessities to welcome the stranger, and had his two young sons study under him. After half a year, he saw that the stranger's nature was open and broad-minded, and his learning and calligraphy were both excellent. Therefore, they sent a matchmaker to arrange for him to become a son-in-law. Shortly after, the merchant died, and his eldest son inherited his business. He looked down on the stranger and played pranks on him, and did not allow the younger brothers to attend school, saying, "Why learn to beg?" The stranger read in the inner chamber, and his wife criticized him, saying, "A man cannot lift himself up by his own efforts, and relies on relatives to do things. I also have no face." The stranger became angry and wanted to leave. His wife said, "I have received strict orders to follow you for life. How could I have other intentions? But I cannot help but encourage you to stand on your own. Now, if you leave me, where will you go?" The stranger said, "Poverty and hardship are my fate. I cannot live by breathing on others' noses. Return me to my old friends, let me go where I please." The wife tried hard to keep him, but he would not. Finally, he took off his fine clothes and put on his old clothes, not having a single coin, and took with him the brush and inkstone he brought, and left.

    19

    行至嘉禾，无腰缠，不能前，止于三塔寺，仍举旧业。卜案之左，有星士为人谈命有验，业甚盛，日进制钱数千。因江湖同道，与公往来，觉异于流辈，使书八字俾决之，曰：「阁下当得一品职，若往北行，不久上达，吾推命多矣，决无错谬。」公曰：「承君美意，奈无赀何？」星士曰：「是不难，吾自来此，积十余金，尽以助阁下。十年后，无忘今日，则吾食报多多矣。」公曰：「诚如是，何敢忘？」遂藉其赀，附粮船，达津门，费用将尽。闻保阳有族人业茶者相识，谋往依之，至则其人已歇业南旋矣。皇皇失所，访得同乡数人，皆无力赀助，荐入藩署科房帖写，日得数十钱，仅敷餬口而已。数月，疟疾作，北方以此症无救，谋弃之。主吏悯公，以数百钱纳怀中，乘其昏迷，使工人负出，置古庙庑下。

    Explanation

    19

    Arriving at Jiahe, he found himself without funds and unable to proceed, so he stopped at San Ta Temple and resumed his old profession. To the left of the divination case, there was an astrologer who was skilled in predicting the future and was quite successful, earning several thousand coins daily. Because of their shared profession, the astrologer interacted with the gentleman and felt that he was different from the crowd. The astrologer asked the gentleman to write down his birth date to make a prediction, saying, "You will attain a high-ranking official position. If you travel north, you will soon rise to prominence. I have predicted many times, and there is no mistake." The gentleman replied, "I accept your kind intention, but what can I do without money?" The astrologer said, "It's not difficult. I have accumulated more than ten gold pieces here and will give all of them to you. Ten years later, do not forget today, then I will receive much reward." The gentleman said, "If it is true, how dare I forget?" Thus, he borrowed the astrologer's money, boarded a grain ship, and reached Jinmen. His expenses were almost exhausted. He heard that in Baoyang, there was a relative who dealt with tea and was acquainted with him, so he planned to go and rely on him. When he arrived, the relative had already ceased business and returned south. In a panic and lost, he found several fellow townspeople, but all were unable to provide financial assistance. He was recommended to enter the provincial office's department of letters, earning several dozen coins a day, just enough to buy food. After several months, he contracted malaria, which was considered incurable in the north, and he planned to give up. The head official pitied the gentleman, put several hundred coins in his pocket, took advantage of his confusion, had a worker carry him out, and placed him under the eaves of an ancient temple.

    20

    时大雪压公身，热气得雪而解，醒知其故，忿忿北行。至漕河，雪益大，不辨道路，扑趺入河水，僵不能起。河上有庙，老僧主之，方围炉假寐，梦伽蓝神告曰：「贵人有难，速往救之。」老僧开目，见河内伏一白虎，惊觉出观，则窭人卧雪中，不知死生，不敢救，入室复卧，见伽蓝神怒叱曰：「出家人以慈悲为本，见死不救，祸且及汝。况救之，将兴尔庙。」老僧遂决救之，其徒与火工力阻之，不听，喝往扶公入，去湿衣，温以棉被，进姜汤而苏。僧问行踪，知为儒者，益敬之，为易衣供奉。卒岁，至春暖时，僧谓公曰：「先生功名中人也，此地无可发迹，我师弟主都中隆福寺方丈，王公大人皆与往来，请以一函书，及赀两缗，送先生往投之。」公欣然附车往，见大和尚，志高气扬，非大众比，谓公曰：「既师兄书来，命侍者引入客舍，姑住此以候机缘。」公得住且住，虽饔飧无虑，而衣赀无所出。

    Explanation

    20

    During a heavy snowfall, the cold pressed down on the person, and the heat dissipated upon meeting the snow. Awakening, the person realized the cause and angrily headed north. Upon reaching the canal, the snow fell even heavier, obscuring the path, and the person fell into the river, becoming stiff and unable to move. On the riverbank stood a temple, overseen by an old monk who was sitting by the stove and dozing. In his dream, the temple guardian deity told him, "A noble person is in danger; quickly go to save him." The monk opened his eyes and saw a white tiger crouching in the river. Startled, he woke up and went out to see a poor person lying in the snow, unaware of whether they were alive or dead. Afraid to save them, he returned to his room and lay down again. The temple guardian deity then angrily rebuked him, saying, "Monks are supposed to be compassionate; if you see someone dying and do not save them, disaster will befall you. Moreover, saving this person will bring prosperity to your temple." The monk then decided to save the person. His disciples and the temple workers tried to stop him, but he paid no heed. He shouted for them to help the person in, removed their wet clothes, warmed them with a cotton quilt, and gave them ginger soup, which revived them. The monk asked about the person's journey and learned they were a scholar, thus treating them with greater respect and providing them with new clothes. By the end of the year, as spring warmed, the monk said to the person, "Sir, you are a person destined for success and fame, but there are no prospects for success here. My senior brother is the abbot of Longfu Temple in the capital, and high-ranking officials and nobles all visit him. Please take a letter of introduction and two strings of cash, and I will send you there." The person happily boarded the carriage and arrived at the temple, where the abbot was lofty and spirited, unlike the common monks. He said to the person, "Since my senior brother sent a letter, I will have the attendant lead you to the guest house. Stay here for now and wait for opportunities." The person stayed, and though food was not a worry, there was no money for clothing.

    21

    众僧皆喜公和婉，暇即聚谈，日习见先生书法甚佳，曰：「曷不于庙外售联，则所需有着。」公听之。买者源源而来，日得数百钱，春服藉以告成。时皇太后许书妙法莲华经百部，施舍天下名山，作大功德。上命词林书式，呈览，不合太后意。有旨，旋命诸王在外访善书者。王识大和尚，命书记僧作字进，愈不合旨，王无以应命，惟有责重大和尚而已。乃与众僧谋，一僧以公对，大和尚哂曰：「此不过卖春联之字法耳，何足以当大任？」僧曰：「舍此无人，盍姑试之？」不得已，使公书字，因王进呈。太后大悦，命延入王府，虔诚书经，功成之日，厚酬之。王自来延请，大和尚皇然失措，盛备行装，送公入府。书经告竣。上请问合旨之意，太后曰：「在廷诸臣，非无书法出其右者，第福分届满，即无功德。此人将来必为正直大臣，有功于国，故其书浑厚多力，可与一官酬之。」上奉懿旨，召公见，钦赐举人，以部曹用。遇缺即补。

    Explanation

    21

    The monks all liked the gentleman's gentle and amiable nature. In their leisure time, they would gather to talk, and they often saw the gentleman's handwriting was very good. One day, they said, "Why not sell couplets outside the temple? Then the required materials would be available." The gentleman listened to them. Buyers came in a steady stream, and he earned several hundred coins each day. He managed to complete his spring attire. At that time, the Empress Dowager allowed the writing of one hundred copies of the Lotus Sutra to be donated to famous mountains across the land, to perform a great meritorious act. The emperor ordered the scholars to write the text, to be presented for review, but it did not meet the Empress Dowager's approval. An edict was issued, and the princes were then ordered to find good calligraphers outside the palace. The prince recognized the great monk and ordered him to write and present it, but it still did not meet the emperor's approval. The prince had no way to fulfill the command and could only blame the great monk. He then consulted with the other monks. One monk suggested the gentleman. The great monk laughed and said, "This is just the calligraphy used for selling spring couplets. How could it be suitable for such a significant task?" The monk replied, "There is no one else, why not try him?" Reluctantly, he ordered the gentleman to write, and through the prince, it was presented. The Empress Dowager was very pleased and ordered him to be brought into the prince's mansion to write the sutra with sincerity and reverence. On the day the task was completed, he was generously rewarded. The prince personally invited him, and the great monk was greatly surprised and at a loss. He prepared elaborate travel arrangements and sent the gentleman into the mansion. The writing of the sutra was completed. The emperor asked about the meaning of the Empress Dowager's approval. The Empress Dowager said, "Among the officials in the court, there were those whose calligraphy was superior, but their good fortune had run out, so they had no merit. This person will surely become an upright minister and will do good for the country. Therefore, his calligraphy is robust and full of strength. He can be rewarded with an official position." The emperor received the Empress Dowager's decree and summoned the gentleman to meet him. He was honored with the title of juren and appointed as a departmental official, to be appointed as soon as a vacancy arose.

    22

    时公以书召夫人，夫人复命曰：「妾自夫子去后，心向空门，今已习静，自维不能相夫子。如念结发情，置媵可也。」公思妇翁识拔恩，竟虚内阃。上信公之为人忠诚朴实，一岁三迁，不及十年，官至直隶方伯。未几，总督畿内，星士来见，为之延誉，获重赀去。漕河老僧，时年八十，因公往祝之，文武员弁以公故，争献寿仪，又为倡修庙宇，规模宏大，且在彼立给孤独园。隆冬，收养流民，通省咸置留养局，无饥寒之民。

    Explanation

    22

    At the time, the official sent a letter to summon his wife. The wife responded with a message: "Since my husband left, I have turned my heart toward the monastic life and have now practiced stillness. I believe I cannot assist my husband. If you remember our marriage vows, then you may take a concubine." The official, thinking of the favor his father-in-law had shown him, decided to leave the inner quarters empty. The emperor trusted the official's loyalty, honesty, and simplicity, and within a year, he was promoted three times, reaching the position of Governor of Zhili Province in less than ten years. Soon after, he was appointed to oversee the capital region. An astrologer came to visit, enhancing the official's reputation, and left with a large sum of money. An old monk associated with the canal river, who was eighty years old, was visited by the official to offer his blessings. Civil and military officials, due to the official's presence, competed to offer gifts. The official also initiated the repair of temples on a grand scale and established a monastic garden. During the severe winter, he took in displaced people, and across the province, shelters were established, ensuring no one suffered from hunger or cold.

    23

    在其境又开水田，通河渠，设桥梁，初北人不习种棉，公聘南方男妇导之，作耕织图以进，上为题咏。当公作帖写时，知吏之利弊，故宫文书皆刻颁格式，使吏不能高下其手。又修复义仓，作义仓图，均贮四乡，以便赈济。于是上下肃清，闾阊丰足，上益重之。入觐，询公尚未有子之故，公以实情奏。上为降旨召夫人，不得不来，以命服迎入署。夫人见公再拜曰：「妾来应君命，然马齿长矣，无生育理，仅能主内政而已。请纳如姬。」公不听，上知之，以江南织造所进宫人赐之，生一子。上贤夫人之不妒，加公宫保衔，命正奏为一品夫人，妾赐宜人，其子后亦为大中丞。
    　　芗厈曰：公之善政，所以结主知者，当不止此，不过依客所能言者记之。或曰：「此方宫保讳观承事。」然核公行状及袁简斋先生《随园文集》所载不合，意或鄙俗之事，节去以成体裁。或传述失实，或未可定。惟小说不嫌荒唐，且历言穷达，亦鼓励寒儒之一道也。

    Explanation

    23

    In his jurisdiction, he cultivated paddy fields, dredged rivers and canals, and built bridges. Initially, northerners were unfamiliar with cotton cultivation, so the official invited southerners to teach them. He created illustrations of farming and weaving to present to the emperor, who then composed poetry about them. When the official was drafting documents, he understood the advantages and disadvantages of bureaucracy, leading to standardized formats for official documents, ensuring that officials could not manipulate them. He also restored public granaries, created maps of these granaries, and distributed them across four regions for disaster relief. As a result, society became orderly, and the people were well-provided for, leading to increased respect from the emperor. Upon his audience with the emperor, the emperor asked why the official had no children. The official reported the truth. The emperor then issued an edict to summon the wife, who could not refuse, and she was welcomed into the official's residence in formal attire. The wife bowed twice to the official and said, "I have come in response to your command, but I am of an advanced age and cannot bear children; I can only manage household affairs. Please take another concubine, Ru Ji." The official did not listen, and the emperor, upon learning this, granted a palace woman from the Jiangnan weaving bureau to the official, who then had a son. The emperor praised the wife for her lack of jealousy, and the official was promoted to the position of Palace Guard, with his wife being granted the title of First-Rank Lady, his concubine being given the title of Lady of Ease, and his son later becoming a high-ranking official.

    The commentator, Xiang Yan, said: The official's good governance and the emperor's favor extended beyond what is recorded here, based on what can be recounted by the author. Some say that the official's name is concealed, but discrepancies with other records suggest that certain vulgar details were omitted for propriety. Some accounts may be inaccurate or uncertain. However, in novels, such fanciful elements are not out of place, and they serve to encourage scholars of humble origins.

    24

    黄大王
    　　大王，豫人，前明诸生，生农家，性喜水。幼孤，母抚之。三岁时，母为人浣衣，从井汲水，儿在其侧，嬉戏井旁，照见己影，跃入从之。母瞥见呼救，邻人咸集，见儿坐水上，两手拍弄己影，人见其不沈也，共异之。以绳悬入下，抱之起。至七八岁，母夫人又殁，其姑，渔家妇也，无子，养为己子，儿随姑父母舟中，更以弄水为乐。其姑夫屡次教戒，顽梗如故，厌之。一日，姑夫闲卧舟首，儿激水湿其衣，怒甚。以足蹬儿，坠河中，随波逐流而去。姑见之，急喊：「何杀我儿？不但绝黄氏后，我老何依？」号泣不已。其姑夫曰：「顽童无用，将贻后患，不如早绝之。」夫妇口角时，下游一舟来，问故，曰：「无伤也。离此十余里，有儿戏水中，乐甚，无乃是耶？速往救之，犹可及。」夫妇放舟下，果见儿在水中，抱大鱼出入波间。

    24

    King Huang
    King Huang was a native of Yu, a student from the previous Ming dynasty, born into a farming family, with a nature that loved water. Orphaned at a young age, he was raised by his mother. At the age of three, while his mother was washing clothes for others and drawing water from a well, the boy played by the well, saw his own reflection, and jumped in to follow it. His mother saw this and called for help; neighbors gathered and saw the boy sitting on the water, playing with his own reflection with both hands. People saw that he did not sink and were all surprised. They used a rope to lower him down and lifted him up. By the time he was seven or eight years old, his mother passed away again. His grandmother, a fisherman's wife who had no children, raised him as her own. The boy followed his grandparents on their boat and found even more joy in playing with water. His grandmother's husband repeatedly taught and warned him, but he remained stubborn as before, growing tired of him. One day, while the husband was idly lying at the bow of the boat, the boy splashed water and wet his clothes, angering him greatly. He kicked the boy, causing him to fall into the river, where he went downstream with the current. The grandmother saw this and cried out, "Why did you kill my child? Not only did you cut off the Huang family line, but what will I rely on now that I am old?" She cried continuously. The grandmother's husband said, "A mischievous child is useless and will cause future problems; it's better to get rid of him early." While the couple were arguing, a boat downstream came and asked why. They said, "No harm was done. About ten miles away from here, there was a child playing in the water, very happy, is that him? Go quickly to save him, it's still possible." The couple released their boat downstream and indeed saw the boy in the water, playing with a large fish in the waves.

    25

    其姑如获至宝，扶之登舟而回，知此儿之不能容于其夫也，使受雇为人牧儿。放牛之际，见村童读书，悦之，日往潜听。师出入屡见之，异其勤也，问儿亦解此耶？儿背诵如流，且讲大旨无误。师异之，告居停，使为学。儿受教，益奋。不数年，入庠，居停以女妻之，遂家焉。其姑夫妇相继亡，生无以为业，因设帐焉。秉资颖悟，无书不解，能剖晰至理，为人所服，故从游者众。名大振，为豫藩周王所闻，招为记室。在府数载，值闯贼肆乱，围豫，生知时不可救，去之。购大小舟数十，沿河而上。贼决黄河灌城，将没，生急救周王亲丁及从者数百人载去，贼追之，作五里雾，迷不知所往。或曰，在嵩岳深处，人迹罕到，为王作第隐其间。生仍回家教读。时土寇虽多，皆遥望生村，甲兵隐现，莫敢犯者，避难者佥往依之。恒见侍卫辈，夜以马邀生，周王召之也。

    Explanation

    25

    Her mother-in-law regarded him as a treasure, helped him onto a boat and returned, realizing that this child was not accepted by his husband, and had him hired to herd children. While tending cattle, he saw village children reading and was pleased by it, so he went daily to secretly listen. The teacher often saw him and found his diligence remarkable, asking if the child understood it. The child recited fluently and explained the main ideas correctly. The teacher was amazed and told the host, who then allowed him to study. The child received instruction and became even more diligent. Within a few years, he entered the school, the host married his daughter to him, and he settled down. His mother-in-law and her husband died one after another, leaving him with no means of livelihood, so he set up a teaching hall. He had natural talent and insight, understood no books, could analyze profound truths, and was respected by others, so many followed him. His fame spread widely, and he was heard by the Duke of Yu Zhou, who invited him to be a secretary. He served in the government for several years, during which the rebel Li Zicheng caused chaos, besieged Yu Zhou, and he knew the situation was beyond saving, so he left. He bought dozens of large and small boats and sailed up the river. The rebels broke the Yellow River to flood the city, about to be submerged, he urgently rescued the Duke of Yu Zhou's family and hundreds of followers, and the rebels pursued him, creating a five-mile fog, bewildered and unable to find him. Some say he was in the deep mountains of Song and Yu, rarely visited by people, building a residence for the Duke to hide. He returned home to teach. At that time, although there were many bandits, they all looked at his village from afar, with soldiers appearing and disappearing, none dared to attack, and those seeking refuge all went to rely on him. He often saw guards, who invited him at night on horseback, summoned by the Duke.

    26

    时我大清兵已定豫，使大臣来，河决不能塞，募能建策者，生出应募，指挥筑堤，无不如意。将合龙之际，选四健卒，使抱椿，随扫下，卒惧死不从。生见之，洒泪而谓之曰：「汝四人数合建此大功，享千年奉祀，若不从，受违令之诛，等死耳。与其死无名，何如神长在耶？」四人乐，尽醉持椿入水，血随波泛。椿定埽进，功以成。大臣欲奏官之，生曰：「我明诸生也，既不能死，又从而官之，圣朝安用无耻之徒耶？我之来，为万民恤难，岂为功名？」遂去之。后水退沙涨，运粮河没，千万人不能开，民不堪命，共荐黄生。

    Explanation

    26

    At that time, our Qing army had already pacified the region of Henan. High-ranking officials were sent to come, but the river had broken its banks and could not be blocked. They encouraged those who could propose plans, and I stepped forward to respond to the call. I directed the construction of the embankment, and everything went as planned. At the moment when the dam was about to be completed, four strong soldiers were selected and ordered to hold the wooden piles, following the current and letting them go down. The soldiers were afraid of death and refused. I saw this and shed tears, saying to them, "You four will certainly help complete this great achievement and enjoy eternal worship for a thousand years. If you do not obey, you will be punished for disobeying orders, which is all the same as dying anyway. Would it be better to die without a name or to live on in spirit?" The four soldiers were happy, drank to their hearts' content, and held the wooden piles into the water. Their blood floated with the waves. The wooden piles stabilized the embankment, and the project was completed. The high-ranking officials wanted to recommend me for an official position, but I said, "I am a scholar of the Ming dynasty. Since I could not die, and now they want to appoint me as an official, what use would the holy court have for a shameless person like me? I came here to alleviate the suffering of the people, not for fame and glory." So I left. Later, the water receded and the sand rose, submerging the canal for transporting grain. Thousands of people could not open it, and the people could not bear the burden. They all recommended me (黄生).

    27

    河督召之不来，使民往请命，始至，相度旧河形势已定，曰：「以某月日兴工，颁示居民远避，吾将独力为之。」至日，风雨雷电交作，云雾中见黑龙下垂，天地震动，喧腾之声，如黄流倒泻，如劲敌鏖兵。远近惊惧，如是督三昼夜而定。河督往视之，运河已成，黄生不知所之矣。访之，闻已劳瘁卒。为奏封河神，立庙河干。后凡黄河有事，则神冕旒见波涛间，前驱四将，即抱椿四卒也。所至有功，进封为王，至今河滨有小黄蚘见，河工官弁，即以舆迎之入庙。设享演剧，或留一二日，或三四日，即不见，人咸谓黄大王寄迹也。

    Explanation

    27

    The river commissioner summoned him, but he did not come. He sent people to plead his case, and he finally arrived. He examined the old river's situation and determined its form, saying, "On a certain date, I will start work. I will announce to the residents to stay far away, and I will do it alone." On the day, a storm of wind, rain, thunder, and lightning occurred. From the clouds, a black dragon descended, and the heavens and earth shook. The roaring sound was like the Yellow River pouring out, like fierce enemies clashing in battle. People far and near were frightened. He supervised for three days and nights until it was settled. The river commissioner went to inspect it, and the canal was completed. Mr. Huang disappeared. When asked about him, it was said that he had died from exhaustion. He was posthumously enshrined as a river god, and a temple was built by the riverbank. Later, whenever there was an issue with the Yellow River, the god appeared with a crown and flowing robes in the waves. The four generals leading the way were the same as the four soldiers holding the stakes. Wherever he went, he was successful, and was posthumously enshrined as a king. To this day, a small yellow creature is seen by the riverbank. The river engineers and officials welcomed him into the temple in a carriage. They offered sacrifices and performed plays. Sometimes he stayed for one or two days, sometimes three or four days. When he disappeared, people all said that he was temporarily residing.

    28

    芗厈曰：古语有云，生而为英，死而为灵。王，英豪也，至今游中州，过大王镇者，犹觉凛凛然有生气。王之全传，事迹尚多，此其大略。
    　　
    　　祝由科
    　　祝由一科，其术甚神，凡金枪及跌打死者，顷刻能生之，系湖南破头老祖所传。其祖师，北宋时人，太祖闻其名，召入禁内。时有小臣，不合上意而斩，非其罪者，祖师为续其首而生。太祖怒，使武士以大斧劈祖师，去其脑而弃之。其徒潜移尸回，以术生之，遁深山穷谷间，从此不履尘世矣。逮今千余年，尚存其传。术分两派：一派非重聘不行，一派不受谢礼，见死必救。受业时，各发誓愿，如违教者，身亡家灭，故敬谨奉持不失。楚中惟米客习是术，多不受谢者，故其术甚神。

    Explanation

    28

    芗厈曰：古语有云，生而为英，死而为灵。王，英豪也，至今游中州，过大王镇者，犹觉凛凛然有生气。王之全传，事迹尚多，此其大略。

    The Master Xiang Yan said: Ancient sayings go that one lives as a hero and dies as a spirit. This king was a hero, and even today, those who travel through Central China and pass by Great King Town still feel a chilling yet vibrant energy. The complete biography of the king contains many events and deeds, but this is a brief overview.

    祝由科
    祝由一科，其术甚神，凡金枪及跌打死者，顷刻能生之，系湖南破头老祖所传。其祖师，北宋时人，太祖闻其名，召入禁内。时有小臣，不合上意而斩，非其罪者，祖师为续其首而生。太祖怒，使武士以大斧劈祖师，去其脑而弃之。其徒潜移尸回，以术生之，遁深山穷谷间，从此不履尘世矣。逮今千余年，尚存其传。术分两派：一派非重聘不行，一派不受谢礼，见死必救。受业时，各发誓愿，如违教者，身亡家灭，故敬谨奉持不失。楚中惟米客习是术，多不受谢者，故其术甚神。

    The School of Zhubaoyu
    The School of Zhubaoyu is a remarkable practice, capable of bringing back to life those who have died from spear wounds or falls within an instant. It was passed down by the founder, the Old Ancestor of Broken Head from Hunan. The ancestor, a man of the Northern Song Dynasty, was summoned to the imperial palace by Emperor Taizu upon hearing of his fame. At that time, a minor official who displeased the emperor was executed, but the ancestor, seeing that the man was innocent, reconnected his head and brought him back to life. Enraged, Emperor Taizu ordered his guards to decapitate the ancestor with a great axe, remove his brain, and discard his body. His disciples secretly retrieved the body and used their skills to revive him, after which he retreated to deep mountains and remote valleys, never again stepping into the world. To this day, over a thousand years later, the tradition still exists. The practice is divided into two schools: one requires substantial payment before acting, while the other does not accept thanks or gifts and will always save the dying. When they take up the practice, each makes a solemn vow, and those who violate the teachings face death and the destruction of their family, so they respect and carefully adhere to the teachings without deviation. In the Chu region, only the Rice Guests practice this skill, and many of them do not accept thanks, which is why their practice is so powerful.

    29

    有冯、陈二客，运米至吾乡，投行主出粜，即寓其家。二人同出剃发，坐肆中。凡发匠，吾乡呼曰待诏。有小待诏者，龙阳君也，方与一客用小刀取耳，有棍徒以手挖小待诏之臀，出其不意，待诏惊耸失手，刀尖直刺客脑，客倒地而卧，肆人皆惊惶无措，肆主执棍徒缚之，将以鸣官。冯客谓陈客曰：「我等不能见死不救，曷以术生之？」陈客曰：「诺。」肆主闻之，欲跪求，冯急止之曰：「如此则不能救矣。诚出吾心，由吾所为则验。汝速沽烧酒一斤，白纸一束来，付陈客行法。」陈客曰：「曷披我发。」戟手持诀，向死者之耳，噀酒令湿，以一纸糊之，喃喃诵咒画符。又噀酒，又盖纸，如是者数十重，酒完纸尽而止，曰：「辫我发，使多人助我拔刀出。」则扶死者出门，喝之走，其人狂奔回家，妻子问之，不答，僵卧于其床。

    Explanation

    29

    There were two guests named Feng and Chen, who transported rice to my hometown, deposited it with a grain merchant to sell, and stayed at his home. The two went out together to get their hair cut and sat in the shop. In my hometown, hairdressers are called "waiting for orders." There was a young hairdresser, known as Longyang Jun, who was using a small knife to trim someone's ears. Suddenly, a ruffian reached out and poked the young hairdresser's buttocks unexpectedly. The hairdresser was startled and dropped his knife, and the tip of the knife went straight into the guest's brain. The guest fell to the ground and lay there. Everyone in the shop was shocked and at a loss. The shop owner grabbed the ruffian and tied him up, intending to report to the authorities.

    Feng said to Chen, "We cannot stand by and do nothing when someone is dying. How can we use our skills to save him?" Chen replied, "Yes."

    The shop owner heard this and wanted to kneel and beg. Feng quickly stopped him and said, "If you do that, we won't be able to save him. If you trust me and let me do what I think is right, it will work. Go quickly and buy one pound of burning wine and a bundle of white paper, and give them to Chen to perform the ritual."

    Chen said, "Why don't you cover my hair?" Holding a sword, he muttered incantations, spraying wine on the dead man's ear and then covering it with a piece of paper. He muttered incantations and drew talismans. He sprayed wine and covered the ear with paper repeatedly, doing this dozens of times. He stopped when the wine was gone and the paper was all used up. "Braid my hair, and have many people help me pull the knife out." Then they carried the dead man out of the shop and shouted at him to run. The man ran wildly back home. His wife and children asked him, but he didn't answer and lay stiffly on his bed.

    30

    家人莫知其故，环守之，经夜而醒，曰：「我忆昨日为小待诏以刀刺耳，疼极而昏，何今日无恙，其梦耶？则发已剃矣。」正转辗自疑问，肆主偕棍徒来问候，始知其故，曰：「我受米客再生恩，当有以报之。」棍徒曰：「是我之过，客脱我罪，已备盛礼来，邀君往谢耳。」其人欣然偕至行家，主人见以礼物来，知谢救生之事者，急阻之曰：「不可，我知客必不受谢。尚高卧后楼，勿扰之。」众皆曰：「岂有受恩不谢哉？客纵不受，亦明我等心耳。且问此后伤复发否？」主人不得已，领入楼下，唤二客，冯客启楼窗见之，摇手曰：「切不可谢，谢则恩将仇报矣。」棍徒与受伤人感极不觉跪地，闻临河后窗开，似有人跃入河中声，冯客顿足曰：「尔等逼死陈君矣。」随下楼同往后河，问众舟子，见一客跳河，打捞无获。冯客亦不甚追究，为脱货易银携装而去。

    Explanation

    30

    The family did not know the reason, and they surrounded and guarded the person, who woke up after a night and said, "I remember yesterday when I was a minor official and was stabbed in the ear with a knife; the pain was so intense that I fainted. Why am I not hurt today? Is it a dream? But my hair has already been shaved off." Just as he was turning and questioning himself, the owner of the shop and the ruffians came to inquire. Only then did he know the reason and said, "I received the life-saving grace of Mr. Rice and should have a way to repay him." The ruffians said, "It was my fault. The guest absolved me of my fault and has already prepared a grand gift to come, inviting you to come and thank him." The person happily accompanied to the guest's house. The host saw the gift coming and knew it was to thank for saving his life. He urgently stopped them and said, "No, I know the guest will definitely not accept the thanks. He is still sleeping high up in the back building. Do not disturb him." Everyone said, "How could there be a case where one does not thank after receiving a favor? Even if the guest does not accept, it also shows our intentions. And asked whether the injury would recur?" The host reluctantly led them downstairs and called the two guests. Mr. Feng opened the window of the upper building and saw them, shaking his hand and said, "Absolutely do not thank. Thanking would turn the favor into resentment." The ruffians and the injured person, feeling deeply moved, unconsciously knelt down. Hearing the back window by the river open, it sounded like someone jumping into the river. Mr. Feng stamped his foot and said, "You all forced Mr. Chen to die." He followed downstairs and went to the back river, asking the boatmen, who saw one guest jump into the river, but no one could find him. Mr. Feng did not pursue it too much, and to unload goods, exchange silver, and leave with their luggage.

    31

    芗厈曰：客之术神矣，不受礼物则可，何至避一跪而水遁？可谓玄之又玄，众妙之门。
    　　
    　　李蒙师
    　　吾乡李生应童子试，年至不惑，不得入泮，遂以训蒙为业。乡农延之，岁入修廿余缗。及门者十数顽童，甘厌其烦，然舍此更无别业可为，不得不下气降心以就之，非其本心也。居停十余家，轮流供膳，有余则以施丐。有一老人，日向先生求乞，不以为厌，求必饱而后去。一日，先生病目，肿甚，伏几卧，老人来视，曰：「先生之疾，易为也。我往觅草药，煮而洗之，不日愈矣。」未几，果以药草来，嗅之香甚。如法熬煎洗，果就痊。

    Xiang Tan said: The guest's skills are truly divine; it is understandable that he refuses gifts, but why avoid a simple act of respect (kneeling) by fleeing? This can be described as mysterious and profound, the gateway to all wonders.

    Li Meng, the teacher:

    My fellow townsman Li took the examination for young scholars, but by the time he was forty, he had not entered the school, so he made teaching children his profession. Local farmers hired him, and his annual income was more than twenty strings of cash. About ten or so unruly children came to study under him, and he was willing to endure their trouble, but apart from this, he had no other means of making a living. He had to lower himself and submit to them, which was not his true intention. He stayed with over ten households, who took turns providing meals. If there was any surplus, he would give it to beggars. There was an old man who daily asked the teacher for alms, and the teacher did not get tired of it, and would give enough until the old man was full before leaving. One day, the teacher's eyes became swollen, and he lay down on the table. The old man came to see him and said, "Your illness is easy to treat. I will go find some herbs, boil them, and wash your eyes; you will recover in no time." Soon after, he indeed brought herbs, which smelled very fragrant. He followed the method to boil and wash the eyes, and he indeed recovered.

    32

    遂以制钱二百具肉食谢。老人来，食讫曰：「先生之目，有以异于平日乎？」先生曰：「无以异也，觉清爽而已。」老人曰：「不然。吾以书置案下，先生试隔木视之。」书似在玻璃中，字字朗澈，先生不胜诧异。老人曰：「先生有此目力，何必教读？请日以百文往博场中压宝，探囊而得，不胜于求童蒙耶？然人生福德有限，不得过贪，日得数百文，一家饱暖，无异仙人。若贪多则犯鬼神之忌，必致祸，戒之！戒之！」先生乐甚，不暇细问其由，老人亦大笑去。

    Explanation

    32

    Then, with two hundred standard coins, he prepared a meat meal to show his gratitude. When the old man arrived, after finishing the meal, he asked, "Is there any difference in your vision compared to usual days?" The scholar replied, "There is no difference, only that it feels clearer." The old man said, "That is not the case. I will place a book under the table. Please look at it through the wood." The book seemed to be in a glass, with every character clear and distinct. The scholar was overwhelmed by amazement. The old man said, "With such vision, why would one need to study? You could go to the gambling hall every day with one hundred coins, easily pick out the winning bet, and it would be no different from being an immortal. However, human fortune and virtue are limited; do not be too greedy. If you win hundreds of coins each day, it can keep your family warm and fed, just like an immortal. But if you are greedy, you will offend the gods and spirits, and surely bring disaster. Be warned! Be warned!" The scholar was very happy and did not have time to ask for more details. The old man also laughed loudly and left.

    次日，先生辞馆，日游博场，家人皆丰衣足食，甚自得也。然谨守老人戒，不敢多取，故人亦不觉。当时有好压宝者富室子张姓，万金事业将尽，不胜忿恨，思求师以佐之。访诸乡人，其弟子以先生目力告，张子欣然执贽往拜。先生初不承，张子跪求无已，先生知机已泄，情不能却，曰：「吾术只可日得数百钱耳，何济于君？」张子曰：「先生守法持廉，不敢逾分，我随先生后，任我所为，无碍先生。且我得恢复旧物，将重酬，先生且无须为此矣。」先生心动，携往场中，先生下百文，其人即满注。

    33

    The next day, the master resigned from his teaching position and spent his days in the gambling house. His family was well-provided for and very content. However, he strictly adhered to the old man's warning and did not dare to take too much, so people did not notice. At that time, there was a wealthy son named Zhang who liked to gamble heavily, and his fortune was nearly exhausted. He could not bear the anger and resentment and thought of seeking a teacher to help him. He consulted the villagers, and his disciples told him about the master's keen eyesight. Zhang went happily with gifts to pay respects. The master initially refused, but Zhang knelt and begged persistently. The master knew the secret was out and could not refuse. He said, "My skill can only earn a few hundred coins a day. How can it help you?" Zhang replied, "The master adheres to the law and maintains integrity. He does not dare to go beyond his limits. I will follow the master, and I can do as I please without hindering him. If I can recover my lost wealth, I will reward you generously. The master need not worry about this." The master was moved and took him to the gambling house. The master bet a hundred coins, and the other person immediately placed a full bet.

    34

    不数日，宝场半为张子败业。赌者聚谋曰：「异哉！张子昔来必败，何近日所向无敌？不求其故，我等皆不能为业矣。」访之，得李先生确耗，众曰：「此人不除，何以营生？」遂共谋以五百金贿丐，告之曰：「某村李先生，吾仇也。与汝等五百金，只须挖其双目，为首者不过军流，以此金至配所营运，富可致矣。且在外乐业，何如在乡贫苦？」一壮者诺之，偕数丐伏林中，见先生过，突出与斗，共擒之，抠其目睛。投官，以忿争误伤自首，得减等，拟城旦。先生失目，悔之晚矣。幸张子复己业，闻先生为所累，改过迁善，以千金报先生，得以考终焉。
    　　芗厈曰：仙人何播弄下愚，益之适以损之。使我遇之，当求性命双修之道，则超凡入圣可期矣，何仅以温饱自得哉？或曰：「君所以不得遇仙人，贪故也。」竟无词以对。

    Within a few days, half of the treasure field was ruined by Zhang Zi. The gamblers gathered and discussed, saying, "Strange! Zhang Zi was bound to fail in the past, why is he invincible lately? If we don't find out the reason, we won't be able to continue our business." They learned the definite news about Mr. Li, and the crowd said, "If this person is not dealt with, how can we make a living?" So they conspired to bribe beggars with five hundred gold pieces and told them, "Mr. Li from a certain village is my enemy. I will give you five hundred gold pieces, just need to gouge out his eyes. The leader will not be sentenced to military exile, use this money to operate at the place of exile, and become rich as a result. And enjoy work outside, how is it compared to being poor in the village?" A strong person agreed to it, and together with several beggars hiding in the forest, they saw Mr. Li passing by and suddenly attacked him, gouging out his eyes. They reported to the authorities, claiming it was a mistaken injury due to a quarrel, and received a reduced sentence, being sentenced to city labor. Mr. Li lost his sight, and it was too late to regret. Fortunately, Zhang Zi restored his own business, and upon hearing that Mr. Li was involved, he decided to reform and do good, giving a thousand gold pieces to Mr. Li, and was able to die peacefully.
    Xiang Yan said, "Why does the immortal play with the foolish, to benefit him actually harms him.     唐词林
    　　吾乡唐生业儒，应童子试，年三十不得游庠。其父市侩也，谓生曰：「吾家世以负贩为业，汝欲读书，不得志，今吾老而汝壮，不得赡养乃翁，固无论矣，但汝何以终身？无已，汝叔在京师，闻事业兴隆，曷往依之？亦可博升斗以养家，胜于坐食多多矣。」生诺诺，自惭不能博一衿，亦图改业，乃随粮艘北上。其叔在前门外，立南货肆，见生来，甚悦，曰：「我肆中正乏人料理，汝二弟皆在学读书，不能助我。一人能有几许精神，而独掌营运耶？汝其为我司帐。岁得数十金，亦可寄家，不无小补。果勤能也，再益汝俸。」生安之。但生喜读书，虽在肆，手不释卷，兴至则拍案朗诵，肆伙及买物者见之，皆大笑。叔愠甚，屡诤不改，谓生曰：「汝既愿读书，我送汝入学，伴两弟读亦可。」生益喜，随送入垫。其师，都中廪膳生也，年逾半百，岸然道貌，收生为徒，曰：「汝齿已长矣，能学文乎？」生曰：「固所愿也，不敢请耳。

    Tang, the Scholar from My Village

    My fellow villager, Tang, studies the Confucian classics. He took the examination for young scholars but, at thirty years old, had not yet entered the school. His father was a petty trader. He told Tang: "Our family has always made a living by trading goods. You want to study, but you have not succeeded. Now I am old, and you are strong. You cannot support your father, so let alone. But how will you support yourself? Why not go and rely on your uncle in the capital? You can earn several dozen taels of silver annually to support your family, which is better than living off others."

    Tang agreed. He felt ashamed that he could not even secure a degree, so he decided to change his career. He followed a grain ship north to the capital. His uncle was in front of the city gate, running a shop selling southern goods. When he saw Tang, he was very pleased and said: "My shop is short of someone to manage it. Your two brothers are both studying in school and cannot help me. One person can only do so much, and I am managing the business alone. You can manage the accounts for me. You will earn several dozen taels of silver annually, which you can send home. It will be a small but useful contribution. If you work hard, I will increase your salary." Tang accepted the job. However, Tang loved reading and, even while working in the shop, he never put down a book. When he was in the mood, he would bang the table and recite aloud. The shop assistants and customers who saw him would all laugh. His uncle was very angry and repeatedly tried to stop him but failed. He told Tang: "If you really want to study, I will send you to school. You can study with your two brothers." Tang was even happier and followed his uncle to school. The teacher was a student who received a stipend from the state, over fifty years old, with a dignified and upright appearance. He took Tang as a student and asked: "You are already grown up. Can you study literature?" Tang replied: "It is what I have always desired. I did not dare to ask."

    36

    」乃命题试之，文成，师阅之，击节赞叹曰：「汝在南方，造诣如是，不能入泮，屈死真才矣。」生见师所改两弟文，甚平庸，心轻之。每遇课期，潜往观剧，晚归，一挥而就，师又善其词也。两弟密告父，含怒至塾，训生曰：「汝在肆，则以读书至高；在学，又嬉戏无度，何怪一事无成，真废物也。」师闻之曰：「乃侄平日勤学，虽课期出外，亦不误作文，其聪明才力，胜乃郎百倍，若以应试，高发可期。」叔曰：「试期在迩，果如先生言，得游庠序，亦可光以门闾，恐未必耳。」师曰：「无他法传，生惟小试场中，断不可自作佳文，当尽心为两弟成之，以余力毕乃事，附名榜尾足矣。盖两弟寄迹久，高标无碍。汝初冒北籍，名列前茅，恐招人忌耳。汝切志之。」生诺。县府两试，谨如师命，助两弟在前十名，自附而已。是年以案首入学，又带一弟，名列第二。从此连捷，中式，登进士，入词垣矣。迎养乃翁，重酬其师，且貤封叔父，所以报本也。

    The teacher then set a topic for the exam. After the essay was completed, the teacher read it and clapped hands in appreciation, saying, "You have achieved so much in the south, yet you were unable to enter the academy, truly a pity for a true talent." Whenever it was time for lessons, he would secretly go to watch plays, returning late at night and quickly finishing his own essay, which the teacher praised highly. From then on, he continued to succeed, passed the exam, became a Jinshi, and entered the Hanlin Academy. He welcomed and supported his father, generously rewarded his teacher, and posthumously bestowed a title on his uncle, all to repay his original source of blessings.

    　　南宋高宗遗事
    　　康王构自金营遁归，创业后，为汪黄所误，复为金人大破，王易服南奔。自泥马渡江后，到处有土神保护。道经盐官州，追兵将及，乱窜至蛇墩。王见田间二人并耕，呼救，农夫视王貌异常，知为贵人，迎谒马前，请王下马释服，与其弟相易。农弟服王衣，骑马南驰，使王以泥污而戴笠荷蓑，立田沟中，执耜工作，农夫候于道左。追兵至，问农夫，告以状貌，曰：「见如此人否？」农夫曰：「适有骑黄马官人，南去不远。」追兵驰及，执之，非王也，怒戮之。时王已去蓑笠裋褐，从别道逸。金兵回斩农夫，四路追寻。
