    Xiang Yan said: Tang Jun, when in the south, is hard to understand; when in the north, he rises rapidly, achieving high status, as if standing among the clouds. Is it truly that northerners are inferior to southerners? Answer: No, it is fate that determines this.

    Southern Song High Emperor's Legacy
    Kang Wang, after escaping from the Jin camp and returning, founded the dynasty but was misled by Wang and Huang, and was then defeated by the Jin, forcing him to flee south in disguise. After the legendary event of the mud horse crossing the river, he was protected by local deities everywhere. Passing through Yanguan State, the pursuing soldiers were about to catch up, and he fled in confusion to She Dun. Seeing two farmers working in the fields, he called for help. The farmer, noticing Kang Wang's unusual appearance, recognized him as a noble person, welcomed him, and asked him to dismount and change clothes with his brother. The farmer's brother wore Kang Wang's clothes and rode south, while Kang Wang was disguised as a farmer, covered in mud, wearing a straw hat and carrying a straw cloak, working in the field. The farmer waited on the side of the road. When the pursuing soldiers arrived, they questioned the farmer about Kang Wang's appearance. The farmer replied, "There was a man on a yellow horse who rode south not far from here." The soldiers caught the man on the horse, who was not Kang Wang, and killed him in anger. By then, Kang Wang had already left his disguise and escaped through another route. The Jin soldiers returned, killed the farmer, and pursued Kang Wang in four directions.

    38

    王至州城郭北有古庙，见茅篷内一僧席地诵经，王潜入求庇，僧以衲衣盖之，嘱勿动。追兵主将骑白马者，遥见大汉入篷，遂下马执刀往，将搜觅。僧见来将，喝曰：「降人欲杀故主，良心安在？即得封侯，亦留万代骂名。况有总领，气谊不投，将冒汝功而戳汝。宋朝气数未尽，不如依老僧言，退去为善。」来将悟，再拜曰：「予实南人，被金人掳去，降非本意。谨遵师命释王。但不能掩北兵耳目，请就死以明心。」遂自刎。兵见主将死，皆散去。王出，僧请无负来将，因不知姓名，封为白马将军、土地尊神。僧指示王速上临安，尚有一难。

    Explanation

    38

    The king reached the northern part of the city wall and saw an ancient temple. Inside a thatched hut, he saw a monk sitting on the ground reciting scriptures. The king secretly entered to seek shelter, and the monk covered him with his robe and instructed him not to move. The leader of the pursuing army, riding a white horse, saw a tall man enter the hut from afar. He then dismounted and went with a sword, about to search. The monk saw the approaching general and shouted, "A person who has surrendered wants to kill his former lord, where is his conscience? Even if you gain a title, you will leave a name cursed by future generations. Moreover, there is a leader who does not share your values, and he will claim your merit and kill you. The fate of the Song Dynasty is not yet exhausted, it is better to follow the old monk's advice and retreat." The general understood and bowed twice, saying, "I am actually a southerner, captured by the Jurchens, and surrendering was not my intention. I will strictly follow the teacher's command and release the king. But I cannot hide the eyes and ears of the northern soldiers, please let me die to show my sincerity." He then committed suicide. The soldiers saw their general die and all dispersed. The king emerged, and the monk requested that the king not betray the general. Since his name is unknown, he was enshrined as the White Horse General and the Land Deity. The monk instructed the king to quickly go to Lin'an, but there is still one difficulty.

    39

    过此即投张帅，能退金人，仍登九五之尊，作南朝创业主也。王谢去。行至半山。追兵又至，王避入桑林，见树上有女采桑，呼救。女下树，出巨筐，使王跃入，以桑叶盖之。甫定，金将入林，问女子，见裋褐高大之男子否？女曰：「过去已半日矣。」诈来将退。女归家，唤父兄舁筐归，倾之，见少年丈夫，父兄皆詈女无耻。王不暇辩，即望山后奔走，天已暮，不知去路，依树憩息。夜将阑，见一灯望树而来，王惊骇，藏树后，一女携灯跪告曰：「此非吉地，请王随妾灯速行。西去即抵张帅营，可平安矣。

    Explanation

    39

    Once past this point, seek out General Zhang, who can repel the Jin forces and ascend to the throne of the Son of Heaven, becoming the founder of the Southern Dynasty. Wang and Xie departed. They reached the middle of the mountain. The pursuing troops arrived again, and King Wang hid in a mulberry grove. He saw a woman picking mulberries on a tree and called for help. The woman came down from the tree, took out a large basket, made King Wang jump into it, and covered it with mulberry leaves. Just as they had settled, the Jin general entered the forest and asked the woman if she had seen a tall man in rough clothing. The woman said, "He has been gone for half a day already." The deceitful general withdrew. The woman went home and called her father and brothers to carry the basket back. When they opened it, they saw a young man, and her father and brothers all scolded her for being shameless. King Wang had no time to argue and immediately ran towards the back of the mountain. It was already dusk, and he didn't know the way, so he leaned against a tree to rest. As night was drawing to a close, he saw a light approaching the tree. King Wang was startled and hid behind the tree. A woman carrying a lamp knelt and said, "This is not a good place, please follow my light and hurry. If you go west, you will reach General Zhang's camp, and you will be safe."

    40

    」王不暇细问，随灯行甚急，转瞬闻鸣钲呵号之声，王止不敢前。女子跪伏万岁曰：「妾采桑人也，因父母不谅，痛加呵责，无以自明，遂缢。此心不昧，故携灯送王，请乞阴封。」王曰：「寡人登极，当敕封汝为半山神君，永享祭祀。」女叩首谢曰：「前途即张帅营，忠臣也。王速投之，妾不能追随矣。」倏不见，天亦向晨。王先闻僧与神言，放胆闯入军营，被获，送帅营。张帅见王来，欢呼迎拜，遂号召韩岳张刘四帅，合击破金军，定鼎于武林。帝不忘救驾功，封二农夫为蛇墩双土地、崇善明王，征僧为护国大禅师，不至。为女神立庙山巅，至今香火不绝，春间佥朝拜半山娘娘云。

    Explanation

    40

    The king had no time to ask further, and following the light, he walked very quickly. In a moment, he heard the sound of gongs and shouts, and he stopped, not daring to proceed. The woman knelt before him and said, "I am a woman who gathers mulberry leaves. Because my parents did not understand, they harshly scolded me, and I had no way to prove myself, so I hanged myself. My heart is not in darkness, so I carry this light to guide you and ask for posthumous recognition." The king replied, "When I ascend the throne, I will decree you as the Half-Mountain Deity, to forever enjoy offerings." The woman bowed in gratitude and said, "The next place is General Zhang's camp; he is a loyal minister. Hurry and seek refuge with him; I cannot follow you anymore." Suddenly, she disappeared, and the sky was turning to dawn. First, he heard the monk speaking to a deity, and with courage, he boldly entered the military camp, where he was captured and sent to General Zhang's camp. General Zhang, upon seeing the king, greeted him with cheers and bows, and then called upon the four generals Han, Yue, Zhang, and Liu. Together, they defeated the Jin army and established their capital in West Lake. The emperor did not forget the merit of rescuing him and enfeoffed two farmers as the Twin Earth Gods of Snake Mound and the Virtuous and Bright King. He summoned the monk to be the Great National Zen Master, but the monk did not come. A temple was built for the goddess on the mountain peak, and the incense continues to this day. During spring, people gather to worship the Half-Mountain Lady.

    41

    王土地
    　　吾乡王生，邑中正士也。奉君子之九思，遵圣人之四勿，朴诚恭敬，为通邑名师。时年逾花甲，在多塾教读，忽谓门人曰：「我将赴任，告归理家事。」门人知先生向无妄言，计出贡未久，焉得官？然不敢诘，谨问先生之任何所？生曰：「玉环耳。限期紧迫，速为尔父兄言之，即此告别。」门人入告，父兄皆来贺，且请文凭阅视。生匣中郑重出之，实无一纸，空指向居停曰：「限仅十日，是以不敢逗留耳。」居停谓先生思为官，入痰迷矣，即具舟备物送归。至家，欣然为妻子述之，咸疑无此事，乃遍拜戚友，约日话别，戚友皆惑，互相商订，于所约之日，移樽候饯。至日，生早起，具衣冠候门，戚友皆集。

    Explanation

    41

    My hometown, Wang Sheng, is a virtuous man in the town. He follows the nine thoughts of a gentleman and adheres to the four prohibitions of a sage, being simple, sincere, respectful, and a respected teacher in the town. At the age of sixty, he teaches in multiple schools. Suddenly, he told his students, "I am about to take up an official post, so I am returning home to settle family matters." The students knew that Mr. Wang had never spoken falsely, but they wondered how he could have an official post since he had only recently passed the imperial examination. However, they did not dare to question him and asked what his official post was. Wang Sheng said, "It is in Yuhuan. The deadline is tight, so quickly tell your parents, and I will say goodbye now." The students went to inform their parents, who all came to congratulate him and asked to see his official document. Wang Sheng took it out from a box, but it was actually empty. He pointed to his host and said, "I have only ten days left, so I cannot stay longer." His host thought that Mr. Wang had become delirious with fever and wanted to be an official, so he prepared a boat and supplies to send him back home. Upon arriving home, Wang Sheng happily told his wife and children about it, but they all doubted that it was true. He then went to visit his relatives and friends, arranging a farewell date. His relatives and friends were all confused and discussed it among themselves. On the agreed-upon day, they held a farewell banquet to see him off. On that day, Wang Sheng got up early, dressed formally, and waited at the door for his relatives and friends.

    42

    生以家贫子幼，谆嘱照拂，戚友唯唯，家人无不惶恐者。若谓有疾，则精神健旺，实无死法。若谓疯疾，则言行清楚，毫无错谬。至夜，在厅事内大开筵宴，生兴勃然，历叙平生旧情，欢呼畅饮。交三鼓，忽闻远来音乐声，异香满堂。生整衣冠，命子开大门曰：「吏役来迎者至矣。」乃居中坐，问来者几人，似以手接物，向空指点，吩咐开道赴任。转向亲朋一揖告别，作登舆势，倒地不动，已卒矣。举哀盛殓毕，夫人欲验其实，使其子往玉环访之。至则土地庙之道人迎于境曰：「王公子来耶？」问何以知之，曰：「某日阖境梦王公莅任，且告道人以公子至期。」随入庙泣拜，居民闻之，来观者百千人。玉环司马恐其惑众，资送公子回籍。
    　　芗厈曰：王公聪明正直，宜其为神，然子孙无达者何也？或曰：「近代如岳武穆、于忠肃，皆赫赫神灵，后裔尚无显达，想必祖宗发泄过甚耳。」余曰：「否。天之报施正人也，香火万年，胜于子孙千亿。」

    Explanation

    42

    Due to his poverty and young children, he repeatedly instructed others to take care of him. Close friends and relatives nodded in assent, and all family members were terrified. If one said he was sick, his spirits were robust, and there was no way he could die. If one said he was mad, his speech and actions were clear, with no mistakes. At night, a grand feast was held in the hall, and he was full of energy, recounting past experiences and cheering and drinking heartily. Around the third drumbeat, they suddenly heard distant music and a strange fragrance filled the hall. He arranged his clothes and hat, ordered his son to open the main gate, and said, "The officials and servants who come to welcome me have arrived." He then sat in the center, asked how many had come, seemed to be receiving something in his hand, and pointed into the air, instructing them to clear the way for him to take office. He turned to friends and relatives, bowed in farewell, made a gesture of getting into a carriage, fell to the ground motionless, and had already died. Mourning and preparing the body for burial were completed. His wife wanted to verify the truth, so she sent her son to Yu Ring to inquire about it. When he arrived, the Taoist priest at the Land Temple greeted him at the boundary and asked, "Has Prince Wang's son come?" He asked how he knew, and the priest replied, "On a certain day, the entire area dreamed that Prince Wang had taken office and told the Taoist priest the time when the prince would arrive." They followed him into the temple, cried, and bowed. The residents heard about it, and thousands of people came to see. The Governor of Yu Ring feared that it would confuse the people and provided funds to send the prince back home.

    Xiang Yan said: Prince Wang was intelligent and upright, so it was fitting for him to become a god. However, why did none of his descendants achieve prominence? Someone said: "In recent times, figures like Yue Fei and Yu Song, who are renowned as divine beings, still did not have prominent descendants. Perhaps the ancestors' blessings were too great." I replied: "No. The heavens reward the virtuous with eternal incense and offerings, which is better than having a thousand generations of descendants."

    43

    许湛然
    　　湛然名澄清，直隶唐山县人。幼失怙，嗣其姑为子。姑后有子皆成立，分与湛然薄地十余亩，使携妻自食。湛然力农，朴诚立志，凡与交者，成人之善，格人之非，尤好排难解纷，故邑人莫不倾心焉。中年家业成就，纳粟得从九品，不愿登仕版，虽不甚读书，而精求歧黄之术，为人医治，立痊，不索谢，曰：「此圣贤遗留济世之道，岂可利己乎？」是以求之者益众，亦无稍厌倦。一日，自乡间治病归，过城外之留养局，局隆冬有人栖止，至春则人散，僻静所也。见局前有少妇，坐地而泣，湛然问故，妇曰：「我相乡某村人，不堪姑虐，出外暂避，不觉行远至此。天将暮矣，既无宿处，又无饮食，是以悲也。」湛然曰：「汝在此，不可动，我将归取饭食汝。」遂去至家，携胡饼来，已不见妇，觅之，闻局内有嚷嚷哭泣声。入见两男子，一老媪，劝妇随伊去，妇号泣不从。

    Explanation

    43

    Xu Zhanran

    Zhanran's name was Chengqing, from Tangshan County, Zhili Province. He lost his father at a young age and was adopted by his aunt as a son. After his aunt had other children who grew up and became independent, she gave him a small plot of land, about ten acres, to support himself and his wife. Zhanran worked hard in farming, simple and sincere in his aspirations. He helped others do good and correct their wrongdoings, and he especially enjoyed resolving disputes and removing difficulties. Therefore, everyone in the county won his heart. Later, he established a successful family business and purchased a minor official position by donating grain, but he did not wish to pursue a career in officialdom. Although he did not read much, he diligently studied traditional Chinese medicine and cured people instantly, without accepting payment. He said, "This is the legacy of sages and saints to benefit the world, how could I do it for my own gain?" As a result, those who sought his help became even more numerous, and he showed no signs of fatigue. One day, while returning from treating someone in the countryside, he passed by a shelter outside the city. The shelter was quiet and secluded, and during the severe winter, people would stay there until spring, when they would disperse. He saw a young woman sitting on the ground and crying. Zhanran asked her why she was crying, and she replied, "I am from a village in the countryside. I could not bear my aunt's abuse and fled temporarily, but I did not realize how far I had gone. The day is coming to an end, and I have no place to stay overnight, nor any food or drink. That is why I am sad." Zhanran said, "You stay here, do not move. I will go home and fetch some food for you." He then went home, brought some flatbread, and returned. However, the woman was no longer there. When he looked for her, he heard loud cries and weeping inside the shelter. Upon entering, he saw two men and an elderly woman, who were trying to persuade the woman to go with them. The woman cried out and refused to go.

    44

    湛然知为匪人，叱曰：「我在此，鼠辈敢尔！」皆张皇遁去。乃唤妇出，使之食讫，曰：「我送汝暂寄尼庵可乎？」妇允诺，遂送交大士庵，老尼收之。湛然于路，已问悉妇人居址，距唐邑三十余里。次日往寻其家，路遇二人，访收留少妇者。湛然问明妇之年貌服色相符，询知二人为妇之夫叔及兄，偕二人归，至尼庵，劝妇回家。妇惧不敢归，湛然曰：「我送汝去，能劝汝姑不加责，而生欢喜心，可乎？」妇曰：「诚如是，一家聚顺，有何不愿？」遂行。湛然先驱，至妇家，则妇之父母翁姑方勃溪，湛然进而排解之曰：「汝等能相安也，还汝妇。否则终必为人掠卖，奈何？」姑曰：「我方悔督责过严，致有此失。使妇无恙而归，有不相安者乎？」湛然始告之故，少妇偕二人亦至。众皆感谢。湛然后他出，过其门，妇之翁姑及夫邀遮入室，见其一庭和睦，妇已生儿，佥再拜感激不已。

    Explanation

    44

    Zhan Ran recognized that they were not good people and shouted, "I am here. How dare you, you scoundrels!" They panicked and fled. He then called the woman out, fed her, and said, "I will take you to stay temporarily in a nunnery. Will that be acceptable?" The woman agreed, and he escorted her to Dashi An, where the old nun took her in. On the way, Zhan Ran had already inquired about the woman's residence, which was over thirty miles from Tang City. The next day, he went to her home, where he encountered two men who had taken in the younger woman. Zhan Ran verified that the woman's age, appearance, and attire matched, and learned that the two men were her husband's uncle and brother. He accompanied them back to the nunnery and persuaded the woman to return home. The woman was afraid to go back, and Zhan Ran said, "I will take you there. If I can persuade your mother-in-law not to blame you and to be happy about it, will that be acceptable?" The woman replied, "If that is truly the case, and the family reunites harmoniously, what reason would I have to refuse?" So they set off. Zhan Ran led the way, and when they arrived at the woman's home, her parents-in-law were in the midst of an argument. Zhan Ran stepped forward to mediate and said, "If you can all get along, return your daughter-in-law to you. Otherwise, she will eventually be abducted and sold. What then?" The mother-in-law said, "I am already regretting that I was too harsh in my reprimands, which led to this situation. If she returns unharmed, how could there be any disharmony?" Only then did Zhan Ran reveal the reason, and the younger woman, accompanied by the two men, also arrived. Everyone expressed their gratitude. Afterward, Zhan Ran went on his way, passing by the door, where the woman's parents-in-law and husband invited him into the room. They saw the entire household living in harmony, and the woman had already given birth to a child. All of them bowed repeatedly, filled with gratitude and emotion.

    45

    又一日，湛然自外来，见坟林内隐隐一男子就树自缢，抚之犹温，急解释之，蹶而苏。年约弱冠，衣虽槛楼，貌殊清俊，不似乞丐中人。问其故，泣告曰：「小人任县某村人，父母伯叔只小人一子。在学读书，被匪徒诱使博，大败，不敢归。无资以应，匪徒尽留小人衣物，尚不足抵，易与破烂衣裤，使推小车送客，觅钱偿债。今送至唐邑而回，思之不胜愤苦，故求死耳。」湛然慰留至家，易其衣服，饮食而教诲之。往访其诸父，因失儿数日，正惶急，湛然告之，同往见少年，皆大悦，如获奇珍。湛然以劝儿改悔之言向述，皆感激涕零，再拜而去。少年归，果绝游戏之事，奋勉为学，次年入泮。

    Explanation

    45

    On another day, Zhan Ran came from outside and saw a faintly visible man hanging himself from a tree in the burial ground. Touching him, he found him still warm, and quickly untied him. The man stumbled and revived. He was about twenty years old, his clothes tattered, but his appearance was exceptionally handsome, unlike that of a beggar. When asked about the cause, he wept and said, "I am from a certain village in Ren County. My parents and uncles have only me as a son. I was studying at school when bandits lured me to gamble. I suffered a great loss and was too ashamed to return home. Lacking the means to pay, the bandits took all my clothes, which still wasn't enough to cover the debt. They exchanged them for ragged clothes and made me push a cart for guests to earn money to pay off my debts. Now I am returning after delivering to Tang City. Thinking about it, I feel overwhelming anger and sorrow, so I sought to die." Zhan Ran comforted and brought him home, changed his clothes, fed him, and taught him. He visited the man's uncles, who were worried because their son had been missing for several days. Zhan Ran informed them, and they went together to see the young man. They were all very happy, as if they had found a rare treasure. Zhan Ran recounted his words of encouragement and repentance, and they were all deeply moved and wept, bowing twice and leaving. The young man returned home and truly stopped playing, strived to study hard, and the following year, he entered the academy.

    46

    自此湛然名益噪，不仅扶危济困而已。邑中修庙宇，建书院，劝赈济，立义冢，诸大事，凡所首倡，无不立成。人信其诚故也。
    　　芗厈曰：湛然以大有为之才，尽力向善，光明磊落，可对天人，实今世所罕见。恒与余言，自恨未曾饱学。余笑慰之曰：「仲尼祖述尧舜，尧舜曾读何书，不过认真十六字耳。彼子衿中，或迂腐固执，或诪张为幻。穷则为闾里之毒蛇，达则为朝廷之大蠹。夫如是，何必读书？」

    Explanation

    46

    From this point on, Zhan Ran's fame grew even louder, not only for his efforts in helping those in danger and distress but also for his broader contributions. In the county, he repaired temples, built academies, encouraged relief efforts, and established public cemeteries. All major projects, whenever he initiated them, were accomplished without fail. This was because people trusted his sincerity.

    Xiang Tan said: Zhan Ran, with his great talent for action, dedicated himself to doing good, was open and upright, and could face heaven and people. Such qualities are truly rare in the current age. He often spoke with me, lamenting that he had not been thoroughly educated. I comforted him with a smile, saying, "Confucius followed the example of Yao and Shun, but did Yao and Shun read any books? They simply adhered to the sixteen words of the Great Learning. Among scholars, some are rigid and stubborn, others are deceptive and deceitful. When poor, they become poisonous snakes in the neighborhood; when successful, they become great pests in the court. If that is the case, why read books?"

    王理堂
    　　理堂名敷正，河南光山县人，随其叔，之任丹徒。值英夷犯顺，崇明危急，中丞檄属员之能解围者。其叔招募乡勇，将以应命，使理堂择得千余人，告之曰：「是行也，有死之心，无生之路，方能奋发有为。汝曹归与父兄谋，不愿者退，无相强也。」翌日，皆来复命曰：「父兄有训，我等所以应募者，急父母之急，非仅崇明也。官能视我等如子，焉有子而敢背亲命者乎？」皆愿死鬬，复查其孤子及兄弟同役者，退一人，得敢死之士八百。欢呼听令，遂给粮饷器械而操演之，与其叔航海而前。时军门所发之救兵千人亦到，见乡勇皆踊跃争先，兵气亦作，二十艘乘风破浪前进。英夷望见，佥掉舟向来船发炮。

    Explanation

    Wang Lizhong
    Wang Lizhong, whose courtesy name was Fuzheng, was from Guangshan County, Henan Province. He followed his uncle to take up a post in Dantu. During the time when the British violated the proper order and Chongming Island was in a critical situation, the provincial governor issued an order to subordinates who could relieve the siege. His uncle recruited local militia to respond to the order. Wang Lizhong selected more than a thousand people and told them: "This journey requires a heart set on death and no way to survive; only then can we be vigorous and achieve great things. You all should go back and consult your parents and brothers. Those who do not wish to go should withdraw; do not force them." The next day, all came to report back and said: "Our parents and brothers have given instructions. The reason we signed up is to help our parents in their time of need, not just for Chongming. The official treats us like his children. How can a child dare to disobey his parents' orders?" All were willing to fight to the death. After rechecking those who were orphans or had brothers serving in the same role, one person was withdrawn, and eight hundred brave soldiers were obtained. They cheered and followed orders. Then, they were provided with food, pay, and weapons and trained. Wang Lizhong sailed with his uncle. At that time, a thousand rescue troops dispatched from the military headquarters also arrived. They saw that the local militia were eager and took the lead, and the morale of the troops also rose. Twenty ships sailed against the wind and waves, advancing. The British saw them and turned their ships toward the incoming ships, firing cannons.

    48

    夫夷舟高大，较我舟超越数倍，是炮皆上飞，烟焰迷空，不睹我舟，夷人意谓已击沈矣，殊不知理堂奋勇当先，炮子落身边，烧其衣襟不顾，冒烟直入，竟抵夷人之火轮船。其将白鬼子所主，理堂以大挠钩，钩其船舷，持刀跃登，乡勇官兵相继，顷刻满船相杀。夷自犯顺以来，从未见勇敢如此者，皆战栗而伏。遂生擒夷将，戮尽丑虏。余舟皆遁，遂报崇明之捷。中丞受俘保奏，给理堂赏戴六品衔。中丞赴浙，援救台州之急，短给口粮，乡勇鼓噪。

    Explanation

    48

    The foreign ships are tall and large, several times larger than our own. All their guns shoot upwards, and the smoke and flames fill the sky, obscuring our view of our own ships. The foreigners thought we had already been sunk, unaware that Li Tang bravely led the charge. The cannonball landed near him, burning his clothes, but he paid no heed and rushed in through the smoke, finally reaching the foreign steamship. The commander of the ship was a white foreigner. Li Tang used a large grappling hook to hook the ship's side and leaped onto the ship with a knife. The local militia and soldiers followed, and in an instant, they were fighting on the entire ship. Since the foreigners invaded, we have never seen such bravery, and they all trembled and surrendered. They captured the foreign commander alive and killed all the remaining enemies. The remaining ships fled, and they reported the victory at Chongming. The governor-general received the captives and recommended Li Tang, awarding him a sixth-rank official title. The governor-general went to Zhejiang to rescue Taizhou in its emergency, but short rations for the local militia led to unrest.

    49

    理堂蠲八百，以安士心，然知其必无功也，虑为所累。适奉母命归省，遂呈其家书，以母老告退，就例报捐九品，分发来燕。方伯知其能，癸卯冬，使往赵州缉捕，驻大桥之元帝庙。理堂不惜辛勤，每夜必出，逡巡各村庄，往往黎明而返，风雪寒冷皆不顾。于是数里无警，几至夜不闭户，民已深感之。时大桥之南村将起庙会，凡会，娼赌在所不免，且无此不足以聚众，会必消索，故主会之衿耆，虑委员执法，欲贿之，遂以制钱十余贯，因庙祝而通于理堂。

    Explanation

    49

    Li Tang exempted 800 people from taxes or labor to pacify the people's hearts, but he knew that this would be futile and feared being burdened by it. He happened to receive his mother's command to return home to visit her, so he presented his family letter and retired due to his mother's old age, following the precedent to donate and be sent to Yan. The high-ranking official knew of his ability and, in the winter of the year of Gui Mao, sent him to Zhaozhou to apprehend criminals, stationing him at the Yuan Emperor Temple. Li Tang spared no effort, and every night he would go out, pacing around the various villages, often returning at dawn, all the while ignoring the wind, snow, and cold. As a result, there were no disturbances for several miles, and the people almost reached a state where they did not close their doors at night, deeply appreciating his efforts. At that time, the village south of the bridge was about to hold a temple fair. Any gathering, prostitution and gambling could not be avoided, and without these, people would not gather, and the gathering would inevitably decline. Therefore, the leaders of the gathering, fearing that the commissioner would enforce the law, wanted to bribe him, so they gave him several dozen strings of cash coins through the temple priest, conveying the message to Li Tang.

    50

    僧为婉达其情，理堂即延衿耆入坐而问曰：「公等恐我执娼赌，此有地方官在，非吾分内事也，我何干预？但娼赌之场混留盗贼，而盗贼之迹难瞒土著，公等能为我寻之，胜于纳贿多多矣。」坚辞不受，衿耆曰：「官顾清廉，仆宜酬志。请以予从者。」理堂曰：「此纳贿方便法门也，我岂为之？公等既悯我仆劳，我宜酬之。」随以衣命僧立质钱三贯，呼仆而给之曰：「此诸公之赐，嗣后不许名一钱也。」衿耆皆感激称叹而退。

    Explanation

    50

    The monk gently conveyed the situation, and the magistrate immediately invited the elders to sit and asked, "You all are afraid that I will enforce laws against prostitution and gambling. There are local officials for this; it is not within my jurisdiction. Why should I interfere? However, the places of prostitution and gambling harbor thieves, and the traces of thieves are hard to hide from the locals. If you can find them for me, it is much better than bribing." The elders firmly refused, saying, "The magistrate is known for his integrity; I should fulfill my intentions. Please give me one of my followers." The magistrate replied, "This is a convenient way to bribe; how could I do that? You all have shown compassion for my servant's labor; I should reward him." He then had the monk pledge his clothes as collateral for three strings of cash and called his servant, giving him the money and saying, "This is the gift from all of you. From now on, I will not allow him to mention a single coin." The elders were all moved, praised, and then left.

    51

    Explanation

    51

    At that time, the magistrate was present at the meeting day and night, patrolling without causing disturbance. The people captured bandits and presented them, so by the end of the meeting, there were no mishaps. The merchants and civilians were grateful, and the magistrate hung a plaque on the temple door. At that moment, the Zhaozhou garrison should have received military pay, but by custom, a civilian official leads while a military officer distributes. The prefect had received the pay but was delayed due to some matter, and it was still not distributed after a month. The entire army became very agitated, planning to besiege the prefecture and seize the prefect. Rumors spread, and the prefect was greatly afraid. Knowing the magistrate was capable, he went to the magistrate's office to consult. The magistrate said, "Under the bright sun, how dare one rebel? This is just empty threats. But since the time has passed, it should be given quickly, and the army will be at ease." The prefect replied, "If given out of fear, what about the future consequences?" The magistrate said, "There is no difficulty; let the main general be punished before giving the pay."

    The governor said, "Is it possible to be like this? How dare I inscribe it?" Li Tang replied, "I have heard that your subordinates wish to seize the military rations. Is this true?" The head official said, "This is the talk of commoners and is not worth mentioning. However, winter rations are usually distributed at the beginning of the previous season, but now they have not been issued for over a month. Has the governor not been appropriating them? Nowadays, there is a theory of deducting one tael per level, which began this winter. The rations issued by the censorate are uncertain whether to be deducted or not, as there is still no clear written order. Therefore, the governor has requested permission before issuing them, and as of yet, no reply has been received, hence the delay."

The commander said, "If you can do this, I will accompany you." They went to the prefecture office with a sense of guilt, and the civil and military officials reconciled as before, immediately distributed the pay, and the entire army was delighted, saying, "We are not saved by Commissioner Public's grace, our parents, wives, and children, all would freeze and starve, not only are we saved from punishment. In the second month of the year Jia Chen, the councilor completed his affairs and was called back to the province. The gentry, soldiers, and civilians of the state of Hezhou, farewelled him on the roadside, with a red canopy led by the people, and today, the two plaques are still hanging at the gate of the Emperor Yuan Temple, and everyone looks up to them.
