    第二卷

    　　权阎罗王
    　　吾乡有延陵生者，甫入泮，夜卧书斋，梦役持红柬来请曰：「有公事，宜速行。」生意谓学师召之耳，未阅其柬，即易衣冠而出，见乘舆候之，生曰：「近在咫尺，何用舆为？」遂登舆急行，见黄沙茫茫，天色似明似暗，所由之路，向所未经。旋入一大城，三街六市，往来者咸避道。至一大署，体统比督抚犹壮。舆入中门，鼓乐鸣炮。至甬道，有红袍纱帽者十六员，迎舆而揖，生欲下，役已当舆唱免，生意学师演剧，使优迎之耳。舆至殿陛始停，出舆见大殿九楹，甚宏敞，殿中以白石筑台，台上金龙黄幕下垂。由左入内，两旁回廊甚深邃，直接后殿。入殿之左室，帘帏之内，陈设精雅，役引至此，请生入坐而退。

    Explanation

    54

    芗厈曰：「古今来颂委员之德，而争悬匾额，实罕闻见。盖微员末职，不过借上游之力，博数金而已。理堂展其才力，竟能如是，非知仁勇三者兼全不能。」

    Xiang Yan said: "Throughout history, it has been rare to hear of people praising the virtue of the commissioner and competing to hang plaques in his honor. This is because minor officials with low-ranking positions typically rely on the power of higher authorities to gain a few coins. However, the commissioner displayed his talents and could actually do so, which is something that cannot be achieved without possessing all three virtues of knowledge, benevolence, and courage."

    第二卷

    权阎罗王

    吾乡有延陵生者，甫入泮，夜卧书斋，梦役持红柬来请曰：「有公事，宜速行。」生意谓学师召之耳，未阅其柬，即易衣冠而出，见乘舆候之，生曰：「近在咫尺，何用舆为？」遂登舆急行，见黄沙茫茫，天色似明似暗，所由之路，向所未经。旋入一大城，三街六市，往来者咸避道。至一大署，体统比督抚犹壮。舆入中门，鼓乐鸣炮。至甬道，有红袍纱帽者十六员，迎舆而揖，生欲下，役已当舆唱免，生意学师演剧，使优迎之耳。舆至殿陛始停，出舆见大殿九楹，甚宏敞，殿中以白石筑台，台上金龙黄幕下垂。由左入内，两旁回廊甚深邃，直接后殿。入殿之左室，帘帏之内，陈设精雅，役引至此，请生入坐而退。

    In the second volume:

    The Power of the Lord Yama

    In my hometown, there was a man named Yanling who had just entered the imperial academy. One night, while lying in his study, he dreamed that a servant came to summon him with a red invitation, saying, "There is official business; you should hurry." Yanling thought it was his teacher calling him, so without reading the invitation, he immediately changed into his formal attire and went out. He saw a carriage waiting for him, and said, "It's just a short distance away; why do I need a carriage?" So he climbed into the carriage and hurried along. He saw a vast expanse of yellow sand, with the sky appearing both bright and dim. The road he was taking was one he had never been on before. Soon, he entered a large city with three streets and six markets, and all the people passing by avoided the path. He arrived at a grand hall, whose authority was even more imposing than that of a governor or a provincial inspector. The carriage entered the central gate, where drums were beaten, music played, and firecrackers were set off. Upon reaching the corridor, sixteen officials in red robes and silk hats came forward to greet the carriage with bows. Yanling wanted to get off, but the servant had already stepped forward to announce that he could remain seated. Yanling thought his teacher was staging a play and had actors come to welcome him. The carriage stopped at the steps of the hall, and Yanling stepped out to see a grand hall with nine bays, very spacious. In the center of the hall, a white stone platform was built, with a golden dragon hanging from a yellow curtain. To the left, he entered the inner chamber, where the two sides were connected by a deep and secluded corridor leading directly to the rear hall. Entering the left room of the hall, inside the curtain, the furnishings were elegant and refined. The servant led him there and invited him to sit before leaving.

    55

    有八童子，年约十一二者进，或捧金幞头，或捧黄龙袍，或捧云履，或捧假面，或捧玉带，或镜或巾或炉，无赤手者，请生易服，生曰：「此何为也？」童曰：「此处规矩，应如是耳。」生不得已，易服冠带履，一童请戴假面，生曰：「何必如是？」童亦以规矩对，生思既强作古装，恐为识者所笑，蒙假面亦得，遂戴之。着面如生成者，引镜自照，失其本来面目，方面长髯，俨然王者像矣。八童齐唱升殿，外似有接唱者，不觉随童行至前殿，自中间自石台之后户，历阶而升，内设公案，签筒印箱朱墨砚俱备。黄幕已启，两青衣吏拥生升座，前十六官入殿恭揖，吏唱免参。阶下吏役不知其数，内有夜叉一部，牛头马面一部，佥跪谒，吏唱起，扬声齐诺，旁列甚肃。

    Explanation

    55

    There were eight children, aged around eleven or twelve, who entered. Some carried golden headbands, others yellow dragon robes, cloud shoes, masks, jade belts, mirrors, towels, and incense burners; none were bare-handed. They asked the protagonist to change clothes. The protagonist said, "What is this for?" The children replied, "This is the rule here, it should be like this." The protagonist, unable to refuse, changed his clothes, headband, and shoes. One child asked him to wear a mask. The protagonist said, "Why do I need to do that?" The children replied with the same rule. The protagonist thought that since he had to wear ancient costumes, he was afraid that people who knew better would laugh at him, so wearing a mask was also acceptable. He put on the mask and looked in the mirror. He lost his original appearance, his face becoming square with a long beard, looking like a king. The eight children all sang to ascend the throne, and it seemed there were others singing along outside. Without knowing the exact number, the eight children led the protagonist to the main hall, where a desk was set up with a signet case, seal box, red and black ink, and a writing brush all ready. The yellow curtain had been opened, and two officials in green robes escorted the protagonist to ascend the throne. The sixteen officials entered the hall and bowed respectfully, and the official sang, "Exempt from attendance." The number of officials and servants below the steps was unknown, but there were a group of night spirits and a group of ox-headed and horse-faced demons, all kneeling to pay homage. The official sang, "Rise," and they all responded loudly, and the side stands were very solemn.

    56

    十六官退分两庑，各有公位。吏役送卷，自外带囚就讯，刑罚甚重，有剥脸破腹抽肠拔舌者，哀嚎甚惨。生坐远，不知所审何词，第见一起毕，则卷案送呈，青衣吏接展案上，仅露年月，请生以朱笔某日书行，即持去，不使见狱词也。未几，外报节孝妇到，吏请生下阶迎，官役咸跪。见天际红云下垂，光华灿灿中，有金童玉女擎幡盖，侍一黄瘦中年妇人，将至地，忽一阵香风，吹往西方去矣。吏请生归座，以签票一卷送案上，仅露其姓名，请生过朱判行，皆男犯也。又呈女犯签票亦如前。生点至某氏，心忽动，疑似其姑母，时方有疾。欲再阅，吏即持去。

    Explanation

    56

    The sixteen officials stepped back and divided into two wings, each with their own public seat. Officials and servants brought scrolls and prisoners from outside for questioning. The punishments were very severe, including face peeling, abdominal splitting, intestine pulling, and tongue extraction, with the prisoners' cries being very painful. The narrator sat far away and did not know what words were being examined. He only saw one case completed, and the scroll and case were presented. A servant in green clothing received and unfolded the case on the table, showing only the date, and asked the narrator to write the date with red ink and mark it as completed. The actual content of the case was not shown to the narrator. Soon after, an announcement was made that a virtuous and filial woman had arrived. The officials asked the narrator to go down the steps to welcome her, and all officials and servants knelt. The narrator saw red clouds hanging down from the sky, in the midst of brilliant light, with golden boys and jade girls holding banners and canopies, attending a middle-aged woman who was thin and yellowish. As she approached the ground, a sudden fragrant wind blew her towards the west. The officials asked the narrator to return to his seat and brought a scroll of tickets to the table, showing only the names, and asked the narrator to mark the tickets with red ink. All were male prisoners. Another scroll of tickets for female prisoners was presented in the same manner. The narrator pointed to a certain surname, and his heart suddenly moved, suspecting it might be his aunt, who was ill at that time. He wanted to read more, but the official took the document away.

    57

    唱公事毕，纷纷告退时，生亦下座，仍入内殿，去假面，易故衣，童送登舆，十六官仍在甬道揖送，惟舆前较来时多大灯一对，上首墨书第七殿，下首书阎罗王。直送生至家，释服仍卧，有送信者在床前唤觉，时甫黎明。生问来人曰：「自大门至此五六层，汝由何入？」来人曰：「并未闭门。」生曰：「异哉！此我夜间亲自关闭者，何人开放？」呼家人，皆未起，问来人，知姑母疾重，使速往。生即趋候，姑母已奄奄一息。张目执生手曰：「汝来甚好，床前鬼使皆趋避矣。汝坐此勿离。」生问疾，慰之曰：「偶患时症，即日就痊，勿戚戚也。」姑哂曰：「汝既不欲我死，何点我名？然天命也，我不能责汝忘亲情。」生悚然莫对。未几，报医来，家人请生出迎之，至再至三，姑始释手曰：「噫！止此一刻，竟不延矣。汝去。」生出而其姑遂逝。

    57

    When the official business concluded, the officials began to disperse. The protagonist also stood up from his seat, re-entered the inner palace, removed his ceremonial mask, changed back into his ordinary clothes, and was escorted into a carriage by a servant. Sixteen officials continued to bow and see him off in the corridor, but in front of the carriage, there were two additional large lanterns compared to when he had come. On the left side, it was written in black ink "Seventh Hall," and on the right side, it was written "Yama King." They escorted him directly to his home, where he took off his ceremonial clothes and lay down. A messenger called him awake in front of the bed, and it was just dawn. The protagonist asked the messenger, "From the main gate to here, there are five or six layers—how did you enter?" The messenger replied, "The door was not closed." The protagonist said, "Strange indeed! This was closed by me personally at night—who opened it?" He called for his family, but all were still asleep. Upon questioning the messenger, he learned that his aunt was seriously ill and instructed him to go quickly. The protagonist hurried to attend to her, and she was already on her deathbed. Opening her eyes, she held his hand and said, "It is very good that you came—the ghost messengers in front of the bed all avoided. Sit here and do not leave." The protagonist asked about her illness and comforted her by saying, "It is just a seasonal illness, it will recover soon, do not be worried." His aunt smiled and said, "If you do not want me to die, why did you call my name? But it is the will of heaven, I cannot blame you for forgetting family affection." The protagonist felt shocked and unable to respond. Not long after, the doctor arrived. The family asked the protagonist to go out to meet the doctor, doing so repeatedly. Finally, the aunt released her hand and said, "Ah! Only this moment, it cannot be prolonged. You go." The protagonist left, and his aunt passed away.

    58

    芗厈曰：异哉！夫何以生人署阎王之职，而又不使之主政，则十六官皆可代也，何用生为？且聪明正直之为神，此生与余一人，交未能信，且为正人君子，岂阴曹之鬼，犹不如生耶？不可解矣。或曰：「阳间显官，岂尽正人君子为之，君何泥也？」余笑曰：「诺。」
    　　
    　　补讼师(二则)
    　　有楚生某，娶妻美而艳。邻有寡妇，与外村少年狎，少年过寡妇家，偶见生妇，极为垂涎，以重赀贻寡妇，谋通之。寡妇曰：「彼宴尔新婚，夫妻和睦，且良家妇，不可以势逼，亦不能以利诱，虽其夫毕姻后，出外教读，但有老媪作伴，亦难以游词进，实无法可施也。」少年情不自禁，以重价觅得积贼闷香来，曰：「我已得计，第不能穿穴逾墙。若诱至汝家，事必偕矣。」寡妇曰：「是不难。」使少年入市，市食物之精者，往候生妇，以甘言结好，后此屡往，密甚。生妇知寡妇家无男子，且近邻，以礼往答。寡妇留生妇入卧室，饭之，而遣媪妇守门户。

    Explanation

    58

    Xiang Yan said: "Strange indeed! How would a living person be appointed as the position of King Yama, yet not allowed to govern? All sixteen officials could replace them. What use is there in being alive? Moreover, the wise and upright are considered gods. This person and I have not been able to trust each other. Moreover, we are both upright and virtuous men. Are the ghosts in the underworld any less virtuous than living people? It is incomprehensible." Someone said, "High-ranking officials in the mortal world, are they all upright and virtuous men? Why are you so rigid in your thinking?" I smiled and said, "Yes."

    Supplementary Cases of Litigation Lawyers (Two Cases)

    There was a man named Chu from a certain place. He married a beautiful and alluring wife. There was a widow living next door. She had an intimate relationship with a young man from another village. The young man visited the widow's house and happened to see Chu's wife, who greatly aroused his desire. He gave the widow a large sum of money and plotted to seduce her. He is newly married and his marriage is harmonious. Moreover, she is a good family woman and cannot be forced by power or enticed by money. Even though his husband has gone out to teach after the wedding, and there is only an old woman for company, it is still difficult to approach her with flattery. In fact, there is no way to do it. The young man could not control his feelings and found a large amount of opium from a notorious thief. He said, "I have a plan, but I cannot break through walls or climb over fences. If I can lure her to your house, the matter will surely be successful." This is not difficult. Have the young man go to the market, buy the finest food, and visit Chu's wife, using sweet words to win her favor. After this, he visited frequently, becoming very close. Chu's wife knew that the widow's house had no men and was a close neighbor, so she went to visit her out of courtesy. The widow invited Chu's wife into her bedroom, served her a meal, and sent the old woman to guard the door.

    59

    时少年预伏室中，室焚闷香，妇觉香甚软，伏于座，少年突出，拥妇登床，寡妇避去。妇手足麻木，口不能言，而心甚了了，任其淫狎，饮泣而已。少年思得其欢心，许与衣饰，妇益忿怒，泪如泉涌。少年知难久留，草草讫事而逸。妇醒，索寡妇，不见，破其室中什物而归，郁郁成疾。其父，名讼师也，往问之，女欲求计划，以实情告。父责其不应轻出，然彼以阴谋来，我当以诡计报之。随作一函，纳女枕畔曰：「能从之，则使媪来，我命两兄助之。」父去，妇阅其书，大喜，病寻愈，益自修饰，使媪强寡妇来谢过，与亲昵之，留寡妇宿，密告之曰：「前日之事，曷不先与我谋，是所恨也。

    Explanation

    59

    At that time, a young man was hiding in the room, and the room was filled with a suffocating incense. The woman felt the incense was very soft, and she lay down on the seat. Suddenly, the young man appeared and dragged the woman onto the bed. The widow fled away. The woman's limbs were numb, she could not speak, but her mind was very clear. She allowed him to indulge in his lust, and she could only weep. The young man wanted to please her and promised to give her clothes and ornaments. The woman became even more angry, and tears flowed like a spring. Knowing he could not stay long, the young man hastily finished and fled. After waking up, the woman searched for the widow but did not find her. She destroyed the belongings in the room and returned, becoming depressed and falling ill. Her father, a famous lawyer, went to ask her. The daughter wanted a plan and told him the truth. The father blamed her for not being careful, but since he came with deceit, he advised her to repay him with cunning. He then wrote a letter and placed it beside her pillow, saying, "If you agree, I will send the old woman to come, and I will have my two brothers help her." After the father left, the woman read the letter, was greatly pleased, and soon recovered from her illness. She began to dress and groom herself more carefully. She sent the old woman to force the widow to come and apologize, befriended her closely, and kept her overnight. She secretly told her, "Why didn't you consult me about the matter from the day before? That is what I regret."

    60

    第事巳如此，纵决西江之水，难洗清白。况良人久客不归，晨昏孤宿，乃子实获我心，但面许我衣饰，何食言也？」寡妇知其心动，曰：「是人富而多情，实慕娘子，无路可通，非负所许也，我为导引何如？」妇曰：「须防外人耳目，来必夜深人静，我逐媪候门，方无他虑。」因与订期而去。归告少年，自诩有功，少年大悦，急购鲜衣美珠，使寡妇先致之。如期留寡妇家，漏四下，潜以指叩门，与妇携手入室，即欲乱之，妇曰：「即来此，何急急？请同酌三杯以助兴。」案上酒餐具奋，妇酌酒以进，少年目视而不饮。妇举杯坐怀中，口含以哺，少年迷乱，接而吞之。

    Explanation

    60

    The matter has already reached this state, even if one were to unleash the waters of the West River, it would be difficult to cleanse oneself of guilt. Moreover, my husband has been away for a long time and has not returned, leaving me to live alone both morning and evening. This young man truly understands my heart, but why would he break his promise regarding the clothing and ornaments? The widow knew that the young man was moved, and said, "This man is wealthy and emotionally expressive. He genuinely admires you, but lacks a way to express it. He is not breaking his promise. Should I guide him?" The woman replied, "We must be wary of being seen or heard by outsiders. He will come when it is late at night and quiet. I will wait at the door to avoid other concerns." They agreed on a time and the widow left. Returning, she boasted to the young man about her success. The young man was greatly pleased and immediately purchased fine clothes and beautiful jewels, sending the widow to deliver them first. At the agreed time, he arrived at the widow's house. At midnight, he silently knocked on the door, took the widow's hand, and entered the room, immediately intending to have relations with her. The widow said, "You've come here, why the rush? Let us drink three cups together to enhance the mood." The table was set with wine and utensils. The widow poured the wine and offered it to the young man, who looked at it but did not drink. The widow held the cup to his mouth and fed him the wine. The young man became confused and accepted the wine, drinking it.

    61

    徒见两壮士操刀直入，少年狂奔出户，遇绳绊足而跌，妇以烛来，壮士缚少年手足，割其辫发，妇释缚纵之逸。壮士携辫操刀，轻叩寡妇门，妇误谓少年归来，俏语曰：「夜已深，正好安睡，何又草草回？想必败阵而逃也。」门甫辟，壮士即刺其胸，饮刃而倒，以辫发缚妇右手数匝，归告生妇曰：「大事已毕，可以复父命矣。」此盖妇两兄，预伏房外而安绊绳者，所哺少年之酒，哑药也。少年逃归，哑不能言。次日，亭长见寡妇被杀于门，鸣官，验得凶刀插心，妇手握发辫，系强奸不从，登时杀死者。密访失辫之人，获少年，无言置辩，遂按律斩之。至今楚俗，凡执奸者，必去其辫发云。

    Explanation

    61

    Only seeing two strong men wielding knives and entering directly, the young man rushed wildly out of the door, stumbling over a rope and falling. The woman brought a candle, and the strong men tied the young man's hands and feet, cut off his queue, and the woman released the bindings and let him escape. The strong men carried the queue, wielding knives, and lightly knocked on the door of the widow. The woman mistakenly thought the young man had returned and said sweetly, "It is already late at night, the perfect time to sleep. Why are you rushing back?" The door just opened, and the strong man immediately stabbed her chest, causing her to fall down after being stabbed. He tied her right hand several times around with the queue. Returning to report to the living woman, he said, "The big task is done, we can now fulfill our father's command." It is likely that these were the woman's two brothers, who had previously hidden outside the room and set the rope as a trap. The drink they fed the young man contained a drug that caused muteness. The young man escaped back, becoming mute and unable to speak. The next day, the local official saw the widow killed at the door and reported it to the authorities. The investigation revealed that the knife was found in her heart, and her hand was tied with the queue, indicating a case of rape resisted, which led to her being killed on the spot. The officials secretly investigated the person who lost the queue and caught the young man, who could not speak in defense. He was then executed according to the law. Until today, in the customs of Chu, anyone who catches a criminal must cut off their queue.

    62

    有潘生者，党讼师，与庵之少尼昵甚，有必正妙常之约。一日，潘生入庵，见州署官亲幕友开宴密室，少尼傅坐。潘生怒叱曰：「汝曹皆关防衙署中人，挟尼饮酒，知法犯法。何以佐尔主理民事乎？」众唯唯谢过而退。回署，传各役之首，谕令能获生奸者有赏。不能，必革役。皆领命，日使散役伏庵左右伺之。生恋尼，晨入庵，役拥而入，脱生与尼衣，合缚之，舁出。将鸣官，遇生党怒目拦阻，或许以重贿，纷纷嬲入班馆，不使速报。一生捷入潘生家，告其母妻，速邀亲戚入庵，嘱老尼用残香烛，在大殿开无量寿经，旁供潘生之父神主。安置毕，知会诸生，各易素衣冠，入州廨鸣冤。官升堂问故，诸生以潘生之父百年阴寿，同眷属戚友在尼庵礼忏，州役讹诈不遂，强以奸论，请官往验。役亦以获奸报。官难辨，同往验之，见有妇女及佛前香烛将尽，曰：「此非仓卒所能办者，其为蠧役无疑。」遂杖役而释生尼。

    Explanation

    62

    There was a man named Pan who was a litigator, and he was very close to a young nun at the hermitage, with a promise of mutual fidelity. One day, Pan entered the hermitage and saw a high-ranking official's close associate hosting a banquet in a private room, with the young nun seated formally. Pan angrily shouted, "You all are people in charge of the government office, yet you are holding a nun for drinking, knowing the law and breaking it. How can you assist your master in handling civil affairs?" The others all apologized and left. Upon returning to the office, he summoned the leaders of the various officials, instructing them that those who could catch Pan in an act of immorality would be rewarded. If they failed, they would be dismissed. All received the orders, and each day, they would send scattered officials to lurk around the hermitage, waiting for an opportunity. Pan, infatuated with the nun, entered the hermitage early in the morning. The officials rushed in, stripped Pan and the nun of their clothes, bound them together, and carried them out. As he was about to report to the authorities, he encountered his fellow litigators who blocked him with angry glares and offered him a large bribe, leading him into a classroom, preventing him from reporting quickly. One of the officials quickly went to Pan's home, informed his mother and wife, and urged them to invite relatives to the hermitage. He instructed the old nun to use leftover incense and candles, open the Infinite Life Sutra in the main hall, and place the spirit tablet of Pan's father beside it. After everything was set up, he notified all the officials, who changed into plain clothes and hats, and went to the state office to lodge a complaint. The official ascended the dais to inquire about the matter, and the officials explained that Pan's father's hundred-year memorial service was being held, with family members and friends attending a confession at the hermitage. The officials had tried to extort money but failed, so they falsely accused Pan of immorality and asked the official to investigate. The officials also reported that they had caught Pan in an act of immorality. The official found it difficult to distinguish the truth, so he went to investigate with them. He saw women and the incense and candles before the Buddha statue were almost finished, and said, "This could not have been done in a hurry; it must be corrupt officials." He then flogged the officials and released Pan and the nun.

    63

    粤东狱
    　　粤东某生，娶某氏女，国色也。偶出观剧，被为富不仁者所见，重贿女母，私之，往来甚密。恐旁人执奸，乃于女卧榻下，穿一地道，通后院密室中。倘有恶耗，为潜避计。未几，某生入泮，使媒来订婚期。富室与母女谋，使生入赘而毙之。母女皆诺，告媒曰：「婿家无父母，老妇亦无夫无子，两无依倚。如肯入赘，两得其便，否则姑缓，待我卒也而后于归。」媒覆之生，欣然愿赘，期于清和之吉完姻。时男女亲朋集贺者数十人，同观花烛，无不啧啧羡新妇美者。生喜甚，送客入席，即归新房与妇对酌。时无一女客，生得畅意为欢，新妇不作恒常羞涩，竟执爵相酬饮，生入醉乡。

    Explanation

    63

    Guangdong Prison
    A certain scholar from Guangdong married a woman from a certain family, who was renowned for her exceptional beauty. One day, while he was out watching a play, he was seen by a wealthy but unkind man who offered a large bribe to the woman's mother, and they began an affair, meeting frequently. Fearing that others might discover their infidelity, they dug a secret passage under the woman's bed, leading to a hidden room in the back courtyard. If there was any bad news, it would serve as a place to hide. Soon after, the scholar passed the imperial examination and a matchmaker was sent to arrange the wedding. The wealthy man and the woman's mother plotted to have the scholar marry into their family and then kill him. Both the mother and daughter agreed, and the mother told the matchmaker, "The scholar's family has no parents, and I am also without a husband or children. We both have no one to rely on. If he agrees to marry into our family, it will be convenient for both of us. Otherwise, we will wait until I die before he comes to live with us." The matchmaker returned to the scholar and informed him of the plan. The scholar happily agreed to marry into the family, and the wedding was set for a favorable date in the Qinghe period. At the time, dozens of relatives and friends gathered to congratulate them, and they all admired the beauty of the new bride. The scholar was very pleased, and after sending the guests inside, he returned to the bridal chamber to drink with his new wife. There were no female guests present, and the scholar enjoyed himself fully and happily. The new wife did not act as she usually did, shy and reserved, but instead held a cup and drank with him, and the scholar became drunk.

    64

    时外客闻内宅惨呼一声，共骇愕间，见新郎衣履如故，散发覆面，狂跃而出，群欲询之，已疾奔出外，客皆追行。里许，遇大河，即跃入水而没。客呼渔舟捞救，经日夜不知尸所在，客叹息而返。新妇与母皆惶急，候于堂，见客来，即问新郎所在，客告之故，并叩其由。妇曰：「婿方在房中筵宴，忽发狂冲门出，我辈不知所以，谅出外，亲友必阻之使归，何任其投河而没耶？是客杀我婿也。」遂鸣诸官，官讯客，皆曰：「我等猝不及防，追之无及，事出意外，岂有至亲好友见死不救哉？」讯诸新妇及母，则哀求还尸而已。官至河涘验勘，荡荡大河，流长源远，无从求尸，遂为疑狱。

    Explanation

    64

    At the time, guests outside the house heard a loud, distressing cry from inside the inner quarters. Startled, they saw the groom, whose clothes and shoes were unchanged, with loose hair covering his face, jumping wildly out of the house. The group wanted to ask him what was wrong, but he had already run quickly outside, and the guests followed him. After about a mile, they encountered a large river, and he immediately jumped into the water and disappeared. The guests called for fishing boats to rescue him, but after days and nights of searching, they did not know where the body was. The guests sighed and returned. The bride and her mother were both anxious and waited in the hall. When they saw the guests return, they immediately asked where the groom was. The guests explained what had happened and asked why he had done this. The bride said, "My husband was just having a banquet in the room when he suddenly went mad and rushed out the door. We didn't know what was wrong, but we thought he had gone out, and our friends and relatives would surely stop him and bring him back. Why did they let him jump into the river and drown? It must be the guests who killed my husband!" She then reported the matter to the officials. The officials interrogated the guests, who all said, "We were caught off guard and couldn't catch up with him. It was an unexpected event. How could close friends and relatives stand by and not try to save him?" When the officials questioned the bride and her mother, they only pleaded for the return of the body. The officials went to the bank of the river to inspect, but the vast river, with its long flow and distant source, made it impossible to find the body. Thus, the case remained unresolved.

    65

    未几，易一令，有明察声，见前官交有是案，反复推求，恍然曰：「婿投河而反诬客，非诬客也，欲客证新郎之死以实之也，是必有故。」变服为星卜流，访诸其邻，邻人曰：「有某富室，素与妇女无亲故，忽往来甚密，我侪亦疑有故。但是日新郎投河，众目共睹，岂非怪事？」令曰：「汝见之否？」对曰：「我亦在坐。」令曰：「汝视新郎貌作何色变？」对曰：「披发覆面不及见。」令曰：「道在是也。富室安在？」对曰：「今日犹见其入新妇家也。」令辞去。易服，率健役百余，突至妇家，围其前后户而搜之，仅有母女在，叩官欲何为？令无辞以对。

    Explanation

    65

    Not long after, a new magistrate was appointed, known for his sharp wit. He saw that the previous magistrate had handled a similar case, and he pondered it repeatedly, suddenly realizing, "The son-in-law threw himself into the river but accused the guest instead. This is not an accusation against the guest, but rather an attempt to have the guest confirm the death of the new husband to substantiate it. There must be a reason for this." The new magistrate changed his clothes and pretended to be a fortune-teller, inquiring among the neighbors. A neighbor said, "There is a wealthy man who has always had no close relationship with the woman, but suddenly they have been meeting very closely. We also suspect there is a reason. But on that day, the new husband threw himself into the river, and everyone saw it. Is this not a strange occurrence?" The magistrate asked, "Did you see it?" The neighbor replied, "I was also present." The magistrate asked, "What color did the new husband's face turn?" The neighbor replied, "His hair covered his face, and I could not see." The magistrate said, "The truth lies here. Where is the wealthy man?" The neighbor replied, "I still saw him enter the woman's home today." The magistrate then left. He changed his clothes again and led more than a hundred strong officials, suddenly arriving at the woman's home, surrounding and searching the front and back doors. They found only the mother and daughter inside, who asked what the magistrate wanted. The magistrate had no words to respond.

    66

    举步将入闺中，老妇横身阻曰：「此嫠女室，三尺童子，不许入门，况为民之父母，而不知礼乎？」令微哂曰：「欲为汝婿明冤耳。」老妇曰：「倘入室而无冤可明，将何如？」令曰：「我偿汝婿命。」乃呼役掖老妇出。令入房，见铺陈精洁，皆是常用什物，无可疑者。正踌躇间，俯视床下，见一男子履，回顾新妇，骇然失色。令呼众役入，移床而观，则地板有新垫者，命役举之，地道见。令带役入，穿出，至一密室。室隅，一鲜衣少年伏焉。执之。推门至院落，见地有新挖状，命役启之，生尸在，经年不变，喉间扼痕显然。遂出，聚案内人证，一讯服辜，论如律。乃知生醉后，妇女与富室，共扼其喉而毙，从地道舁入后院埋之。投水之人，系富室以重价觅善泅者为之也。

    66

    The magistrate raised a step to enter the inner room, but an elderly woman blocked his path, saying, "This is the widow's chamber; even a child of three feet tall is not allowed to enter, let alone a magistrate who should know better!" The magistrate smiled faintly and replied, "I wish to clear your son-in-law's name." The old woman asked, "What if entering the room reveals no wrong?" The magistrate said, "I will compensate your son-in-law's life." He then called upon his assistants to escort the old woman out. Entering the room, he saw the furnishings were neat and clean, all being common household items, nothing seemed suspicious. As he hesitated, he looked down at the bed and saw a man's shoe; looking back at the new wife, he was shocked and pale. The magistrate called his assistants to move the bed for inspection, and they found a new layer of padding on the floor. Ordering his assistants to lift it, they revealed a hidden passage. Leading his assistants through the passage, they emerged into a secret room. In the corner of the room, a young man in fine clothes was crouching. The magistrate seized him. Pushing open a door to the courtyard, they saw signs of recent digging. Ordering his assistants to dig, they found a corpse that had been there for years, with a clear mark of strangulation on the throat. Returning to gather evidence and witnesses, the magistrate conducted a thorough investigation and found the guilty party according to the law. It was then known that the man had been killed after getting drunk, by a woman and a wealthy person who strangled him. The body was thrown into the water by a wealthy individual who paid someone skilled in swimming to do so.

    67

    芗厈曰：人之阴谋诡计，惟图色为甚。然而天道昭彰，竟无不破之案，是以大盗亦戒采花。是案也，彼庸庸者流，竟谓新郎投河而死，众目观瞻，与妇女何尤？遂成疑案。其有心者，不过揣新郎之发狂也，或以药酒为之，疑女有故。然不能破其奸，敢讯诸乎？后令之勘访搜寻，可谓有胆有识。然使床下之男履不露，何从发其覆乎？我故曰：「天道也。」

    Explanation

    67

    Xiang Yan said: People's hidden and deceitful schemes are most extreme in their pursuit of beauty. However, the way of heaven is clear and evident, and no case remains unsolved. Thus, even great thieves are wary of picking flowers. This case, those ordinary people, claimed that the bridegroom drowned in the river, under the scrutiny of many eyes, what fault do they have with women? Thus, it became a suspicious case. Those with insight, no more than guessing that the bridegroom went mad, perhaps it was done with a drugged drink, suspecting that the woman had a reason. Yet unable to uncover their deceit, dare to ask about it? Later, the official investigated and searched, can be said to have courage and insight. Yet if the man's shoes were not revealed under the bed, how could they uncover the truth? I therefore say: 'It is the way of heaven.'

    68

    职谬
    　　滇南米商某，列肆于市。值县之少尉出，四人肩舆，隶卒擎盖执仗，前拥后呼，辟人于道，遇坐者喝之起。商适与客核账，思索出神，不及起。尉见之怒，执之舆前，责掌二十。尉去，商大哭。客哂之曰：「父母官责尔不敬，能不顺受，徒泣何为？」商曰：「彼父母官者，犹夫人耳，何以尊严若是？何科甲出身耶？」客笑曰：「彼铜进士出身，汝何不知？」商曰：「吾实不知铜进士为几甲？」客曰：「是不过银子科第三甲耳。」商曰：「如客所云，吾亦有银，何难与埒，甘受其辱。不亦过乎？」决意止肆，携赀入都，报捐未入流，分发畿南。但未习仪注，难以谒宪。

    Explanation

    68

    A Merchant's Mistake

    A merchant from Diannan set up his stalls in the market. At this time, a low-ranking military officer (少尉) was passing by. Four people carried his sedan chair, and attendants held an umbrella and a spear, clearing a path for him. When they encountered someone sitting, they shouted at him to stand up. The merchant, engrossed in calculating accounts with a guest, did not notice and remained seated. The officer saw this and became angry, ordering the merchant to be taken to the front of the sedan chair and receiving twenty blows with a stick. After the officer left, the merchant cried bitterly. The guest smiled and said, "Your honor, the local official scolded you for not showing proper respect. You should have accepted it calmly. Why are you crying?" The merchant replied, "That local official is just an ordinary person, why does he have such authority? What rank did he pass in the imperial examinations?" The guest laughed and said, "He is a copper scholar-official, how could you not know?" The merchant said, "I really don't know what rank a copper scholar-official is." The guest said, "He is just a third-rank scholar-official in the silver examination." The merchant said, "If that is the case, I also have money, why can't I match him? Why should I endure such humiliation? Is it not excessive?" Determined to change his situation, the merchant closed his shop, took his money to the capital, and reported and donated to obtain a minor official position. He was assigned to the southern part of the capital region. However, he had not yet learned the proper etiquette and procedures, making it difficult for him to pay respects to the governor.

    69

    幸都中有干仆，为之谋曰：「主所有者财耳，何不普拜乡亲，大开筵宴，既联桑梓之谊。藉学趋跄之礼，彼同仕者，孰不愿为指教耶？」商是其言，遍拜同乡，饮之食之，乡人皆乐为教，肆习旬余，拜跪叩首，皆无谬误。众议先见府道，以熟其仪，如无错谬，则可谒宪司矣。乃往见郡伯，嘉庆二十五年六月也。商公服而纬帽。郡伯者，人甚谦和，凡属员叩首，必手自扶之，扶之不起，必回礼。时商趋入遽跪，郡伯俯扶之，商纬帽极滑泽，贯郡伯朝珠于首，猛然起，珠散而郡伯几跪。凡有珠者，深恶此兆，以为不祥，故郡伯拂袖而入。左右检珠，咸笑曰：「客可以退矣。」商乃失色出，同官传为笑柄。众尤商曰：「汝未能从容进退，不可以见上宪，尚须练习。

    Explanation

    69

    A servant in the capital suggested a plan, saying, "The master has nothing but wealth. Why not widely greet fellow townspeople and hold grand banquets, thus connecting with the ties of hometown? Use this opportunity to learn the etiquette of formal bowing. Who among those in the same profession would not be willing to teach?" The person followed the advice, greeted all fellow townspeople, and treated them to meals. The townspeople were all happy to teach, and he practiced for about ten days. Bowing, kneeling, and prostrating, he performed these actions without any mistakes. Everyone agreed to first meet the officials of the prefecture to familiarize themselves with the etiquette. If there are no mistakes, then one can visit the governor's office. He went to see the prefect in the sixth month of the twenty-fifth year of the Jiaqing era. The person was dressed in official attire with a hat. The prefect was very modest and kind, always personally helping officials when they bowed. If they couldn't get up, he would certainly return the courtesy. Upon entering, the person hurriedly knelt. The prefect bent down to help, but the hat was extremely slippery and slid onto the prefect's neck beads. Suddenly standing up, the beads scattered and the prefect almost knelt. Those who wear beads deeply dislike this omen, considering it inauspicious. So the prefect brushed off his sleeves and left. The attendants collected the beads and laughed, saying, "The guest can leave now." The person then left in a panic, and his colleagues spread the story as a joke. Everyone criticized him, saying, "You cannot move in and out gracefully, so you cannot see the higher officials; you still need to practice."

    70

    」又逾月而国恤闻，官皆白衣冠，避舍二十七日后，素服顶帽见客。商之乡亲有与方伯司阍者善，谓之曰：「有敝乡里，初出茅庐者，恐贻同官笑，能使之独见宪台否？」司阍曰：「是不难，我主素无拘束，随到随见，使早来，我有以位置之。」随告商。时商已谒观察无误，方欣欣自得。次日，入藩署投谒，彼宪司之门房，强于下寮之厅事，铺设斐然。司阍者盛服据上坐，问其仆曰：「某官已至乎？」仆乃引商入。商见陈设眩目，人物轩昂，意为即方伯，趋入拜脆，献履历。司阍者笑曰：「误矣，敝主人不在此，且请少憩无躁。」商知有误，赧然坐。

    Explanation

    70

    After more than a month, the news of the national mourning period was heard, and all officials wore plain white clothing and hats, staying away from their homes for twenty-seven days before meeting guests in such attire. The merchant's fellow villager had a good relationship with the gatekeeper of the high-ranking official. He told him, "There is someone from my hometown who is just stepping out of the thatched hut, and I am afraid he will be laughed at by my colleagues. Can you arrange for him to see the high-ranking official alone?" The gatekeeper said, "It is not difficult. My master is usually not bound by strict rules and will see anyone who comes. If he comes early, I will arrange for him to be seen." Then he told the merchant. At that time, the merchant had paid his respects to the high-ranking official without any mistakes and was very happy and satisfied with himself. The next day, he went to the provincial governor's office to pay his respects. The reception area of the high-ranking official's office was better than the main hall of a lower-ranking official's office, with impressive decoration. The gatekeeper was wearing formal attire and sitting in a prominent position. He asked his servant, "Has a certain official arrived?" The servant then led the merchant in. The merchant saw the impressive decoration and the dignified people, thinking that it was the high-ranking official. He hurriedly went in to pay his respects and presented his resume. The gatekeeper smiled and said, "You are mistaken. My master is not here. Please rest for a while and do not be impatient." The merchant realized that he was mistaken and sat there with a blush.

    71

    司阍嘱其仆人探方伯，而内随官者，询知司阍之友，欲逞能而见好，命其仆引商先入客室，以候方伯。商见客堂一色纯白，无字画陈设，铺垫皆黑麻为之，不如门房远甚，意谓是必随官之室，不可自卑，再贻人笑，遂首座而趺坐。时方伯由内出，随官皆不及知，见上座有客，金其顶者，意谓幕中人，拱手让坐。商见方伯青衣，猝然问曰：「足下高姓？」方伯道其姓，商诧曰：「足下与大人同姓，可喜可贺。」时随官闻有人接谈，于门隙窥见主人已出，不觉皇然入，陈商之手版。方伯俯首阅，商甫见珊瑚其顶，惶恐之极，趋跪膝前曰：「大人该死！大人该死！」方伯拂然大怒，叱退之。后郡伯入见，方伯怒犹未息，语以故。郡伯曰：「是即散卑府之朝珠者，闻系市侩。」方伯曰：「商者无失其为商，何可乱我仕版？仍使归市可也。」遂休之。

    Explanation

    71

    The gatekeeper instructed his servant to inquire about the magistrate. The official inside, upon learning that the gatekeeper's friend wanted to show off and gain favor, ordered his servant to lead the merchant into the guest room first to wait for the magistrate. The merchant saw that the guest room was entirely white with no paintings or decorations, and the cushions and mats were made of black hemp, far inferior to the gatehouse. He thought this must be the room of the official, and one must not be humble, or else it will be laughed at, so he sat in the main seat in a cross-legged position. When the magistrate came out from inside, the officials did not know about it. Seeing a guest in the main seat with a gold-adorned hat, they thought he was someone from the inner office and bowed to let him sit. The merchant saw that the magistrate was wearing plain clothes and suddenly asked, "May I ask your surname?" The magistrate stated his surname, and the merchant exclaimed, "We share the same surname as the magistrate, which is a cause for joy and celebration." The official heard someone speaking and peeped through a crack in the door, seeing that the host had already come out. He rushed in and presented the merchant's visiting card. The magistrate bowed and looked at it. The merchant, upon seeing that the top was adorned with coral, became extremely frightened, hurriedly knelt in front of the magistrate, and said, "Sir, I am guilty! Sir, I am guilty!" The magistrate got extremely angry and scolded him away. Later, the prefect arrived to see, and the magistrate's anger was still not subsided. He told him the reason. The prefect said, "That is the one who scattered the morning pearls of the prefecture. It was heard that he was a merchant." The magistrate replied, "Merchants should not lose their identity as merchants; how can they disrupt the official records? Let them return to the market." Thus, he was dismissed.

    72

    芗厈曰：是躁人也，不第杂职中有之。闻有某尹，蜀人也。谒制军，问及峨嵋山猴子究有多大，尹对曰：「同大人大。」制军哂之。尹自觉谬，惶然改口曰：「与卑职一般大。」一日，与藩臬道会议，三官皆吸烟，命仆为尹点烟，尹曰：「卑职性不食烟，有三子均喜吸烟，恶之不暇，而身自犯耶？」皆传为笑柄。余故曰：躁则妄，妄则言多谬，当以三愆为戒，为之徐徐云尔。或曰不然，昔有人戒友之躁者，其人衣适着火，友见之而不言。火焚及身，怒其仆不早为扑灭。友曰：「我早见之，君戒我躁，我姑徐徐云尔。」若遇是人，又将何说？余恍然悟曰：「然则举世皆谬，若欲不谬，何如出世？」

    Explanation

    72

    Xiang Yan said: This person is impulsive, and such traits are not only found among those in miscellaneous positions. I once heard of an official from Sichuan who paid a visit to the provincial governor. When asked about the size of the monkeys on Mount Emei, the official replied, "As big as you." The governor smiled at him. The official then realized his mistake and, feeling anxious, changed his words to say, "As big as I am." One day, he met with officials of various ranks, and all three were smoking. The governor ordered a servant to light a pipe for the official. The official said, "I personally do not smoke; I have three sons who all enjoy smoking, and I dislike it too much to do it myself. How could I do it myself?" All this became the subject of ridicule. Therefore, I say that impulsiveness leads to rashness, and rashness leads to many false statements. One should take three faults as a warning and act cautiously. Some might say otherwise, however. In the past, there was someone who tried to caution a friend against impulsiveness. His friend's clothes suddenly caught fire, but the friend saw it and did not speak. The fire burned him, and he became angry at his servant for not extinguishing it earlier. The friend said, "I saw it early, but you warned me to be cautious, so I let it burn slowly." If one encounters such a person, what can one say? I suddenly realized, "Then the whole world is mistaken. If one wants to avoid being mistaken, how about leaving the world?"

    73

    智女
    　　嘉庆初年，白莲党之扰川楚也，贼帅掠良家妇女无算，内有楚女，英英特立，秀出冠群，帅爱而教留之。女曰：「得为将军之妻，妾之愿也。但妾诗礼旧家，虽乱杂中，不得父母之命，媒妁之言，然花烛合卺之礼，不可废也。日后为王为相时，妾叨福庇，称王妃夫人，确系堂堂配偶，得自立于人前，无苟合之讥。亦将军之光。」贼帅悦其词令，不觉首肯，使入室改装成礼。于是择掠得衣饰之美者，及脂粉之类，送与添装。复使他妇数人，入供役使。女退之，传命曰：「今日初见良人，无须役，明日惟命。

    Explanation

    73

    Translation:

    The Wise Woman

    In the early years of the Jiaqing era, during the disturbances caused by the White Lotus Rebellion in Sichuan and Hubei, the rebel leader captured countless women from respectable families. Among them was a woman from Chu, who was exceptionally intelligent and independent, standing out among her peers. The leader loved her and instructed her to stay. The woman said, "To become the general's wife is my wish. However, I come from a family with a tradition of scholarly and literary pursuits, and even in this chaos, I cannot marry without the consent of my parents and the involvement of matchmakers. Nevertheless, the traditional wedding ceremony involving the lighting of candles and the drinking of wine from a shared cup cannot be neglected. In the future, when I am called a princess or lady consort, I will be a proper and dignified spouse, able to stand before others without the criticism of a hasty or improper union. It will also be a source of glory for the general." The leader was pleased with her words and nodded in agreement, instructing her to enter the room to dress for the ceremony. They then selected beautiful clothing and cosmetics and sent them for her to adorn herself. The leader also sent several other women to assist her. The woman rejected this and conveyed a message: "Today is the first time I meet my husband, and there is no need for assistance. Tomorrow, as you command."

    74

    」贼以其处子碍羞，允之。女乃盥沐凝妆，见有利刃，窃袖之。贼帅因久待不出，入室窃窥其新装，益增秀媚，不觉心动，突入拥抱。女以刃直刺其心，立死之，推尸床上。以己之装饰饰贼尸，傅粉涂朱，剪己鬓贴其首，加以钗钿，望之宛似女身。女乃衣贼帅衣冠佩剑，薄暮出，呼马执旗而遁。其亲信者候之，彻夜不归。次日午刻，大营有令，众议将军昨何往，谅夫人知之。不得已，入室请命，见夫人尚卧，不敢骤近，觉血腥出于床，呼众人捡之，方知装夫人者将军。将军装者，不知其何往也。嗣是贼营得妇女，不敢留，掠人之风，因之稍戢。

    Explanation

    74

    The bandit, moved by the young woman's innocence and modesty, reluctantly agreed. The young woman then washed and dressed herself carefully. She saw a sharp knife and secretly put it into her sleeve. The bandit leader, having waited for a long time without seeing her, sneaked into the room to secretly look at her new attire. He was even more impressed by her grace and charm, and unconsciously felt a surge of desire. He suddenly rushed in and embraced her. The young woman stabbed him directly in the heart with the knife, killing him instantly, and pushed his body onto the bed. She used her own decorations to adorn the bandit's body, applied powder and rouge, cut her own hair and attached it to his head, and added hairpins and ornaments. To the onlookers, he looked like a woman. The young woman then wore the bandit leader's clothes, hat, and sword, left at dusk, called for a horse, held a flag, and fled. His trusted men waited for him all night without him returning. The next day at noon, the main camp issued an order, and the soldiers discussed where the general went yesterday, believing the general's wife knew. Reluctantly, they entered the room to ask for instructions and saw the general's wife still lying down. They dared not approach hastily, but noticed the smell of blood coming from the bed. They called everyone to investigate and realized that the general was disguised as the general's wife. The one who was disguised as the general, no one knew where he went. Afterward, the bandits in the camp did not dare to keep women, and the habit of kidnapping people gradually diminished.

    75

    芗厈曰：以甘言悦贼帅，使不备反而刺之，此古之节烈妇女为之者，不乏人。所可异者，颠倒阴阳，悠然而逝，出人意外。使不及追，且能全他人之节，何胆智之精细而雄烈耶？同时有贼得美妇，拦入深林，欲奸之，妇坚拒，不能成，贼怒甚，断其首而去，妇尸自移就首，竟凑合而生，年逾八旬乃卒。时又有百十妇女，以带联结众身，各持刀作方阵而行，贼冲之不散，围之不克，无可奈何，以火枪轰击而并殪之。惜乎，不得智女为之帅，以成奇观也。

    Explanation

    75

    Xiang Yan said: To win over the bandit leader with sweet words, making them unprepared and then stabbing them, this is a strategy employed by ancient chaste and heroic women, and there are many examples. What is strange is that they defy the natural order, depart quietly and mysteriously, and occur beyond people's expectations. If one cannot catch up, they can still preserve the chastity of others. How meticulous and heroic are their courage and intelligence! At the same time, a bandit obtained a beautiful woman, leading her into a deep forest, intending to rape her. She firmly refused, and he could not succeed. Enraged, he severed her head and left. The woman's body moved herself to reattach her head, and she lived to be over eighty years old before dying. There were also hundreds of women who linked their bodies together with ropes, each holding a knife and moving in a square formation. The bandits could not surround and capture them, and unable to do so, they killed them all with gunfire. Alas, not having a wise woman as their leader, they could not achieve a remarkable feat.

    76

    陆清献公遗事
    　　公讳陇其，号稼书，淛之当湖人。以理学名家，配享圣庙。公以进士即用，宰直隶灵寿县，父老相传，遗风善政，有足录者。昔公之任，无幕友官亲，二仆与官，三人而已。早起盥沐后，冠带坐堂上，唤吏役告之曰：「凡莅民，以省事为第一关，我无多事，不须若干人祗候。或农或贾，各就所能，以养尔父母妻子。但已领工食，应为国家办事，不能尽去。每日酌留书吏二人，衙役四名，轮班听事，余各执业，勿远离也。」暖阁之内，左右二几，一具律，一具平码，完粮银者，当堂弹兑，余厘毫，必还之。投呈者，呼至案前，细为评点曰：「某一节，人错待汝；某一节，无此情理，谎词也。

    Explanation

    76

    Final Translation

    The Legacy of Lord Lu Qingxian

    Lord Lu Qingxian, also known as Lu Longqi and styled Jiashu, was from Danghu in Zhejiang Province. Renowned for his expertise in Neo-Confucianism, he was enshrined alongside the Temple of Confucius. As a newly appointed Jinshi (imperial scholar), he was assigned to govern Lingshou County in Zhili Province. The elders of the county passed down stories of his good customs and wise governance, which are worth recording. When he took office, he did not have any advisors or relatives accompanying him; only two servants and himself, making a total of three people. After washing and dressing, he would sit on the dais and call the clerks and attendants to inform them: "In governing the people, the first principle is to simplify affairs. I have few matters to attend to, so there is no need for many people to wait on me. Whether you are farmers or merchants, each should do what you can to support your parents and families. However, those who have received their salaries should still perform their duties for the state and cannot all leave. Each day, I will choose to keep two clerks and four attendants, who will take turns attending to matters, while the rest should return to their professions and not stray far."

    In the warm chamber, there were two tables on either side, one with legal codes and the other with weights and measures. Those who paid their taxes in silver would have their transactions verified on the spot, and any remaining fractions would be returned to them. For those who submitted petitions, he would call them to the desk and carefully evaluate their cases, saying, "In one aspect, people have treated you wrongly; in another aspect, there is no such reason or logic, which is a lie."

    77

    」应讯者，即书票钤印过朱，差原告往传被告到案，曲为开导曰：「尔原被非亲即故，非故即邻，平日皆情之至密者，今不过为婚姻田土钱债细事，一时拂意，不能忍耐，致启讼端。殊不知一讼之兴，未见曲直，而吏有纸张之费，役有饮食之需，证佐之亲友，必需酬劳，往往所费多于所争。且守候公门，废时失业，一经官断，须有输赢，从此乡党变为讼仇，薄产化为乌有，切齿数世，悔之晚矣。即如此案某人故薄待某人。」即检律例以指示之曰：「罪应笞杖，但国法不加有礼之人，某合与某叩首服理，即回去静思三日，倘彼此豁然，来授结可也。」往往感激涕零，情愿当堂具结，和好如初，因此互相劝勉勿讼。半年之后，门庭如水，堂可张罗。

    Explanation

    77

    The person summoned to court is immediately issued a summons, stamped with an official seal, and passed through the red. The plaintiff is then sent to summon the defendant to court, and the process is gently guided by saying: "You, the plaintiff and defendant, are either relatives, friends, or neighbors, and in daily life, you are very close to each other. Now it is only about minor matters such as marriage, land, money, and debts. A moment of dissatisfaction, inability to tolerate, leads to the start of a lawsuit. You do not realize that when a lawsuit starts, the right and wrong have not yet been determined. Officials have expenses for paper, and servants have needs for food and drink. Friends and relatives who testify must be rewarded. Often the expenses exceed the amount in dispute. Waiting in court, wasting time and losing one's job. Once the court makes a decision, there must be a winner and a loser. From then on, neighbors turn into enemies due to litigation. Meager property is lost entirely. To harbor resentment for generations, but it's too late to regret. In this case, someone treated someone else poorly." The law is then checked and explained: "The crime should be punished with caning or flogging, but the law does not punish those who are polite. One should bow and accept the reason. Go back and reflect for three days. If both parties can resolve the matter, they can come to a settlement." Often they are deeply moved, willing to settle the matter in court, and reconcile as before. Therefore, they encourage each other not to litigate. After half a year, the court is as quiet as a deserted place, and the hall can be used for other purposes.

    78

    公无事，带一书一役，挨村讲乡约，训以孝弟忠信，节义廉耻，必引经据典，参以时事，民皆乐听，浅直易从，无窒碍难行者。遇孝慈节义之人，立即表扬，且为之咨嗟叹赏曰：「我所不及。」凡获小偷到案，则曰：「汝亦有人心者也，何至为此？」偷曰：「小人为贫所迫耳。」公曰：「是不难。为利之最厚者，莫如纺织，且人人能为之。」随命仆市棉花斤余，使偷在堂右，教以纺花之法。曰：「能，即释汝；不能，即惰也，罪加倍。」偷愿速释，无不留心学习，数日间，即能为矣。公曰：「此赀本不过数百钱耳，今数日内，循环例换，已赢余若干，除汝饭食外，尚剩有数百钱，汝回去执业。倘再犯，不恕汝也。」偷泣而去，改过迁善者多。间有犯，则杖而后教之，在堂上纺花一月。三犯，则曰：「是不能改矣。」使二役挟之急行千步，以热醋灌之，一碗饮至半，使一人突拍其背，则嗽终身不愈，不能作贼矣，仍纺花以没世。

    78

    Translation of the Source Text

    When the magistrate had no official duties, he would take one book and one assistant and go through the villages to preach the village regulations, teaching the people with the virtues of filial piety, fraternal duty, loyalty, trustworthiness, righteousness, and honor, always quoting classical texts and relating them to current events. The people all enjoyed listening, the teachings were simple and easy to follow, and there were no obstacles that made them difficult to implement. Whenever he encountered people who were filial, kind, righteous, and honorable, he would immediately praise them, and he would express admiration and praise, saying, "I cannot match this." Whenever a thief was caught, he would say, "You also have a human heart, why would you do this?" The thief would reply, "It is poverty that drives me to this." The magistrate would say, "It is not difficult. The most profitable thing is weaving, and everyone can do it." He then ordered a servant to buy a few pounds of cotton, had the thief stand to the right of the hall, and taught him the method of spinning cotton. He said, "If you can do it, I will release you; if you cannot, it is due to laziness, and the punishment will be doubled." The thief wanted to be released quickly, and with great attention, learned to spin cotton within a few days. The magistrate said, "The capital is no more than a few hundred coins, but within a few days, through repeated exchanges, it has already made a profit. After deducting your food expenses, you still have a few hundred coins left. Go back and practice your trade. If you commit the crime again, I will not forgive you." The thief left in tears, and many repented and reformed. If there were occasional offenders, they were beaten and then taught to spin cotton in the hall for a month. If someone could not be reformed, he would say, "This one cannot be reformed." He would have two assistants grab him and make him run a thousand steps quickly, then pour hot vinegar down his throat until half a bowl was consumed, and suddenly slap his back. He would have a cough that never healed, and he would never be able to steal again. He would continue to spin cotton until the end of his life.

    79

    时尚未设养廉。若奉文有摊捐款，必具文申请曰：「职奉银四十五两，仅敷自食，所需捐款，动钱粮耶？抑杂税耶？」道府寿，以挂面十束、筋烛一对，躬亲致祝。上游皆恶其执，甄别已之。后任甫至，即有报案者，系以斧杀人于旷野，不知凶手为谁。后官访于公曰：「老前辈任此数年，囹圄空虚，案无留牍，可见一邑之人，皆在春风化雨中矣。弟甫下车，即有疑难命案，若留疑以有待者，何也？」公曰：「方自愧虚糜，何敢当兄台盛誉？命案有无，偶然耳。案在何处？」曰：「某村。」公思之曰：「必某人所为也。」后官拘其人至，曰：「案无事由，杀无证佐，何所见而执吾？」后官曰：「此前官所教，必无谬误。」其人曰：「前官，圣贤也，岂肯冤人？」后官无词可答，曰：「带汝见前官，谅必有说。」于是押犯诣公。其人见公，即有惭惧之色。

    Explanation

    79

    At that time, the system of official salaries (养廉) was not yet established. If there was an order requiring the collection of donations, one must submit a formal request stating, "I am given forty-five taels of silver, which is barely enough to sustain myself. Are the required donations taken from regular revenue (钱粮) or miscellaneous taxes (杂税)?" When the prefect or governor celebrated their birthday, one must personally present ten bundles of noodles and a pair of strong candles as a gift. Superiors all detested his strict adherence to rules and removed him from office. As soon as the new official arrived, a report of a crime was filed. It was reported that someone was killed with an axe in the wilderness, and the identity of the murderer was unknown. The new official approached the previous official and said, "Respected elder, having served here for several years, your prison was empty, and there were no unresolved cases. It can be seen that the people of the entire county are under the gentle influence of benevolent governance. I have just taken office, and immediately a difficult murder case arose. If a case is left unresolved for future investigation, why is that?" The previous official replied, "I am just ashamed of my own incompetence, how dare I accept your high praise? The presence or absence of a murder case is purely coincidental. Where is the case?" The new official said, "In a certain village." The previous official thought for a moment and said, "It must have been done by a certain person." The new official then detained the suspect and said, "There is no clear motive for the killing, and no witnesses or evidence. What leads you to suspect me?" The new official said, "This is what the previous official taught me, and it must be correct." The suspect said, "The previous official was a sage, how could he wrong an innocent person?" The new official, unable to find words to respond, said, "Take you to see the previous official, he must have something to say." Thus, the suspect was brought to see the previous official. When the suspect saw the previous official, he immediately showed signs of shame and fear.

    80

    公呼使前，曰：「某人，汝忘余谆戒之苦心耶？余初至汝村讲乡约时，见汝面有凶横气，历历开导，汝色渐和。逾今三载，前色顿变，其为不改凶心，致有此事。可知杀人者死，罪无可逃，与其受尽责扑而后陈，不如直陈无隐，身不受亏，而恩犹可冀。」其人叩首泣曰：「洞见小人肺腑矣！昔年我与被杀之某，共交一嫠妇，后某独占而屏我，是不平。嗣公至以善劝人，人皆革面洗心，其不能者，为众所不齿。某偕妇出亡，我亦闻公言自悔。今公甫谢事，某与妇仍归旧村，且讪笑村众曰：『汝等不过畏陆青天耳，渠不能自保，今尚有此不近人情官耶？』小人恨其词，触前忿，潜杀之，意谓无人能破此寨，不意公竟先觉也，虽死奚辞！」后官怜其尚有良心，薄其罪而流之。国法，凡甄别官，例引见。公入都面君，见其岸然道貌，奏对从容不苟，圣祖大悦，卿相复保奏之，用为礼部主事，洊升侍御，致仕归。

    Explanation

    80

    The official called the person forward and said, "You, have you forgotten my earnest warnings and the effort I put into them? When I first came to your village to explain the village regulations, I saw that you had a fierce and violent appearance. I patiently and clearly instructed you, and your expression gradually became more peaceful. After three years, your expression suddenly changed. It seems you did not change your violent nature, leading to this incident. You know that the punishment for murder is death, and the crime cannot be escaped. It is better to confess everything openly and honestly, so that you do not suffer more punishment, and there is still hope for mercy." The person knelt and wept, saying, "You have seen through my heart! Years ago, I had a relationship with the woman who was killed. Later, he took her exclusively and excluded me. This was unfair. After the official came and taught people to be good, everyone changed their ways. Those who could not change were despised by others. I left with the woman. I also heard the official's words and repented. Now the official has just retired. I and the woman returned to our old village, and we mocked the villagers, saying, 'You are only afraid of the upright official. He cannot protect himself, and now there is still such an inhuman official?' I hated his words, and my anger was stirred, so I secretly killed him. I thought no one could break this conspiracy, but I did not expect the official to discover it. Even if I die, I have no regrets!" The official felt pity for him because he still had a conscience, so he reduced his punishment and exiled him. According to the national law, officials who are being evaluated are usually summoned for an audience. The official went to the capital to meet the emperor. He saw the official's dignified and virtuous appearance. The official answered questions calmly and without carelessness. Emperor Kangxi was very pleased. The grand councilors and high officials recommended him again. He was appointed as an official in the Ministry of Rites, then promoted to a higher position, and eventually retired.

    81

    芗厈曰：人之所以异于禽兽者，廉耻二字。若忘此，虽圣贤不能化也。故盗贼之三犯者，只好饮之以醋而已。至杀人者，虽因奸也，实缘讪笑公而顿激忿怒，斯人尚有良心。彼甄别公者，直斯人不若矣，当以醋灌之。
    　　
    　　补骗子(五则)
    　　京师布肆，大业也。有乡人来，阅布数十匹，约值京钱五十余贯。拣既，谓肆主曰：「我初学肩贩，须同伙来定，姑待之可乎？」应曰：「诺。」别为他人贸易。乡人坐半日，见买卖渐稀，谓肆主曰：「我尚未饭，伙又不来，身无余钱，所存赀本银两系合伙者，未便换钱，腹中馁甚，奈何？」肆主曰：「既有银两，无患无钱，若未便换，典之可也。」乡人欣然出银，灿然一提，揖肆主曰：「我不知质库在何处，此银二十两，请烦贵伙代为入典。但我不过饭食所需，质钱一缗足矣。」肆主交其伙典钱一串，并券交付，乡人感谢去。未几复来，肆主曰：「何速也？」曰：「吾侪小人，果腹而已，不求甚佳。

    Explanation

    81

    Xiang Yan said: "The difference between humans and animals lies in the two concepts of integrity and shame. If one forgets this, even sages cannot transform them. Therefore, for a thief who has committed three crimes, one can only make them drink vinegar. As for a murderer, though provoked by jealousy, he is actually driven to sudden anger by mocking him. Those who distinguish themselves by mocking him are even worse than him, and should be made to drink vinegar."

    Supplement on Fraudsters (Five Cases)

    In the capital, a cloth shop is a major business. A villager came and selected dozens of bolts of cloth, worth more than fifty thousand coins. After selecting, he said to the shop owner: "I am new to carrying goods, and need my partner to come to finalize, can I wait a bit?" The shop owner replied: "Yes." He then went to trade with others. The villager sat for half a day, seeing that business was slowing down, he said to the shop owner: "I haven't had my meal yet, my partner hasn't come, I have no extra money, the silver I have is from my partnership, so I can't exchange it, I'm very hungry, what should I do?" The shop owner said: "Since you have silver, you don't have to worry about lacking money, if you can't exchange it, you can pawn it." The villager happily took out the silver, presented it in a shining manner, and bowed to the shop owner: "I don't know where the pawnshop is, this silver is twenty taels, please ask your partner to deposit it for me. But I only need enough for my meal, pawning a thousand coins would be sufficient." The shop owner gave his partner a thousand coins and a pawn ticket, and the villager thanked him and left. Shortly after, he returned, and the shop owner said: "Why did you come back so soon?" He replied: "We common folk, just want to fill our stomachs, we don't demand much."

    82

    」余钱八百余文，掷柜上，坐守至晚，其伙竟不来。乡人惶然谓肆主曰：「天将暮，难出城，我伙或以要事不得来，盍以我二十金之券，抵运布去，尚有余钱，明日偕伙来算可乎？」应曰：「可。」乡人乃郑重出券，交之曰：「此即贵伙代当者，请留三日，我自赎取归账。」肆主验之无误，遂收执。乡人以余钱雇驴车，载布去。候之三日，竟不来，乃赴质库取银，仅有二两，肆主曰：「我所质者二十两大锭也，何以仅止此？」典主查簿示之曰：「是日贵伙以二十金质钱一串，我疑其所需过少，问之，曰：『是客物也，只需此为饭食耳。』我予券去。随即有乡人持券加利取去，又有二人，以此小锭亦质钱一串，汝所收之券是也。」肆主始恍然悟为骗子掉换去矣。

    Explanation

    82

    The shopkeeper had eight hundred plus cash coins left over, which he tossed onto the counter, sat waiting until evening, but his partner finally didn't come. The villagers anxiously said to the shop owner, "The day is ending, it's difficult to leave the city, my partner may have been unable to come due to urgent matters. Why not use my twenty gold coins' voucher to pay for the shipment of cloth? There is still some leftover money, can we settle the rest tomorrow with my partner?" The shop owner replied, "Yes." The villagers then carefully presented the voucher, gave it saying, "This is your partner's voucher, please keep it for three days, I will redeem it and settle the account myself." The shop owner verified that it was correct and then took it. The villagers hired a donkey cart with the leftover money and took the cloth away. They waited for three days, but finally didn't come, so they went to the pawnshop to get the silver. There was only two taels. The shop owner said, "The twenty taels' large ingots I pledged, why is it only this much?" The pawnbroker checked the ledger and showed it saying, "On that day, your partner pledged twenty gold coins for a string of cash coins. I suspected that what they needed was too little, so I asked them. They said, 'These are the guest's things, they only needed this for food.' I gave the voucher to them. Immediately, a villager came with the voucher and took it away with interest. And two more people used these small ingots to pledge a string of cash coins. The voucher you received is this one." The shop owner suddenly realized that the fraudsters had switched it.

    83

    京师骡马市，大集也。有贵官，戴五品冠，服色甚丽，气象雄伟，似武弁入朝者。至鞍鞯市，择一佳者，出大银一锭，谓肆主曰：「我仆因买他物，分遣开矣。烦汝伙肩此鞍至骡市，我欲试良马也。」主者即遣一人为负去。至市，择一大骡甚骏，价值数百金，命来人以鞍鞯备之曰：「汝在此姑待，我试骑之。」卖骡人见有仆在，任其鞭驰而去，久不返。谓其人曰：「汝主何往耶？」其人曰：「我鞍鞯铺之伙，孰为我主？」卖驴人骇曰：「是必骗子也。汝铺亦被诓矣。」其人曰：「幸有银在。」于是偕往铺中，出银公估，则铅心伪物也。共鸣诸官，海捕而已。

    83

    Final Translation

    In the capital city's horse and donkey market, a large gathering was taking place. A high-ranking official, wearing a fifth-rank official's hat and dressed in splendid attire, had a majestic and imposing appearance, resembling a military officer entering court. He arrived at the saddle and bridle market and chose one of the best saddles, producing a large silver ingot and saying to the shop owner, "My servant went to buy other things and was sent away. Please have your assistant carry this saddle to the horse market. I want to try out a good horse." The shop owner immediately sent an assistant to carry it away. Arriving at the market, the official chose a very strong and fast donkey worth several hundred gold coins and ordered the assistant to prepare the saddle and bridle, saying, "You stay here for a moment. I will try riding it." The donkey seller, seeing that there was an assistant, allowed him to ride off. The assistant did not return for a long time. The donkey seller said to the assistant, "Where did your master go?" The assistant replied, "I am just an assistant from the saddle and bridle shop. Who is my master?" The donkey seller was startled and said, "This must be a scammer. Your shop has also been deceived." The assistant replied, "Fortunately, there is still some silver." So they went to the shop together and presented the silver for public appraisal, which turned out to be a fake with a lead core. The officials were alerted, and a manhunt was launched.

    84

    某观察，富而淫者也。姬妾满前，各自树党争宠，而正夫人不顾也。需次会垣时，恒有花婆出入公馆，忽带少妇，携珠翠求售。其为人也，轻盈软媚，妇女皆爱怜之。夫人乐于盘桓，曰：「那得若个好娘子，长为我伴，则我得所托矣。」妇笑曰：「妾何如人，敢当夫人青目耶！妾夫素跟官，若夫人不弃，言于大人，则夫妇皆有倚赖矣。」长跪而请。夫人曰：「是不难。尔能并事大人，与我一气，何事不可也？」妇再拜称谢。

    Explanation

    84

    A certain provincial inspector, rich and indulgent, had numerous concubines and maidservants, each forming factions to compete for his favor, while his principal wife remained indifferent. During his time in the capital awaiting an appointment, a matchmaker frequently visited his residence. One day, she brought a young woman, adorned with jewelry, seeking to sell herself to the official. The woman was graceful, soft, and charming, and the women in the household all loved and pitied her. The principal wife was delighted to have her stay, saying, "How I wish there were a woman like you to be my companion; then I would have someone to rely on." The woman smiled and said, "What kind of person am I, to be favored by the lady? My husband has always served the great man. If you do not reject me, speak to the great man on my behalf, and then both my husband and I will have a place to rely on." She knelt long and begged. The principal wife replied, "This is not difficult. If you can serve the great man together with me and be in harmony with me, what cannot be done?" The woman bowed twice in thanks.

    85

    适观察入，夫人使妇递茶，即以眉目传情，观察大悦，问此妇何来？夫人以夫妇愿投靠对，观察曰：「其妇如是，其夫可知。我正少一知心青衣，收之可也。」妇即迎膝叩首，观察手援之，即扶观察之手而起，益悦之，于是妇留而花婆去。唤其夫来，果干仆也。其夫妇遂迁居邻院，朝出暮归，殷懃奉侍。观察虽与妇情密，调唇抚乳，无所不为，而未及于乱者，公馆无隙地也。一日，妇送茗至书室，观察置诸膝而恳曰：「能毕乃公心事，则衣珠财物惟汝所欲。」妇曰：「非不甘心，奈众目昭彰乎？无已，请遣我夫他出，晚至妾室，惟命是从矣。」言甫毕，报客至，妇脱身入。

    Explanation

    85

    Just as the magistrate arrived, the wife sent a woman to serve tea. Immediately, the woman conveyed her feelings through her facial expressions, and the magistrate was greatly pleased. He asked where this woman came from. The wife responded that the couple wished to rely on him. The magistrate said, "If the wife is like this, the husband can be known to be similar. I am lacking a trusted female servant, and taking her in is possible." The woman bowed deeply and knelt before the magistrate. He lifted her by the hand, and she helped him stand up, making him even more pleased. Thus, the woman serving tea left, and the couple moved to a neighboring courtyard. They diligently served the magistrate, going out in the morning and returning in the evening. Although the magistrate had a close relationship with the woman, engaging in intimate physical contact, they did not act on it due to the lack of privacy in the magistrate's residence.

    One day, the woman brought tea to the study room. The magistrate placed her on his knees and earnestly said, "If you can fulfill my desires, then clothes, jewels, and wealth are yours to desire." The woman replied, "Not unwilling, but how can it be done with so many eyes watching?" If there is no other way, she suggested sending her husband away, and she would meet him alone in the evening, following his commands. As soon as she finished speaking, the report of guests arriving came, and the woman quickly left to avoid being seen with the magistrate.

    观察乃以数十金，使其夫远出干事，当晚潜入妇室，妇亦早归，正好合时，其夫持刀排门突入，喝曰：「我知汝年轻。必不能安其室，果留男子，合杀却否？」妇泣跪曰：「非妾敢犯救，主人势逼，无奈相从。」夫曰：「必非主也，岂有身后贵官，而知法犯法哉？」妇泣唤主起，夫乃持刀视曰：「果是主人，将何以全奴颜面乎？」观察曰：「汝能周旋，将以汝为长班。得官之日，政由宁氏，祭则寡人，能容之否？」其夫半跪称谢，呼妇起曰：「汝好好伺候主人，我出差去矣。

    86

    The official gave several dozen taels of silver and sent his husband away on some errand. That night, he secretly entered the woman's room. The woman had also returned early, and they met just in time. The husband, holding a knife, burst in and shouted, "I know you are young and cannot keep your husband content.     」观察色丧神颓，妇起闭门，投怀而慰解之，始得安于阳台。未几，观察得缺，竟以其司阍，妇则留于内室，不复出矣。其夫大权在握，任其播弄，观察无可如何，听之而已。然能劝其主勉事上官。未几权廉访，其夫招摇撞骗，无所不为。时有富室身犯大辟，许以数万金出罪，富室知为廉访信使，从之，得赃而遁，富室首于中丞。廉访始知其事，亟传妇严讯之。妇曰：「是非妾夫也，妾本妓女，彼以重聘雇妾来，认为夫妇，嘱妾勾引主人，若得满载而归，许以半分，妾故愿为之使。然不知其何许人，姓氏亦未确也。」廉访无可奈何，坐此败官。后妇之本夫来，又不得不重酬妇而遣之。

    Explanation

    87

    The observer's appearance was disheartened and his spirit weary. The woman got up, closed the door, embraced him, and comforted him, and he finally found peace on the bed. Shortly after, the observer was given a vacancy and was eventually appointed as a gatekeeper. The woman stayed in the inner chamber and did not come out again. Her husband held great power and manipulated things as he pleased. The observer could do nothing about it and simply tolerated the situation. However, he could still advise his master to be diligent in serving his superiors. Shortly after, he gained the position of Censor-in-Inspector. His husband became ostentatious and deceitful, engaging in all kinds of misconduct. At that time, a wealthy man was sentenced to death and was offered the chance to escape punishment by paying a large sum of money. Knowing the Censor-in-Inspector was involved, the wealthy man paid the bribe and escaped with the money. He then reported the incident to the vice-premier. The Censor-in-Inspector then learned of the matter and immediately summoned the woman for a strict interrogation. The woman said, "This is not my husband. I was originally a courtesan, and he hired me with a large dowry, treating me as his wife. He instructed me to seduce the master, promising half the loot if I succeeded. I willingly did as he asked, but I do not know who he really is or his true name." The Censor-in-Inspector could do nothing about it and was disgraced and dismissed from office. Later, the woman's original husband came, and the Censor-in-Inspector had to heavily reward her and send her away.

    有徐大诳者，丝市中伙也。平日喜诳人取笑，以是得其美称。一日，随居停至吴下贸易，舟泊太子码头，居停谓徐曰：「予起货去，汝留此须慎防之，此处多骗子，勿为所诳。」徐曰：「吾不诳人，人其诳我乎？人果行其诳，我将诳谁矣？」居停曰：「咍！此处骗子，皆鲜衣盛服，充衣冠中人。汝若遇之，必逢迎不惶，恐小巫见大巫，堕其术中而不觉也。汝必慎之。」徐曰：「诺。请予洋银二牧，我将作虎邱之游。」居停给之而去。见肆有锡洋钱，为孩童所玩弄者，与真无异。

    There was a man named Xu Da Kuang, a common figure in the silk market. He enjoyed deceiving people to make them laugh, and thus gained a good reputation. One day, he traveled to the Wu region with his host for trade, and their boat docked at the Prince's Dock. The host told Xu, "I will go to fetch goods, so you must stay here and be cautious. There are many deceivers here, and you should not be deceived." Xu replied, "I do not deceive others, so how could others deceive me? If others indeed deceive, who would deceive me?" The host said, "Ha! The deceivers here are all well-dressed and appear respectable. If you meet them, you will be too eager to please, and you might be outmatched by a superior and fall into their tricks without realizing it. You must be careful." Xu said, "Yes. Please give me two silver dollars, and I will go on a trip to Tiger Hill." The host gave him the money and left. Xu saw counterfeit silver coins being played with by children in a shop, which were indistinguishable from real ones.

He carried the bag back to his boat, changed into simple rural attire, and wandered in the market holding an umbrella and carrying the bag. He saw a well-dressed customer sitting in front of an antique shop. It was the height of winter, and the customer was wearing a luxurious fur coat of red fox, a hat and leather shoes of raccoon, and holding a tobacco pipe with a jade mouthpiece, silver head, and ebony body. Gradually, something stirred in his heart, and he sat on the steps of a large house across the street. He showed his account and the tinsel coins in front of the customer, juggled real foreign coins, and muttered complaints.     I am a native of a certain county. Because my niece is about to get married, my brother gave me a hundred yuans and an invoice, to buy her wedding clothes. I arrived in a big city, but I didn't know where the big silk and satin shop was, nor did I know if the items on the invoice were sufficient. No one guided me, and that's why I was resentful. A guest took the invoice and looked at it, and saw that all the items were urgently needed for the dowry. He believed it to be true and smiled, pointing out, "A mile or so to the north, inside a high wall and big gate, there is a silk and satin shop. It is set up by my relative. Even though there is a signboard, I can't recognize it. Please let me follow you for a guide." The guest said, "Fortunately, I have nothing to do. You should follow me."

    」徐负囊随其后，行未几，徐曰：「我尚未餐，腹中馁甚，官人肯同一点心否？」客乃引入麫肆上坐，徐坐其旁，麫尚未至，徐促额曰：「我患疟痢未痊，不意又发作矣，中急而寒甚，奈何？」客曰：「去厕不远，汝去登之。」徐曰：「奈此累坠物乎？」举囊交客曰：「暂累官人看守，我非不放心，奈寒甚，乞假我短挂一披，烟管一吸。」客自思火狐短挂与烟管不过三十余金，诓其百洋，其利倍蓗，乃故作踌躇而后解语之曰：「此百金物，汝速往速来，慎勿污我衣。」徐乃郑重披裘执筒而逸。客待其出肆，携囊遁回，谓家人曰：「今日诓得洋银百元，当为我贺。」出囊审之，疑有伪，急请识者，方知皆锡物，不禁哑然失笑曰：「我一生骗人为业，反为人骗，数十年老阿婆，今竟倒绷孩儿矣。」

    Xu carried a bag and followed behind, walking not far when Xu said, "I have not yet eaten, my stomach is very hungry, will you share some food with me?" The guest then led Xu into a flour shop and sat down, with Xu sitting beside him. The bread had not yet arrived, and Xu pressed his forehead, saying, "I am suffering from malaria and diarrhea, which have not fully healed, and unexpectedly, they have flared up again. I feel hot and cold alternately, what can I do about it?" The guest said, "The toilet is not far away, go and use it." Xu replied, "What about these heavy items?" He lifted the bag and handed it over to the guest, saying, "Temporarily entrust you to watch over it, I'm not being careless, but I'm very cold, so I ask for a short coat to wear and a pipe to smoke." The guest thought that a short coat and a pipe were worth no more than thirty or forty silver dollars, and if he could trick a hundred silver dollars, the profit would be doubled. So he hesitated and then said, "This is a hundred-dollar item, go quickly and come back quickly, be careful not to dirty my clothes." Xu carefully put on the coat and took the pipe, then left quickly. The guest waited until Xu left the shop, carried the bag and hurriedly returned, telling his family, "Today I tricked a hundred silver dollars, you should congratulate me." He took out the bag to examine it, suspecting it might be fake, and quickly asked someone knowledgeable, who found out they were all tin. He could not help but laugh helplessly, saying, "I have been in the business of deceiving others all my life, but now I have been deceived myself, after many years as an old trickster, I have been duped by a child."

    查禁倭烟之年，有伪符假役，在江河之间，挨船搜索，讹攫银钱，为害行旅。惟不掠贷物，不携衣装，是以告讦之案甚少。有黠客贩货入楚，舟泊江滨，突来壮役七八人，铁索郎当，手持签票，口称官命，查抄鸦片，入舟搜检。见银钱皆取之，以充饭食。值客卧病，其伙拦阻不及，盘缠被攫尽矣，不觉垂泪。客徐起见之，笑曰：「毋作妇人态。从来悖入者亦悖出，被将十倍偿我，无忧也。」是时同泊之舟，无一免者，人皆切齿。

    92

    In the year when the ban on Japanese opium was enforced, there were fake officials and impostors who, in the rivers and streams, searched boat by boat, deceiving and seizing silver, causing harm to travelers. They only seized silver and did not take goods or clothing, which is why cases of accusation and denunciation were few. A shrewd merchant transporting goods to Chu had his boat anchored by the riverbank. Suddenly, seven or eight strong men appeared, with iron chains clinking, holding official-looking documents, claiming to be acting by official orders, searching and confiscating opium, entering the boat and searching. They took all the silver and used it to pay for food. When the merchant was ill, his companions could not stop them in time, and all his travel money was taken, causing him to unconsciously shed tears. The merchant slowly got up and saw them, smiling and saying, "Do not act like a woman. What goes in against the rules will come out against the rules; I will be compensated tenfold, there is no need to worry." At that time, no boat moored there was spared, and everyone was furious.

    黠客于是择舟子之强有力者十余人，饰以仆从之服，自乃冠水晶顶，造作令箭，急易快舟，尾追伪役，沿江而下。役掳掠满载，忽绕出其前，使仆截擒，即以其铁索锁之。登邮亭而讯曰：「本厅奉军门查拿伪役抄抢案，送省枭示。」先起其赃，彼舟载银钱已数千矣，伪授皆叩首乞命。于是运赃入己舟，将伪役交驿卒看守曰：「候本厅禀报后，来取若人，勿任逃脱，自干重罪。」竟扬帆逆流而归，以钱俵分舟子，银则归己，无不欢呼痛快。伪役忽解悟，告驿卒曰：「是官也，何以获赃不获犯？假可知也。」驿卒亦悟，曰：「无论真假，我辈岂白与人看待哉！」伪役已无一钱，乃各脱其衣履贿驿卒，始得纵归。
    　　芗厈曰：骗子奇矣，然不过乘人所欲而中之，乃竞有骗骗子者，使之笑不得哭不得，大快人心。可见天下事，出奇无穷。纵有智士才人，只好一齐俯首。

    93

    The cunning guest then selected more than ten strong boatmen, dressed them in the attire of servants, and himself donned a crystal crown, creating a forged command token. He quickly exchanged for a fast boat and pursued the fake officials downstream along the river. The impostors, laden with loot, suddenly turned and appeared before him, allowing his men to intercept and capture them, binding them with iron chains. He ascended the post station and questioned them, saying, "This office has been ordered by the military commander to investigate and apprehend the fake officials involved in looting cases, to be sent to the province for public display." He first confiscated their loot, which amounted to thousands of silver and coins, and the fake officials all knelt and begged for mercy. He then transported the loot to his own boat and handed the fake officials over to the post station guards for custody, instructing them, "After I report back, come and take these people; do not let them escape, as you will bear the consequences." He set sail upstream and returned, distributing the money among the boatmen, keeping the silver for himself. All cheered with great satisfaction. Suddenly, the fake officials realized the truth and told the post station guards, "He is an official. Why did he seize the loot but not the criminals? It is known to be a deception." The post station guards also realized, saying, "Regardless of whether it is true or false, we cannot be treated as if nothing." The fake officials, having no money left, each removed their clothes and shoes to bribe the post station guards, finally being allowed to go free.

    Xiang Yan said: The trickster is indeed extraordinary, yet he merely takes advantage of what others desire and strikes at it. But there are those who trick the tricksters, leaving them unable to laugh or cry, greatly pleasing the heart. It is evident that in the world, the unexpected is endless. Even if there are wise and talented people, they can only bow their heads in unison.

    奸僧狱
    　　浙有嘉禾生，为邑之巨富，将入棘闱，偕其妻与姑母仆婢辈，同赴武陵，寓西湖山庄，以便游观。生妇少艾而佞佛，以天竺进香为请，生从之，命仆唤肩舆。仆体主人省约意，不投行家，散雇舆六乘，价甚廉。生妇艳妆盛饰，罗绮满身，珠翠盈头，价值千金，乃与姑母仆妇婢女辈乘舆而行，生骑马在先，仆携香烛随行。至半途，生妇之舆杆折，五乘皆随骑而前，是舆落后。一夫抽取折杆回去，谋易新者，一夫守之，仆亦立候。舆夫笑曰：「主人将抵山门矣。汝不以香烛去，有不失误詈汝者乎？况五乘前行，仅一乘伙回易杆，即来，何须呆守耶？」仆信其言，追奔而去。一夫以杆来，共舁入乱山中。生妇惶惑诘问，何以行僻径，舆夫曰：「为时已久，恐官人守候，出快捷方式，入庙之后户，不甚便耶？」妇亦信之。未几停舆，见墙缺朱门，舆夫轻叩其铜环，一沙弥提关出曰：「来耶？」至舆前，请夫人下舆。

    Explanation

    The Case of the Deceitful Monk
    　　In Zhejiang, there was a wealthy man named Jiahesheng. He was about to enter the imperial examination halls and, accompanied by his wife, mother-in-law, and their servants, headed to Wuling. They stayed at a residence near West Lake to facilitate their sightseeing. His wife, a young and beautiful woman devoted to Buddhism, requested to go to Tianzhu (India) to offer incense. Jiahesheng agreed and ordered his servant to call for sedan chairs. The servant, understanding his master's frugal intentions, did not hire them from a professional carriage house but instead hired six sedan chairs separately, which were very cheap. His wife, dressed in luxurious silk robes and adorned with jewels and jade worth a thousand gold pieces, set off with her mother-in-law and the servants in the sedan chairs, while Jiahesheng rode ahead on horseback, and the servant carried the incense and candles. Halfway through their journey, the pole of one of the sedan chairs broke, and all five chairs followed on horseback, leaving the broken one behind. One man removed the broken pole and went back to replace it with a new one, while another stayed to guard it, and the servant also waited. The sedan chair carrier laughed and said, "The master is about to reach the temple gate. If you don't go with the incense and candles, will you not be blamed for making a mistake? Besides, with five chairs already ahead, only one needs to return to replace the pole, and it will be here soon. Why should you wait idly?" The servant believed him and went off in pursuit. One man came back with the new pole, and they carried her into the mountains. His wife, in a state of confusion, asked why they were taking a shortcut. The sedan chair carrier replied, "We have been waiting for a long time, and we are afraid the master will be waiting. This is a quick way to enter the temple through the back gate, which is not very convenient?" The wife also believed him. Soon, the sedan chair stopped at a place with a red gate and a wall. The sedan chair carrier lightly knocked on the copper ring, and a novice monk opened the door and said, "Come?" They then asked the lady to get off the sedan chair.

    生妇曰：「我家人安在耶？」沙弥曰：「多在前殿，候夫人久矣。」生妇视沙弥，年不过八九龄，谅无他，不得已，从之入门，曲折引入密室，请夫人少坐。沙弥去而健妇至，生妇益惶急，亟询官人安在，健妇笑曰：「休问官人，我辈皆香客，亦为大师掠至，无奈相从，汝若婉顺，则此间吃着不尽。且人尽夫也。何乐如之？否则暴虐相加，无从逃避。」妇知入危地，悲忿觅死。一僧突入曰：「何来泼妇，入我法门中，敢肆横耶？」喝令健妇并沙弥齐上。将生妇衣饰洗剥，以布带缚其手足于醉翁椅上，强奸之。生妇痛骂，又一僧以麻桃塞其口而递淫之，妇亦昏沉如醉，听之而已。至夜，健妇以米粉汤执鼻而灌，不得不咽，仍劝其相从，自苦无益。生妇任以巧言，合目不答，健妇以衾覆之而去。次日来，除其失溺，为之洗沐，焚香于室，群僧复入，互相嬲也。如是六七日，忽见群僧变色相谋，变头接耳，不可闻。是夜健妇灌之以药，冥然如死。

    The wife of the living person said, "Where are my family members?" The novice monk replied, "They are mostly in the front hall, waiting for the lady for a long time." The wife knew she had entered a dangerous place and sought death out of sorrow and anger. A monk suddenly entered and said, "What kind of scolding woman comes here?
