That night, the strong woman poured powdered rice soup into her nose, forcing her to swallow it. She still encouraged her to comply, saying it would be futile to suffer. For six or seven days, they suddenly saw the monks change color and plot together, whispering to each other, unheard. That night, the strong woman gave her medicine, and she became completely unconscious like a dead person.

    After three days, there was still no trace of the person in question. The student then went to the examination hall to wait for the test and discussed the matter with his relatives and friends. An experienced person advised, "The high-ranking official now cares for scholars. The patrol officer submitted a public petition, and the high-ranking official ordered to summon the plaintiff and several experienced people. He said to them, "A certain student brought his wife to the exam and led her to wander around. This is inherently impolite, leading to teaching theft and lust, all of which cannot be determined. However, if there is such a major case and it cannot be solved, it is also the responsibility of high officials." He then ordered the mid-level military commander to lead five hundred strong soldiers, change clothes and disguise, and spread out to search in various temples in West Lake, with a deadline of three days to capture the criminals and rewards for success. The prefect and county officials nodded and withdrew, ordered hundreds of servants, pretended to be incense-burning visitors, spread out in various temples, and had the student's servant act as an informant to look for them.

    98

    逾二日无迹，文武员弁惶恐，共谋将挨搜僧之密室。僧大惧，以药迷生妇，夜使健者负置乞丐茅棚，丐者惊呼，兵役咸集，见一蓬首垢面着僧衣裤之妇，奄奄一息，势将毙矣。急唤生来认，确系其妻，呼仆妇来，舁之归寓。以开通小药灌之，穷日夜乃醒。见姑母在旁，泣诉所苦。时兵役因已得妇，皆回署禀报，生亦以前情补呈府县。各官聚谋曰：「虽有妇而不知其地其人，将何以定案？无已，尽拘西湖僧，使妇辨之，冤可白矣。」乃使生归而谋诸妇，妇愧怍难言，乘人不备而缢。生又鸣诸官，官亦无可如何矣。时诸僧已集千余人，无不呼冤者。即有奸僧在内，无可对证，良莠莫辨，以告中丞，乃命兵役遍抄静室，于兰若内搜得女舄，即以所住之僧锻炼成狱而斩之。冤乎不冤，未可知也。

    Explanation

    98

    After two days, there was no trace, and both civil and military officials were filled with anxiety. They collectively plotted to search the monk's private chambers. The monk was greatly afraid and used medicine to sedate the living woman. At night, he had strong men carry her to a beggar's hut. The beggars cried out in alarm, and the soldiers gathered. They saw a woman with unkempt hair, a dirty face, and wearing monastic clothing, on the brink of death, seemingly about to die. They urgently called the husband to identify her, and it was indeed his wife. They then called the servants to carry her back to the inn. They gave her a mild medicine to revive her, and she woke up after many days and nights. She saw her mother-in-law beside her and wept, recounting her suffering. At that time, the soldiers, having found the woman, all returned to report, and the husband also submitted a report to the county and prefecture about the previous events. The officials gathered and said, "Although we have found the woman, we do not know her location or identity. What shall we do to resolve the case? There is no other way, so we must arrest all the monks in West Lake and let the woman identify them. The injustice can be cleared." They then sent the husband back to consult with his wife. The wife felt ashamed and could not speak, and she hanged herself when no one was looking. The husband then reported to the officials again, but the officials could do nothing about it. At that time, all the monks had gathered, numbering over a thousand, and none of them did not cry out in their innocence. Even if there were guilty monks among them, there was no evidence to prove it, and it was impossible to distinguish between the good and the bad. They reported to the governor, who then ordered the soldiers to search all the quiet rooms. They found women's shoes inside a temple, and they then convicted the monk who lived there and executed him. Whether it was a miscarriage of justice or not, it is hard to say.

    99

    芗厈曰：僧固不法，而生实自贻伊戚，冶容诲淫，何可厝崭于火？是以律禁妇女入庙烧香，此正本清源之良法也。至案已成，即使妇不死，赧颜辨认。余知此等奸僧，必不在千百众之内，送女出时，早已纠集远扬矣。然以僧室而有女舄，纵非此案奸僧，而平日所，谅必更甚于此，是以神泄其机，致被搜获，斩之亦不为冤。况杀一可以警百，亦大中丞力也。否则，此等案件，地方官只好置诸海捕而已。

    Explanation

    99

    Xiang An said: Monks are indeed lawless, but the trouble they cause is self-inflicted. Adorned appearance invites lust; how can such people be thrown into the fire? Therefore, laws prohibit women from entering temples to burn incense, which is a good method to address the root of the problem. When the case is resolved, even if the woman does not die, she must be ashamed to admit her involvement. I know that such wicked monks are not among the thousands, and when they send the girl out, they have already gathered and fled far away. However, since there are women's shoes in the monks' quarters, even if these monks are not the ones involved in this case, their daily actions are likely even worse, so the god revealed the secret, leading to their capture and execution, which is not unjust. Moreover, killing one can warn a hundred, which is also the strength of the Grand Censor. Otherwise, such cases would only be dealt with by issuing a general warrant for the arrest of the bandits.

    Righteous Thief
    Huang Bazi, a notorious bandit from Taihu Lake, followed the bandit leader to rob a wealthy household, with eighteen men armed with torches and weapons. They broke down the door and searched room by room for valuables. The bandit leader entered the room of the household's daughter, who was only fifteen or sixteen years old. She heard the commotion and crying outside, was terrified, and lay under the quilt trembling. The bandit pulled the quilt, causing her to fall, and saw her beautiful appearance. He forcibly pushed her onto the bed and violated her. The other bandits gathered in the outer room with the stolen goods but did not see the bandit leader. Huang Bazi went back to search and found the bandit leader with the girl, lying on the bed. Huang Bazi stamped his foot and said, "Ah! You are doing such an unjust thing, you will surely be killed, and we have been misled by you!" The bandit leader got up and laughed, saying, "A good flower not picked, what is the point of living in the world? Do not blame each other."

    我让汝一乐何如？」八子曰：「汝不记吾党规条乎？采花必败，天道昭彰，我将去汝不暇，尤而效之，非人也。」遂出告诸盗，辞别欲散。盗魁留之，不听，与之物，不取，脱然长往。至海昌，投县，自首丝肆被窃案。此案实非八子所窃，因与是夜同时，冒之以就轻也。羁禁日久，因无原赃，不能结。时有刑书某，以办漕亏欠收禁，八子深与结纳，问得若干银，可仍回刑房？书以四百金告，八子曰：「是不难，我为先生完此事。」书悦曰：「果能如是，我必有以报。」因此交更密。书家送饭食，恒与八子共之。一日晚膳，食炖羊腿，八子甘甚，问系自置乎？书曰：「买诸市肆。」八子曰：「何处有？」书曰：「熟食铺皆有。

    Explanation

    100

    How about I let you have some fun?" Ba Zi said, "Don't you remember the rules of our group? Picking flowers will inevitably lead to failure, for the way of heaven is clear and evident. I will not even have time to leave you, yet to imitate such behavior is not human." He then went out to inform the bandits, bidding farewell and intending to disperse. The bandit leader tried to keep him, but he did not listen, and when offered goods, he refused to take them. He departed resolutely. He arrived in Haichang, went to the county office, and confessed to the theft case at the silk shop. The case was actually not stolen by Ba Zi, but because it occurred on the same night, he claimed responsibility to receive a lighter punishment. After being detained for a long time, the case could not be resolved due to the absence of the original stolen goods. At that time, there was a certain clerk of the criminal department who was detained for failing to meet the grain transport quota. Ba Zi deeply befriended him and asked how much silver he needed to return to the criminal department. The clerk said he needed four hundred taels of silver. Ba Zi said, "That is not difficult, I will complete this matter for you." The clerk said, "If you can do that, I will certainly reward you." As a result, their relationship became even closer. The clerk's family sent food, which Ba Zi often shared with him. One evening, they had a late meal, and Ba Zi found the stewed lamb leg very delicious. He asked if it was made by the clerk. The clerk said, "It was bought from a market stall." Ba Zi said, "Where can I get one?" The clerk said, "All the cooked food shops have them."

    101

    」八子骤欲饱啖，书曰：「门已封矣，明日嘱家人多备可也。」八子不能俟，取钱出院，但闻锁镣脱落声，禁子出视，只有刑具，而八子不知所矣。书嘱禁卒勿张皇，此人去必来，决无他虑也。未几，仍锁镣而入，肩羊腿，笑曰：「幸不辱命。」共切食之。书曰：「君去来何其神速？」八子曰：「我今与先生交深，敢以实告。我因盗党采花必败，避重就轻，故认此案，惟原赃难得。先生出后，可托事主，不必深究，见赃即领，我事毕矣。不然，脱禁而去，亦有何难？所不肯为者，避前事耳。

    Explanation

    101

    The eight-man suddenly wanted to eat heartily. The scholar said, "The gate is already closed, please prepare more food tomorrow." The eight-man could not wait and took money to leave the prison, but he only heard the sound of the shackles falling off. The guard came out to look, and there were only the instruments of punishment, but the eight-man was nowhere to be found. The scholar instructed the prison guard not to panic, saying that this person would surely return, and there was no need to worry. Soon after, the eight-man returned with the shackles still on, carrying a lamb leg and smiling, "I did not disgrace my mission." They shared the meal together. The scholar said, "How quickly you came and went?" The eight-man replied, "Now that I have become close to you, I dare to tell you the truth. I took responsibility for this case because the thieves' plot to steal flowers will surely fail, and I chose to avoid the heavy and take the light. The original stolen goods are difficult to find. After you leave, you can entrust the matter to the owner, and there is no need to investigate deeply; take the goods immediately, and my task will be complete. Otherwise, escaping from prison is not difficult. What I did not do was to avoid previous matters."

    况我日在禁中，夜则游行自在，同盗多人，皆不及知。今已与先生言明，夜将往取财帛，以了先生事。」因复潜出，伏巨室屋上，系库书某家，方夜宴，为出脱一重囚，纳贿千金。八子俟夜深人静，窃取而回。次日，以四百金交书，完亏释放。值是案破，缘被奸之女羞忿自缢，事主上控，上峰奏参，奉旨严拿，盗魁与十六人全获，无一漏网者。供及黄八子，行文到县。刑书以八子是月日夜方在此行窃丝肆，岂能远往三百里外从盗乎？其为仇攀可知。启令移覆，彼处亦不深究。书为关说事主，以物之相似者，充原物领认，八子之案遂定，以其自首减等，城旦而已。

    Explanation

    102

    As for me, who am always in the palace, at night I roam freely, with many accomplices, none of whom were aware. Now I have explained everything to you, and tonight I will go to take the wealth, to settle your matter. Then I slipped out again and hid on the roof of a large house. The household of a certain official, who was holding a night banquet, accepted a bribe of a thousand gold to release a serious prisoner. The eight men waited until late at night, when it was quiet, and stole the money back. The next day, they handed over four hundred gold to the official, and the prisoner was released. When the case was uncovered, the woman who was defiled, out of shame and anger, hanged herself; the victim reported the matter to the authorities, who then reported to the higher-ups, and the emperor issued an edict for a thorough investigation; the ringleader and sixteen others were all captured, not one escaped. The confession mentioned Huang Baizi, and a document was sent to the county. The county magistrate argued that Huang Baizi was in the city that night, robbing a silk shop, so how could he have gone three hundred miles away to join in the theft? It is clear that this is a case of someone seeking revenge and falsely accusing him. The magistrate ordered a re-examination, and the other place did not investigate deeply. The official persuaded the victim to accept similar items as the original stolen goods, and Huang Baizi's case was settled; because he confessed, his punishment was reduced to a lesser form of penal servitude.

    103

    芗厈曰：好好色，人情之常，贤者不免。八子盗也，乃能力拒此关，非有大魄力不能。故其艺亦甚精，惜乎无有能荐之者，若得其人为将，国家何忧外侮哉？

    　　悟知子
    　　悟知子，不知何许人。初业儒，不得功名，弃而学贾，不得财帛，偃蹇半生，一无成就，幸无妻子，孑然游荡。遇江湖卜者，学推算五行法，昕宵研精，寒暑不辍者三年，恍然大悟曰：「道在是矣。」随立肆于市，垂帘卖卜。诣之者，所决事皆当，故得钱无虚日。正为人作卦，左右环观，猝有一道人来，着折角巾，褦襶不堪。坐椅上，椅顿折，人皆笑之。道人抱歉将行，悟知子婉留之。

    Xiang Yan said: To appreciate beauty is a common human emotion, even the virtuous cannot escape it. Eight Subs, though thieves, were able to resist this temptation, which is not possible without great willpower. Therefore, his art is also very refined, but unfortunately, there is no one who can recommend him. If such a person were to become a general, the country would have no worries about foreign invasions.

    　　悟知子
    　　悟知子，不知何许人。初业儒，不得功名，弃而学贾，不得财帛，偃蹇半生，一无成就，幸无妻子，孑然游荡。遇江湖卜者，学推算五行法，昕宵研精，寒暑不辍者三年，恍然大悟曰：「道在是矣。」随立肆于市，垂帘卖卜。诣之者，所决事皆当，故得钱无虚日。正为人作卦，左右环观，猝有一道人来，着折角巾，褦襶不堪。坐椅上，椅顿折，人皆笑之。道人抱歉将行，悟知子婉留之。

    Wuzhi Zi
    Wuzhi Zi, of unknown origin. Originally studying Confucianism, he did not achieve fame or success, and gave up to become a merchant, but did not gain wealth. He lived a difficult life for half of his life, achieving nothing, fortunately without a wife or children, wandering alone. He met a fortune-teller from the countryside, learned the method of divination based on the Five Elements, studied day and night with great effort, persisting through cold and heat for three years, and suddenly had a great realization, saying, "The truth is here." Then he set up a stall in the market, selling divination services behind a curtain. Those who came to consult him, all the decisions made were correct, so he earned money without a day of emptiness. While making a divination for someone, surrounded by onlookers, suddenly a Taoist came, wearing a broken-cornered cap, tattered and unable to bear it. Sitting on a chair, which suddenly broke, everyone laughed at him. The Taoist apologized and was about to leave, but Wuzhi Zi gently persuaded him to stay.

    104

    卜完人散，悟知子诣道人膝前，跪称仙师求教，那道人曰：「予游方之士耳，何所见而仙予？」悟知子曰：「弟子早推定数，请观坐坏之椅背。」道人观之，上书「某年月日，此椅为仙人坐折」。道人曰：「孺子可教哉！惜费聪明于无益之地。子既仙我，盍言尔志？」曰：「求赐仙丹，度脱尘凡，相随门下。」道人笑曰：「子犹俗见，误甚。子先业儒，曾作文投明师。道家丹药，犹儒家笔墨，子能吞墨举笔，即成名家乎？」曰：「不能。」「能使师入尔心腹，代为著作乎？」曰：「不能。」「能求师一日，间诲汝作通人乎？」曰：「不能。」「我知汝不能也。仙道犹儒道，须专心致志，历阶而进，断无饵一粒丹，即飞升天上者，皆好事者托词以误世也。

    Explanation

    104

    After divination, people dispersed, and the student approached the Daoist master, kneeling before him and calling him a sage, seeking instruction. The master said, "I am just a wandering scholar. What have you seen that makes you call me a sage?" The student replied, "I have long divined my destiny. Please look at the worn chair back." The master examined it and saw an inscription: "On a certain day and month, this chair was broken by a sage." The master said, "This child is teachable indeed! It is a pity to waste intelligence on something unproductive. Since you see me as a sage, why don't you tell me your aspirations?" The student said, "I seek the elixir of immortality, to transcend the mundane world, and to follow you as a disciple." The master laughed and said, "You still hold a common view, which is a great mistake. You once studied Confucianism, wrote essays, and sought guidance from a master. Daoist elixirs are like Confucian writing and ink; can you swallow the ink and pick up the brush to become a renowned scholar?" The student replied, "No." "Can you make the master enter your innermost thoughts and write for you?" The student replied, "No." "Can you ask the master for a day's instruction to help you become a learned person?" The student replied, "No." "I know you cannot. The Daoist path is like the Confucian path; it requires dedication and steady progress. There is no such thing as eating a single pill and immediately ascending to heaven; all such claims are fabricated by those who spread false doctrines to mislead the world."

    105

    子善悟，我先示子丹头。」乃从袖中出一轴展之，中间大书「诚」字，上书「真」字，下书「妄」字，右书「实」字，左书「幻」字，曰：「此即大丹原委，成始成终，尽在于是。」悟知子曰：「弟子愚昧，敬请详示。」道人曰：「上求其真，下劈其妄，右依即实，左依即幻。如为人之道，孝悌忠信，礼义廉耻，八者无愧，是即诚也。天岂有弃此八字之仙乎？故入道之始，曰真人，言真能克尽人道也。一有不然，即流于妄。纲常既不明，则人且不成，何有仙乎？能右此八字，敬慎勿失即实，实则德明，无物不明矣。故曰『至诚前知』。

    Explanation

    105

    You are wise and perceptive. I will first show you the key to the mystery. Then I took out an axis from my sleeve and unfolded it. In the center was written the character "sincerity," above it was written "truth," below it was written "falsehood," on the right was written "reality," and on the left was written "illusion." This is the essence of the great elixir, from beginning to end, all is contained here. The perceptive student said, "Your disciple is foolish and ignorant; please explain in detail." The Daoist said, "Seek truth from above, cut through falsehood from below, rely on the right side for reality, and rely on the left side for illusion. As for the way of being human, filial piety, fraternal respect, loyalty, and trustworthiness, propriety, righteousness, integrity, and shame, without shame or guilt in all eight aspects, this is sincerity. How could heaven abandon those who possess these eight virtues? Therefore, at the beginning of the path, one is called a true person, meaning that true people can fully fulfill the human way. If there is any deviation, it flows into falsehood. If the fundamental principles are not clear, then one cannot become a person, how can one become a sage? If one relies on these eight virtues, with reverence and caution, one will not lose reality. Reality leads to clarity of virtue, nothing remains obscure. Therefore, it is said, 'sincerity foresees the future.'"

    106

    左此八字即幻，幻则狂妄，荒诞不经矣。故曰『左道惑众』。子能一心守真实，去幻妄，诚在其中，自然入定，定则静，静则精气神三宝之先天自见，见而团聚之勿散，即是内丹。道在是矣。」悟知子曰：「师所云理学，常谈也。道尽于此乎？」道人曰：「儒释道三教同源，其流则分。儒在明明德，释在波罗密，道在清静头，彼圣佛，无不从此入门也。即如子之神卜，亦从庸流所论五行入手，能劈去浮游而存精实，非由一诚得之乎？大小一理，子何信其小者而略其大者乎？」悟知子曰：「唯。」即失道人所在。三年后，悟知子亦不知去向。

    Explanation

    106

    Left these eight characters are illusions. Illusions lead to arrogance and recklessness, and are absurd and illogical. Therefore, they are called "heretical teachings that mislead the masses." If you can wholeheartedly uphold truth and discard illusions, sincerity will be found within, and you will naturally enter a state of meditation. When meditating, calmness will follow, and when calm, the three treasures of essence, energy, and spirit will naturally manifest. When you see them, gather them and do not let them disperse—that is the essence of internal alchemy. The way is here. The student said, "The teacher's talk about Neo-Confucianism is commonplace. Is the way exhausted here?" The Daoist replied, "Confucianism, Buddhism, and Taoism have the same origin, but their streams diverge. Confucianism manifests virtue, Buddhism practices the six perfections, and Taoism seeks purity and tranquility. Sages and Buddhas all enter through this. Even your divine divination starts with the five elements as discussed by common people. By cutting away the superficial and retaining the essence, is this not achieved through sincerity? The same principle applies to both big and small. Why believe in the small while neglecting the big?" The student said, "Yes." Immediately, the Daoist was lost. Three years later, the student's whereabouts were also unknown.

    107

    芗厈曰：纯阳为仙，纯阴为鬼，人在阴阳之中，故可鬼可仙。惟刻求诚明，自有四通八达之日。任意荒怠，即中七情六欲之迷。道人所云，堂堂之阵，正正之旗也，明者自知。知而不行，行而不专，是自趋于鬼道也。 　

    第三卷

    　　严氏
    　　金阊张子，率妻严氏，在都市开张杂货肆，即在后胡衕作寓。其宅三上四厢，垣外客房三楹，寓内惟少妻幼子，雇一年轻嫠妇作伴而已。肆内一伙，年逾五旬，严作餐，其夫传食。伙悯主人之劳也，曰：「何不觅一仆，任其事乎？」张子首肯。其伙每早起，洒扫肆外，似已有人代为扫除洁净，留心察之，则一少年所为也。伙叩其意。少年曰：「我南人，落魄于此，日为人效奔走以餬口。夜寄庑下，君虽不知，我心不安，略效微劳。何足齿也？」伙悦其勤敏，荐与主人试用。其人不惜辛勤，不辞劳瘁，凡所作为，能先得主人意，内外皆爱怜之。但半载为仆，已暗与嫠妇通。

    Explanation

    107

    Xiang Yan said: Pure yang leads to immortality, pure yin leads to the realm of ghosts. Humans exist between these two extremes, and thus can become either ghost or immortal. Only through earnest pursuit of sincerity and clarity can one achieve a state of enlightenment and understanding. However, if one allows oneself to become idle and negligent, one will fall into the entanglements of the seven emotions and six desires. The teachings of the Daoist say that one should maintain a dignified and honorable stance, and those who are wise will naturally understand this. Knowing but not acting, or acting without dedication, leads one to the path of the ghost.

    Chapter Three

    Yan Shi

    In Jin Chang, there was a man named Zhang, who lived with his wife Yan in the bustling city. They operated a small shop selling various goods, and their residence was located in a quiet alley behind the shop. The house consisted of three main rooms and four side rooms, with three guest rooms outside the walls. Inside the residence, there was only the young wife and their child, along with a young widow hired to keep them company. The shop had a group of employees, all over fifty years old, with Yan preparing meals and her husband distributing them. The employees felt sorry for the owner's hard work and suggested, "Why don't you hire a servant to take care of these tasks?" Zhang agreed. Each morning, the employees would clean the area outside the shop, as if someone had already tidied it up. Upon closer observation, they realized it was a young man doing the work. The employees asked him about his intentions. The young man replied, "I am a southerner, and I have fallen on hard times here. I earn my living by doing odd jobs for others. At night, I stay in the shed, and even though you may not know about it, I feel uneasy in my heart. So, I try to do a little work to ease my conscience. It's nothing to boast about." The employees were pleased with his diligence and recommended him to the owner for trial. The young man was willing to work hard without complaint, and he always managed to anticipate the owner's needs. Both inside and outside the household, everyone loved and pitied him. However, after half a year of service, he had secretly become involved with the widow.

    108

    一日，张子置货赴通州，嘱其仆住客房，守门户，惟严氏带十二岁子，与嫠妇同室。漏三下，子已沉睡，二妇尚作女工，忽有叩房门者。嫠妇拉关，仆操刀入室，突拥严氏曰：「汝必与我为欢，否则杀之。」严氏急呼嫠妇护救，嫠笑曰：「一家人，无伤也。主人不在，姑试尝之。」严氏知其同谋，料难力敌，转嗔作喜，谓仆曰：「汝果有情耶？此室有孺子在，恐被目见，事必泄漏，不能永欢矣。汝先入西厢俟我何如？」皆笑曰：「真精细人也。」嫠先抱其衾枕而去，仆料其孤力难拒，亦携刀随往。严氏乃去大衣，紧束其身，潜入西厢。仆起拥抱曰：「果来耶？且解我渴。

    Explanation

    108

    One day, Zhang Zi traveled to Tongzhou with his goods, instructing his servant to stay in the guest room and guard the door. Only Lady Yan, accompanied by her twelve-year-old son, was in the room with the widowed woman. At the third strike of the night bell, the boy had already fallen asleep, while the two women were still engaged in needlework. Suddenly, someone knocked on the door. The widowed woman pulled the door shut, and the servant entered the room with a knife, suddenly seizing Lady Yan and saying, "You must have sexual relations with me, otherwise I will kill you." Lady Yan urgently called out for the widowed woman to protect and save her, and the widowed woman laughed and said, "We are family, no harm will come. The master is not here, let's try it." Lady Yan knew they were conspiring and realized she couldn't fight back, so she changed from anger to joy, and told the servant, "Do you really have feelings for me? There is a child in this room, if he sees us, the matter will surely be revealed, and we won't be able to enjoy it forever. How about you go to the western wing and wait for me?" Both of them laughed and said, "Truly a meticulous person." The widowed woman first took her bedding and left, and the servant thought she was alone and couldn't resist, so he also took his knife and followed. Lady Yan then took off her outer robe, tightly bound her body, and secretly entered the western wing. The servant got up and hugged her, saying, "Did you really come? Let's quench my thirst."

    」严氏笑却之曰：「我索爱汝精细，今何粗莽乃尔？此事也，我向不愿清醒相对，是以男子在家时，合有药酒，临时饮之，能坚战，男女交畅，不亦可乎？」嫠曰：「我亦知之，未得尝试，仰慕已久。」严氏曰：「今我三人同心，可尝试之。」乃指藏酒所，同嫠取一樽至，并携果食，共倾饮之，香美异常。严氏力劝二人尽量，且媚灌其仆，任其糊戏抚摩，若甚甘心者。仆乃大醉，自脱上下衣，仰卧炕上，呢呢语曰：「速来试我具。

    严氏笑着拒绝道：“我一向欣赏你的细心，今天为何如此粗鲁？这件事，我以前不希望清醒地面对，所以男子在家时，应该有药酒，临时饮用，可以增强体力，使男女交合更加畅快，不是吗？”嫠人说：“我也知道，但还没有机会尝试，已经仰慕很久了。”严氏说：“现在我们三人意见一致，可以尝试一下。”于是指着藏酒的地方，和嫠人一起取了一樽酒来，还带了一些水果和点心，一起倒酒喝，酒香美得异常。严氏极力劝二人多喝些，并且用甜言蜜语给仆人灌酒，任由他胡闹抚摸，好像非常乐意的样子。仆人于是大醉，自己脱掉了上下的衣服，仰面躺在炕上，轻声说道：“快来试试我的东西。”

    110

    乘此酒兴，切勿再延。」严氏遣嫠睡去曰：「事毕，易汝何如？」嫠妇含笑去。严闭门，索其刀，犹在身畔，乃举刀力砍。已破其腹，仆跃起，复劈其脑，仰跌炕上，手掷足扬而毙。嫠闻声，披衣叩门，笑曰：「汝等如是猛战，邻舍闻之，不泄漏机关耶？」呼仆开门：「我欲作壁上观也。」严乃反臂隐刀身后，潜拔其关，嫠扑入，瞥见炕上血尸，正欲声喊，严从脑后力劈之，颠扑炕上，亦毙。乃解弃血衣，携灯出，反锁其门，回房与子同卧。

    Explanation

    110

    Riding on this drunken mood, he urged, "Do not delay further." Yan sent the widow to sleep and said, "Once the matter is done, what if you were to replace her?" The widow smiled and left. Yan closed the door, searched for her knife, which was still by her side, and then picked it up to strike with all his might. He had already slashed her belly; she fell and sprang up, then he struck her head again. She fell backward onto the bed, dying with her hands flung and feet kicking. The widow heard the noise, put on her clothes, and knocked on the door, smiling and saying, "You two are fighting so fiercely, won't the neighbors hear and reveal the secret?" She shouted to the servant to open the door, "I want to watch from the sidelines." Yan turned his arm back to hide the knife behind him, secretly opened the lock. The widow rushed in, glancing at the bloody corpse on the bed, was about to shout, but Yan struck her from behind with all his might. She fell onto the bed and also died. He undressed and discarded the bloody clothes, carried a lamp out, locked the door from the outside, and returned to the room to lie down with his child.

    111

    次早，倩邻妇呼其伙来，告之曰：「昨夜仆与妇同逃，幸未窃物去，汝速遣人唤主人归，商其事，合报官否？」伙雇人唤张子回，询其事，严含糊答对。夜深人静，方以杀奸事白之，张子愕然。严曰：「君必首之，有罪妾任。若潜隐其事，日久必破，君亦不得辞其咎矣。」张子思其言，遂首诸司坊，官来验讯，严氏侃侃直陈，奏交秋部大司寇鞠之。严氏理直气壮，坚执不挠，乃释严氏夫妇而瘗二尸。案定后，乡人之宦游京师者，咸羡严之胆智，公悬额以旌之。

    Explanation

    111

    The next morning, she asked her neighbor woman to call her companions, and told them: "Last night, my husband and I fled together, fortunately we did not steal anything before leaving. You quickly send someone to call the owner back and discuss whether to report the matter to the authorities." The companions hired someone to call the owner, Zhang Zi, back. When questioned about the matter, the owner vaguely answered. Deep into the night when everyone was quiet, he only then told him about the act of killing the villain. The owner was startled. The wife said, "You must report it; if there is any guilt, I will take responsibility. If you conceal the matter, over time it will be exposed, and you also cannot escape blame." Zhang Zi thought about her words and decided to report the matter to the relevant authorities. Officials came to investigate and question, and the wife calmly stated straightforwardly. The case was submitted to the Ministry of Punishment for the highest judicial official to try. The wife was reasonably and confidently firm and unyielding, and then the couple was released and the two bodies were buried. After the case was settled, people from the village who served in official posts in the capital all admired the wife's courage and wisdom, and officially hung a plaque to honor her.

    112

    芗厈曰：智明者，胆必壮。严氏初心，亦犹恒人，未尝不呼嫠妇共拒。迨嫠妇同谋，知难免矣，乃速转关作荡妇态，诱其入我彀中。刀可得，仇可报也。然亦有天幸，若仆必欲先污之而后饮，我知仆之命，必不能脱其手。而严氏不得为完人，饮恨无穷矣。或曰：「必不被污也，仆视严氏犹几上肉，断不能脱我口，何妨姑且作乐？况以两情交畅之言动之，有不垂涎愿从者乎？从之，则必酩酊，二人皆自取杀身也。」我愿世之君子室无严氏，断不可使少妇壮仆在一处，即有严氏，多一事，不如少一事也。

    Explanation

    112

    Xiang Yan said: The wise and discerning are sure to be bold. Yan's original intention was also like that of an ordinary person, who has never failed to call out the widow to resist together. When the widow joins in the plot, knowing that escape is impossible, then quickly change tactics to act like a wanton woman, luring her into my trap. The knife can be obtained, and the enemy can be avenged. But there is also a stroke of luck; if you want to defile her first and then kill her, I know your life will not escape from my grasp. And Yan will not remain a virtuous person, harboring endless resentment. Someone might say: "She will certainly not be defiled. I regard Yan as meat on the table, cannot escape my mouth, why not take pleasure in the meantime? Especially when using words of mutual affection to move her, who would not be tempted and willing to follow? If she follows, she will surely become drunk, both will bring about their own deaths." I wish that gentlemen's households do not have women like Yan, definitely do not allow young women and strong servants to be together, even if there is a Yan, having fewer things is better than having more.

    潘善人
    　　潘翁，粤东香山人，谈者忘其名字，生在前明中叶，家赀千万，席丰履厚，有善必为，如刷印经文、创修庙宇、造桥铺路、掩骼埋胔，以及赠亲朋、济邻里，犹不足以尽其心。乃日食千百人，不使邑有乞丐，当博施济众时，有媪旦暮必至，索食饭之，索饮茗之，无倦色，如是者久，无如旱涝之年，闻善人之名者，远近就哺，日以万计。翁虽富，力渐不支，然不肯中止，犹去质库，卖田宅为之。迨时和年丰，灾黎散而善人贫矣，前媪尚日诣之。翁犹自减口粮以为之食，始终不怠。媪不自安，谓翁曰：「我孤独无归之嫠也，今汝业已败，我何忍累汝？曷以住宅施我作大士阁，我愿为优婆夷，自主香火，藉以常得温饱，无求于汝矣。」人旨怒叱之，翁曰：「诺。」即谋迁妻孥，举宅以施。媪曰：「汝舍去，将何所依？得无怨我乎？」翁曰：「否。

    Explanation

    113

    Pan the Good Man
    　　Pan翁, a native of Xiangshan in eastern Guangdong, is so well-known for his good deeds that people forget his name. He lived during the middle period of the Ming Dynasty and was a man of immense wealth, with a fortune of millions. Despite his prosperity, he always performed good deeds, such as printing scriptures, building temples, constructing bridges and roads, and burying the bones of the dead. He also gave gifts to relatives and friends and helped his neighbors, but these acts were still not enough to fully express his benevolence. He fed thousands of people daily, ensuring that there were no beggars in the town. During times of great need, when he was distributing food to the masses, an old woman would come every morning and evening, asking for food and drink, and Pan翁 would provide them without showing any sign of fatigue. This situation continued for a long time, even though it was not during the years of natural disasters. People from far and near came to seek food because they knew of Pan翁's good deeds.

    Despite his wealth, Pan翁 gradually became unable to support the needs of so many people. However, he did not stop. He pawned things and sold his land and houses to continue helping others. Eventually, when there was a good harvest and favorable conditions, the disaster-stricken people dispersed, and Pan翁 became poor. The old woman still came to see him daily, and Pan翁 continued to reduce his own food to give her food, never slackening off.

    The old woman felt uneasy and said to Pan翁, "I am a lonely widow with no place to return. Now your business is already ruined. How can I bear to burden you? How about giving me your house to build a Bodhisattva pavilion? I wish to be a laywoman, manage the incense and fire, and thus always have enough to eat and drink, without asking anything from you."

    Pan翁 agreed and immediately began planning to move his wife and children, and he gave his entire house to her. The old woman asked, "If you leave, where will you go? Will you not resent me?" Pan翁 replied, "No."

    114

    北郭外有山地数顷，因历年旱涝，寸草不生，无人肯售，去结茅庐亦足栖止，何怨之有？」媪曰：「此地吾前见之，有大风水在，汝因历年为善，未及葬汝父母，今既已迁此，我当为卜宅。其山之阳，枯木之下，天生石穴一区，直佳城也，窀穸于此，不但旧业可复，将亿万斯年，吃着不尽。汝信之乎？」翁曰：「谨受救。」媪执引送之，指牛眠穴，坎山离向，以罗浮为案，以大海为荫，曰：「此凡夫之所见不及者也，且使庐墓而居。

    Explanation

    114

    Outside the northern outskirts, there are a few acres of mountainous land, which, due to years of drought and flooding, has not a blade of grass growing, and no one is willing to sell it. If you build a thatched hut there, it is sufficient for habitation, so what is there to complain about? The old woman said, "This place I have seen before; it has great feng shui. You have been virtuous over the years, but you have not yet buried your parents. Now that you have moved here, I will predict the auspiciousness of this place. On the sunny side of the mountain, under a dead tree, there is a naturally formed stone cave, which is a good place for a tomb. Burying your parents here will not only restore your old business but also ensure that you have more than enough to eat and live on for countless years. Do you believe this?" The man replied, "I will follow your advice." The old woman led him there, pointing out the cow's resting place, with the tomb facing south and the back to the north, using the Lufu Mountains as a screen and the sea as a shelter. She said, "This is something that ordinary people cannot see, and you can live in a thatched hut near the tomb."

    」乃出异果数斗，给之曰：「以此遍撒荒田，俟其生长勿伐，三年乃成，三年后，必有蛇虺守此，汝当别迁。欲得此异物者，惟五月五日，可使健男子，身涂雄黄，醉饱来伐取，行将独擅天下之妙业矣。」翁曰：「将为何物？必先教之。」媪笑曰：「汝将来观其形状，似何物即创为何物，何必先知？但我所与者，菩提果也，勿以予人。纵予人，无益。」媪乃去。翁于是安庐种果，半载方休。入城视己旧居，已成观音堂，香火甚盛，有尼住持，媪已不知去向矣。

    Explanation

    115

    The old woman then produced several baskets of strange fruit and gave them to the old man, saying, "Use this to scatter over barren fields, wait for it to grow without cutting it down, and it will take three years to mature. After three years, there will definitely be snakes and venomous snakes guarding this place, so you should move away. If you want to obtain this strange thing, only on the fifth day of the fifth month, you can have a strong man cover his body with realgar, come drunk and full to cut it down, and you will then uniquely possess the wonderful art of the world." The old man asked, "What will it be? You must first teach me." The old woman smiled and said, "You will see its shape later, and whatever it resembles, you should create accordingly. Why must you know it beforehand? But what I give you is the Bodhi fruit. Do not give it to others. Even if you give it to others, it will be of no benefit." The old woman then left. The old man settled down to live in a hut and cultivate the fruit, and after half a year, he stopped. He went into the city to see his old residence, and it had already become a Guanyin hall. The incense and fire were very prosperous, and there was a nun in charge. The old woman was no longer known where she went.

    116

    翁归不数月，其物萌茁，形似芭蕉，遍山皆是。爱护之，勿敢伐。历三年，叶形成扇，翁乃剥其粗者，贱售之。人皆争市，一夏得数万钱。时已有巨蛇出没，毒气射人，翁不能存身，仍迁城市。次年，如媪嘱，以重价雇壮丁，于五月一日始，人各执斧持钻，腰带雄黄酒，绳索入山，砍其细者，捆载而出。五日毕事，拣其细心完善者，以玳瑁象牙作柄，绵绣其边，一柄值银数钱。商贩之徒，争来售置，其门如市，后遂广行宇内，自贵官长者、文人墨士及闺阃中，几至人执一柄，以为雅玩。以是复业，传至子孙，至今三百余年。家益富，他人欲窃效之，俱不能，盖蕉为虺蛇所守，平日入山者，受毒即毙，故无敢窃。亲友乞其种，亦未尝吝惜，但树他处，变为美人蕉，结花娇红可爱，叶小而脆，不堪作扇，然后知媪即观自在菩萨，传翁绝业，为天下后世为善者示劝。

    Explanation

    116

    After a few months, the plant began to sprout and grow vigorously, taking on the shape of a banana tree and spreading all over the mountain. The old man cherished and protected it, daring not to cut it down. Over three years, the leaves formed like fans. The old man then peeled the coarse ones and sold them cheaply. People all competed to buy them, and in one summer, he earned tens of thousands of coins. At that time, there were already large snakes appearing, emitting toxic gas that shot at people, making it impossible for the old man to stay there. He moved to the city. The next year, as instructed by the old woman, he hired strong men with high prices. Starting on the fifth day of the fifth month, each person held an axe and a drill, wore a belt of realgar wine, and carried ropes, entering the mountain to cut the finer ones, bundling and loading them out. They completed the task in five days, selecting the fine and complete ones, using tortoise shell and ivory for handles, and embroidering the edges. Each one was worth several silver coins. Merchants and traders competed to sell and place them, and his door was like a market. Later, it spread widely throughout the land, from high officials, elders, literati, and women in the inner chambers, almost everyone held one, considering it a refined plaything. Thus, he resumed his business, passing it down to his descendants, until now for more than three hundred years. His family became even wealthier, and others tried to secretly imitate him, but none succeeded, because the banana was guarded by venomous snakes. Those who entered the mountain on a regular basis, if poisoned, would die, so no one dared to steal. Relatives and friends asked for its seeds, and he never hesitated to give them, but when planted elsewhere, it turned into a beauty banana, with beautiful red flowers that were lovely, but the leaves were small and brittle, unsuitable for making fans. Then it was known that the old woman was Guanyin Bodhisattva, transmitting the old man's unique business, showing encouragement to those who do good in the world.

    117

    芗厈曰：天之报施善人也，大善则大报之，小善则小报之。如潘翁之博施济众，直欲掠美唐虞，天乃报以万年不拔之基，以是知生物不测，造化无穷。

    　　身毒国
    　　无无子者，不知何许人，亦不详其姓氏。其为人也，愤世嫉俗，好作汗漫游。一日，附洋船随风飘至一国，见其人凹目深鼻，皆衣白，熙熙浩浩，无争竞心。见中国客到，争饭之。米大而香洁，无肉食，并无菜蔬。虽言语不通，而貌甚恭敬。走报一红衣老者来，自言曾出使中华数次，能华言，邀无无子至家曰：「先生欲知我国风土人情乎？请译而道之。我国分男女两部，王曰元首，男部统之。其下十二司，分三等。上司三，曰耳目司、口鼻司、喉舌司。中司四，曰左肱司、右肱司、心腹司、臂指司。下司五：曰前阳司、后阴司、左股司、右股司、皮毛司。

    Explanation

    117

    Xiang Yan said: Heaven rewards good people according to their virtue—great virtue is rewarded greatly, small virtue is rewarded small. For example, Pan翁's extensive acts of kindness and assistance to the masses, which could be seen as taking credit for the achievements of Tang and Yu, were rewarded by Heaven with a foundation that would last for ten thousand years and cannot be uprooted. Thus, we understand that the power of life is unfathomable, and creation is endless.

    In the country of Shendu,
    There was a man named Wuwu, whose origin and surname are unknown. He was a person who was angry at the world and disgusted with convention, and enjoyed aimless wandering. One day, he boarded a foreign ship and was carried by the wind to a country. He saw the people there with sunken eyes and deep noses, all dressed in white, bustling and lively, without any competitive spirit. When they saw a Chinese guest, they competed to feed him. The rice was large, fragrant, and clean, with no meat or vegetables. Although the language was not understood, their appearance was very respectful. A messenger ran to report that an elderly man in red clothes had come, who said he had been on diplomatic missions to China several times and could speak Chinese. He invited Wuwu to his home and said, "Sir, do you want to know about the customs and people of our country? Please allow me to translate and explain. Our country is divided into male and female departments. The king is the head of state, and the male department is in charge. Under it, there are twelve departments, divided into three levels. The upper-level departments are three: the departments of ears and eyes, mouth and nose, and throat and tongue. The middle-level departments are four: the departments of left arm, right arm, heart and abdomen, and arms and fingers. The lower-level departments are five: the departments of front yang, back yin, left thigh, right thigh, and skin and hair.

    118

    十二司戴元首，合而为身毒国，毒译督，言一司总督诸司也。耳目口鼻喉舌最贵，比中华之宰相尚书卿贰，左右肱比都督将军，心腹比抚按，臂指比提镇。前阳主刑名，后阴主钱谷，比中华之有司。左右股比汛弁，皮毛司比佐贰杂职。自王以下，皆布衣，以色分品级。王衣（黄炎），上司衣朱，中司衣蓝，下司衣青，民衣白。田地无主，亦无旷土，产香谷，大于中华之稻米，一岁三收。至春夏秋三时，人之有力者，不拘何地，尽量布种。自王以下，并耕而食，无分彼此。诸司督耕，能多得谷者，司举奏王，以下司爵之，有递迁至朱衣者。第非考较出身，仅虚职荣之耳。怠情者，发穷黎岛，日给一粥终其身。

    Explanation

    118

    In the state of Shendu, twelve departments support the head, forming a unified nation. "Shendu" is a play on words, where "毒" (du) is a pun for "督" (du), meaning "supervise," and "言一司总督诸司也" (yan yi si zong du zhu si ye) means "it is said that one department supervises all other departments." The most important roles are represented by the eyes, ears, mouth, nose, throat, and tongue, which are compared to the high-ranking officials of the Chinese government: the prime minister, ministers, and vice-ministers. The left and right arms are compared to military leaders or generals, the heart and belly to trusted advisors or ministers, and the arms and fingers to local governors or commanders. The front yang is responsible for legal matters, and the rear yin handles financial affairs, similar to the divisions in the Chinese government. The left and right thighs represent lower-ranking military officers, and the skin and hair departments represent minor or auxiliary positions. From the king down, everyone wears simple clothing, with colors distinguishing ranks: the king wears yellow and red, higher-ranking officials wear red, middle-ranking officials wear blue, lower-ranking officials wear green, and common people wear white. There is no idle land, and the land is well-managed, producing fragrant grain that is more abundant than Chinese rice, with three harvests per year. During the spring, summer, and autumn seasons, people with strength, regardless of location, plant as much as possible. From the king down, everyone works the land and eats together, without distinction. The departments supervise farming, and those who can produce more grain are reported to the king, and some may be promoted to a lower rank, with some even being promoted to red rank. However, these promotions are not based on examination results but are honorary positions. Lazy people are sent to the poor island, given one bowl of porridge per day for life.

    119

    年丰，则家藏一岁之用，余尽归元首，分贮十二司。若歉年，十二司积储，仍散于民，故无饥馑，亦无贫富。上下皆食谷，不知有菜，何来荤腥？虽产有金银珠玉宝贝，不足贵也，不过为布地饰屋之需，犹中华之砖瓦朱粉。所贵者米布，如中华之银钱，凡动用之物，皆以此交易。我王相传，为净饭王分枝，八十四世裔孙，其长枝，即阿弥陀佛，代传一那摩佛，即中华所称喇嘛大班禅活佛也，能参四禅八定。诸司选民之后，俊秀者，送入学道，或三四年，或五六年，由那摩佛，考较道行之浅深，送王补诸司缺，故皆慈祥，为国为民。后曰元后，女官统之，凡女皆习工作。

    Explanation

    119

    In years of abundance, households store enough food for one year, and any surplus is returned to the ruler and distributed among the twelve departments. In years of scarcity, the stored reserves of the twelve departments are still distributed to the people, so there is no famine, nor are there poor and rich. Both the upper and lower classes eat grain, and they do not know of vegetables, so how can there be meat and fish? Even if there is production of gold, silver, jewels, and precious stones, they are not considered valuable, as they are only needed for covering the ground and decorating houses, like bricks, tiles, and red powder in China. What is valued is rice and cloth, like silver coins in China, and all movable goods are traded using these. Our king, traditionally, is a branch of King Suddhodana, the 84th generation descendant. The eldest branch is Amitabha Buddha, and the next generation is a Namo Buddha, which is the Dalai Lama, the great living Buddha in China, able to participate in the four stages of meditation and eight attainments. After the selection of people by the various departments, the talented and handsome ones are sent to study the Way, for three to four years, or five to six years, by the Namo Buddha, who examines the depth of their spiritual practice, and they are sent to the king to fill vacancies in the various departments, so they are all kind and compassionate, for the country and the people. The queen is called the Yuan Hou, and female officials oversee her, and all women learn to work.

    120

    自后以下，俱能种棉织布，成衣以易谷食。凡男年二十以上思妻者，投前阳司送女部，后配与年相若者一人，三宿而去。若再过之，则又另配人矣。生女则留，生子，抚养至五六岁时，发男部，任人予之，只许人领一子。有夭殇者，许再，故民无氏族，亦无绝后之人。凡男女年至六十，不耕织，所颁女子，力作养之，亦无违弃者。死则公殓以大瓮，亦无棺椁。邻邦皆尚繁华，以我国为鄙陋，故无侵犯，我国只求内治，亦不征伐。故自净饭王以来，数千年不易姓，如是而已，无他长也。」无无子大悦曰：「此极乐世界，我愿受一廛而为氓。」老者笑曰：「我国法，不留外人。子回中华，卧而思之自得，何必留此？」乃怅伥而返。

    Explanation

    120

    From then on, everyone could plant cotton, weave cloth, make clothes to exchange for grain and food. Men over twenty who sought a wife had to approach a specific office to be matched with a woman of similar age for a trial period of three nights. If he returned again, then another person would be matched to him. Daughters were kept, but sons were raised until they were five or six years old, after which they were given to others, with the condition that only one son could be taken. If a child died, another could be taken, so there were no surnames, and no one was left without an heir. Men and women over sixty were no longer required to work and were supported by the community. When they died, they were publicly buried in large jars, without coffins. Neighboring countries all valued luxury, considering our country crude, so they did not invade us; our country only sought internal governance and did not engage in warfare. Thus, since King Purnamasa, for thousands of years, the surname had not changed, and that was all; there was nothing else remarkable. The person without a son was very pleased and said, "This is a paradise, I wish to accept a small plot of land and become a commoner." The old man laughed and said, "Our country's law does not allow outsiders to stay. You return to China, lie down and think about it yourself, why should you stay here?" So he left sadly.

    121

    芗厈曰：身毒国十司皆妥，惟前阳、后阴二司尚可议。以前阳能刚能柔，能进能退，故主刑名耶？然少者浮躁，老者疲软，奈何？至后阴只出不入，何可司钱谷耶？或曰：「后世之能者，出糟粕而纳精华，君其未知之耶？」予笑应曰：「唯。」

    　　某制军夫人

    Explanation

    121

    The wife of a certain military governor said: "All ten departments of Shendu are in order, except for the front yang and rear yin departments, which are still open to discussion. The front yang department is flexible, able to be both firm and gentle, advancing and retreating as needed, so it is in charge of penal law. However, the younger members are restless, and the older members are weak. What should be done? As for the rear yin department, it only has outflow and no inflow. How can it manage finances and grain? Someone said, 'Those who are capable in later generations can discard the dross and take in the essence. Do you not know this?' I smiled and replied, 'Yes.'"

    122

    某制军由科甲出身，好士爱才，门下皆一时誉髦也。制军风雅甚，如夫人甚众，琴棋诗画，各擅一长。咸使名士传之。有某孝廉者，年逾弱冠，品貌俊逸，诗如其人。家屡空，投制军谋食。时制军新得宠姬某氏，诗笔清新，与孝廉相类，遂使姬作女学生。传递诗词，两情甚洽，有文君之约，而未得其便。值制军寿诞，内外优剧，百戏并作，乃乘喧杂时，姬偕孝廉卷其细软，逾花圃后垣同逸。次日，仆妇书童，报二人夜不归室之事，制军大怒，传心腹武弁入内室，授之剑而谕之故曰：「迅往南追，取二人首。认姬作汝妻，被孝廉奸拐，故追而斩之。投所在官司自首，汝既无罪，且不次超迁汝职。」弁领命将行，夫人遽出喝止。乃谏制军曰：「机事不密，则害成。此等事，想已扬播省垣矣。引盗入室，斩之非义。一顶绿头巾，终脱不去，徒然掩耳盗铃，不贻笑士林耶？且孝廉才名甚着，爱之者不仅夫君一人。使士林抱不平，察实而发其覆，贻害无穷矣。

    Explanation

    122

    A certain military governor, having risen through the imperial examinations, loved scholars and valued talent, and his followers were all the most distinguished of their generation. The military governor was very refined and cultured, and he had many concubines, each excelling in one of the four arts: music, chess, poetry, and painting. All had had famous scholars write about them. There was a scholar-official named Mr. X who, over twenty years old, was handsome and elegant in appearance, and his poetry reflected his character. His family was often in poverty, so he sought sustenance by approaching the military governor for employment. At the time, the military governor had recently acquired a favored concubine, whose poetry was fresh and clear, similar to that of the scholar-official. He then had the concubine pretend to be a female student, and they exchanged poems, their feelings being very harmonious. They had a secret agreement like that of Sima Xiangru and Zhuo Wenjun, but did not find the opportunity to act on it. On the occasion of the military governor's birthday, there were performances inside and outside, with all kinds of entertainments going on. They took advantage of the noisy and chaotic time, and the concubine and the scholar-official packed their belongings and escaped over the wall of the flower garden together. The next day, the servants and the scribe reported that the two did not return to their rooms at night, and the military governor became very angry. He summoned a trusted military officer into his inner chamber, gave him a sword, and explained the reason, saying, "Go south quickly to catch them and bring back their heads. Pretend that the concubine is your wife and that she was abducted by the scholar-official, so you can chase and kill him. Surrender to the local authorities, and you will be free of blame and promoted to a higher position." The military officer was about to leave, but the lady of the house suddenly came out and shouted to stop him. She then advised the military governor, saying, "If secret matters are not kept confidential, they will cause harm. Such matters must have already spread throughout the provincial capital. Inviting a thief into your home and killing him is unjust. Wearing a green headband (a symbol of infidelity) will never be shaken off, it's just like plugging one's ears while stealing a bell, and it will make you a laughingstock among scholars. And the scholar-official is very talented and well-known, loved by many besides the military governor. If scholars feel unjustly treated, they will investigate and expose the truth, causing endless harm."

    123

    夫君聪明阔达，岂不见及此？妾恐一时忿怒昧之耳。」制军不觉怒息，曰：「为之奈何？」夫人曰：「是不难，昔杨越、裴晋二公，皆人杰也。盗其侍妾者，不但不追，间有厚赠者。曷不仿而为之？请作札，遣家人赠以行资，则孝廉有不感愧图报者乎？且以美姬赠名士，古人恒为之。不但士林不笑，且宽大之誉，遍环区矣。孰得孰失，君试思之。」制军大悦曰：「非夫人之论，我几大误。

    Explanation

    123

    My lord, you are wise and broad-minded, yet how can you not see this? I fear that in your moment of anger, you have lost sight of it. The general unconsciously calmed down and said, "What should we do about it?" The lady replied, "It is not difficult. In the past, Yang Yue and Pei Jin were both outstanding individuals. Those who stole their concubines not only did not pursue them, but sometimes even gave them gifts. Why not follow their example? Please write a letter and send the family to give them travel expenses. How could the scholar-official not feel ashamed and seek to repay you? Moreover, giving a beautiful concubine to a famous scholar was something the ancients often did. Not only would the scholarly community not laugh, but you would also be praised for your magnanimity throughout the region. Who gains and who loses? Please consider it carefully." The general was greatly pleased and said, "Without my wife's advice, I would have made a great mistake."

    124

    」即作书以四百金，遣奴子追赠，其书略曰：「仆年逾花甲，所以室有少女者，非自好也。诚以聪明俊秀之产，造物亦几费经营，使之误配莽夫，殊深惋惜，是以罗而致之，且随其姿质，教成学术，以配君子，岂非天下大快事耶？故某女遣随足下，仆早有作合之心。所不预言者，缘此女学未大成，欲其精进而后成之。不意巫山神女，竞自投楚王矣。其识见亦属非凡。仆当顺其情，以遂好逑佳话。但不别而行，妙手空空，腰缠何藉？未免累及君子。故遣仆走馈赆，伏冀哂存。所有足下行囊，与某女衣饰，俱捡点附上。」

    Explanation

    124

    I immediately wrote a letter and sent it with a gift of four hundred gold pieces, dispatching a servant to catch up and deliver it. The letter reads as follows:

    "I am over sixty years old, and the reason I have a young daughter is not because I am fond of it. Indeed, the creation of intelligent and handsome offspring also requires considerable effort, and if they were to be paired with a coarse man, it would be deeply regrettable. Therefore, I gathered them together, and according to their talents, I taught them scholarly pursuits, to match them with a gentleman. Isn't this a great joy in the world? Thus, this girl is sent to accompany you; I had long intended for this match. What I did not predict was that this girl's learning was not yet complete, and I wanted her to refine her studies and then complete them. Unintentionally, the goddess of Wuchang fell into the arms of King Chu. Her insight is also extraordinary. I will follow her feelings to fulfill this good match. But without saying goodbye, with empty hands, how can one rely on the money in the belt? It cannot help but burden the gentleman. Therefore, I sent a servant to deliver a gift, hoping you will accept it with a smile. All your belongings and the girl's clothes have been carefully checked and attached."

    125

    二人得书，惭愧悲感，望东叩首，对曰：「夫子之德，竟是二天。当作犬马图报。」再拜作禀申意，其词曰：「忆自亥子春秋，获游夫子门下。已渝妾奏，得近云门；葑菲下材，顿亲琪树。乃康成雅度，欲听慧婢之诗；而小子何知，俾作丽娘之傅。于是银蝉入户，共赓隔巷之清歌；红杏出墙，愿借邻家以艳色。以致宓妃留枕，非关韩豫偷香。携手星奔，抱衾露宿，方虞飞洞宾之剑，何期添裴晋之装。夫子休休有容，勤勤乐育，使狗偷鼠窃，不作青磷；成凤侣鸾俦，同偕白首。且惠以赆仪四百，行李增光；从此弱水三千，片帆稳渡。感周旋之仔细，益愧寸衷；期报答以辛勤，难酬尺泽。惟思砺顽钝之器，庶不贻冰鉴之羞。千载遭逢，万言莫罄。敢因臂指，敬布腹心」云云，后孝廉捷南宫，由词林入谏垣。有与制军为难者，多方营救之。与某姬偕老且多子云。

    Explanation

    125

    The two received the letter, feeling ashamed, sad, and moved. They faced east and knelt, saying, "The virtue of our master is truly as great as two heavens. We shall repay him like dogs and horses would to their master." They bowed twice and wrote a letter to express their feelings, which read: "Recalling the years of the Pig and Rat, we had the good fortune to study under your tutelage. Having been allowed to approach your teachings, we, lowly and unrefined, were suddenly treated with respect, like common vegetables near a rare jade tree. Your noble character, like that of Kang Cheng, wished to hear our poetry, though we are mere ignorant youths who have been entrusted with teaching Liang Nian. Thus, the silver cicada entered our home, and we sang together, like neighbors across the alley. The red apricot blossom, so beautiful, we wished to borrow its charm from the neighboring household. The goddess of the Luo River left her pillow, not because of the theft of fragrance by Han Yu. We held hands and ran like stars, sharing a blanket under the moon, fearing the flying sword of the fairy, but unexpectedly adorned with the magical garment of Pei Jin. Your noble and generous character, dedicated to education, protected us like a noble person, preventing us from becoming thieves and decay. We became loyal and devoted partners, sharing a lifetime. Moreover, you generously gave us 400 units of money to enhance our status; from now on, we will cross the vast sea with a single sail, steady and secure. We are deeply moved by your care and feel even more ashamed. We wish to repay your kindness with our efforts, but find it difficult to fully repay even a small part. We resolve to improve ourselves, so as not to bring shame to you. This encounter is a rare one in a thousand years, and our gratitude is beyond words. We dare to express our innermost thoughts with your guidance." Later, the jinshi passed the imperial examinations, moving from the imperial library to the office of censors. When there were difficulties with the high-ranking military official, he used various means to help them. He lived happily with a concubine and had many children.

    秦良玉遗事
    　　女帅秦良玉，石柱土司所属人也。生而警敏多机智，父母皆爱怜之，有兄莽夫也。良玉五六岁时，邻人被窃，多方构之不得，与其父咨嗟叹惜。良玉曰：「无事多求，此必米具所为也。」邻曰：「何以知之？」玉曰：「我本不识具，日者潜窥汝室。彼以我为幼，不之避。倏又一人来呼曰：『米具，汝何为耶？』具即与耳语而去，是夜被偷，非具而何？」缉之果得。及笄时，土俗皆自择夫。春秋之际，纵少男女于山野，唱歌求配。

    Explanation

    126

    The Deeds of Qin Liangyu

    Qin Liangyu, a female general, was from the Shizhu Tusi. She was born with a keen mind and was very intelligent and quick-witted. Her parents loved her dearly, and she had an older brother named Mangfu. When Qin Liangyu was five or six years old, a neighbor's property was stolen, and despite multiple investigations, the culprit could not be found. Her father and the neighbor were both sighing and lamenting over the situation. Qin Liangyu said, "Don't look for trouble unnecessarily; this must be the work of Mi Ju." The neighbor asked, "How do you know?" Qin Liangyu replied, "I don't know Mi Ju, but I saw someone secretly watching your house. He thought I was too young to notice him, so he didn't avoid me. Suddenly, another person came and called out, 'Mi Ju, what are you doing?' Mi Ju then whispered to him and left. That night, the theft occurred. Who else could it be but Mi Ju?" The investigation confirmed her suspicion.

    When Qin Liangyu was of marriageable age, it was a local custom for young women to choose their own husbands. During the Spring and Autumn period, young men and women would meet in the countryside to sing songs and find partners.

    127

    有马生者，土司宗族也，年及冠，无父母昆季，贫而好学，美秀而文。玉一见即携手同归，父母及兄皆贫之。玉曰：「事在人为，我只求同心者耳。贫不足道也。」谓生曰：「君得我不忧不富贵，我得君不忧不多闻。君所感者家贫，我所感者腹贫。家贫易为力，我请任之；腹贫须好学，君其为我助之。」生曰诺，相得甚欢。良玉恒执女工，伴读辄有所悟，忽谓生曰：「君所读之书，以治身心则有余，非我辈救时之策也。曷求富强之学，以成我愿。」生乃购借《韬钤武备》及《三农致富》等书数十种，闭户讲论。

    Explanation

    127

    There was a man named Ma Sheng, a member of the Tu official's clan. He was of the age of adulthood, without parents or siblings, poor but fond of learning, beautiful, refined, and cultured. Yu saw him and immediately took his hand and brought him home. His parents and elder brother all pitied him for his poverty. Yu said, "Success depends on human effort; I only seek those who share my heart. Poverty is not worth mentioning." He told Ma Sheng, "If you have me, you will not worry about not becoming wealthy and powerful; if I have you, I will not worry about not gaining much knowledge. What you feel is poverty at home, what I feel is poverty of the mind. Poverty at home is easier to overcome, I will take care of it; poverty of the mind requires good learning, you should help me with it." Ma Sheng said, "Yes," and they got along very well. Liang Yu always did women's work, accompanying him in his studies, she often had insights. Suddenly, she said to Ma Sheng, "The books you read are sufficient for cultivating the mind and body, but they are not strategies for saving the times. Why not seek knowledge of wealth and strength to fulfill my wish?" Ma Sheng then purchased and borrowed dozens of books, including Taoqian Wubei (Military Strategy) and San Nong Zhi Fu (Agricultural Wealth), and they closed the door and discussed them in depth.

    128

    年余，玉曰：「得之矣。」乃出门，遍历荒山，得无主之地数十顷，归而尽其所有，皆易钱，不足，乞贷父兄亲族以益之。使生置芋粟，一名苞谷，此贱而易成之物，遍撤山地。玉乃日游里闾，结好众瑶妇，得其爱戴心，谓之曰：「本年当大旱，救荒之计，我已密布山间，将来成熟时，可以周济汝等，但须为我照料耳。」众妇皆悦，为之挟刃巡逻。秀实时，争为收割，不失一茎。时果夏秋无雨，禾苗枯槁，惟此独茂。玉乃计口授瑶妇粟，欢呼拜谢而去。尚余千锺，粜之，得千余金。偿债之外，犹称小康。次年，瑶妇皆来请种，愿为耕耘。玉曰：「今年应涝，惟稷独成。」购种遍播之。夏秋果大雨，诸谷皆淹没，稷高丈余，不畏水，又获丰收。仍分给酬劳外，剩数千锺，粜之，大富，起厦屋居之。

    Explanation

    128

    After some time, the man said, "I have it." He then went out to explore the wild mountains and acquired tens of hectares of unclaimed land. Upon returning, he sold all his possessions for money, but when that was not enough, he borrowed from his father, brothers, and relatives to supplement the amount. He had someone plant yams and millet, which is also known as maize, an inexpensive and easily cultivated crop, and planted it throughout the mountainous area. The man frequently visited the village, building good relations with the Yao women and earning their love and admiration. He told them, "This year is expected to be very dry. My plan to alleviate famine is already in place in the mountains. When it matures in the future, it can help you all, but just need to look after it for me." The women all agreed and took turns patrolling with weapons. When the crop was ripe, they competed to harvest it, ensuring that no single plant was left unharvested. It turned out that there was no rain during the summer and autumn seasons, and the crops withered, except for the millet, which flourished. The man distributed millet based on the number of people, and the Yao women cheered, bowed in gratitude, and departed. There were still a thousand dou remaining, which he sold, earning more than a thousand gold pieces. After paying off debts, he was still considered moderately well-off. The next year, the Yao women all came to ask to plant and were willing to cultivate. The man said, "This year is expected to be flooded, but only millet will succeed." He bought seeds and planted them widely. In summer and autumn, it rained heavily, and all other grains were flooded, but the millet grew over ten feet tall and was not afraid of water, and had another abundant harvest. Still distributing rewards, and had several thousand dou remaining, which he sold, becoming very wealthy, and built a large house to live in.

    129

    他察官民皆乏食，流为盗贼，而石柱赖以无恙。男女咸敬佩良玉如神明，愿为服役者甚众。玉择其勤能者留之。生亦喜曰：「卿何以知天支，测之皆验？」玉笑曰：「《前汉书》曰『巢居知风，穴居知雨』，我师蚁耳。凡旱年，其穴必深，涝年，必迁高处。以是卜之，百不失一，何须高谈天文，炫奇惊异哉？」生乃服其读书之得闻也，曰：「卿言富，则果富矣。贵乌在？」良玉曰：「勿急，我后必貤封君，为天下妇人吐气。

    Explanation

    129

    He observed that officials and common people were all short of food, and as a result, some turned to banditry, but the region of Shizhu remained safe and unharmed. Both men and women deeply respected and admired Liang Yu as if he were a deity, and many were eager to serve him. Liang Yu selected the diligent and capable individuals to retain. The official was also pleased and asked, "How do you know about the heavenly signs, and how did your predictions all prove accurate?" Liang Yu smiled and replied, "The History of the Former Han Dynasty says, 'Those who live in nests know the wind, and those who live in holes know the rain.' I learned from the ants. During drought years, their nests are always deep, and during flood years, they always move to higher ground. Using this method, I never miss a prediction. Why bother with complex discussions of astronomy or showing off strange phenomena?" The official then admired Liang Yu's knowledge gained from reading and said, "You speak of wealth, and indeed you are rich. But where is your nobility?" Liang Yu replied, "Do not hurry. In the future, I will definitely be ennobled and speak on behalf of all women."

    The arrangements had just been completed when the neighboring camp indeed harbored ill intentions, sending dozens of people to steal. Breaking into the house, they all rushed to the warehouse, and another six or seven out of ten died by falling into the cellar. Only a dozen or so remained. Neighbors came to rescue and bound them all, handing them over to the authorities. Thus, the neighboring camp used this as an excuse to invite all the other camps, and they all rose up to attack. The chieftain drove the townspeople into battle, suffering a great defeat, and was subsequently killed. The villagers were greatly alarmed and publicly discussed that Liang Yu's husband, who was related to the chieftain, should inherit the position. The people said, "It would be better if it were her wife." The people entered Sheng's home and firmly requested Liang Yu to take charge of the chieftain's seal to defend against the enemy. Liang Yu said, "The way to defend against the enemy is for everyone to work together, like the arm and fingers working in unison, to achieve success. If everyone acts independently, the lessons of the past are clear, and that would be my death. Can you all follow my orders?"     132

    于是，略其地方三百余里，料其民得十万余众。立为大寨，居中，以亲信者同住。环作小寨，居其民。择其强壮者，训以兵法，坐作进退，井井有条。寨外掘长壕周匝，壕中皆置毒蒺藜，上覆机板，并如居室法，外伏毒弩。寨之四隅，树长木，木颠以辘轳悬作屋。穴孔向外，以老花近视二镜，迭作筒，安孔中，即千里镜也，能睹百里外人马。使能书者居其上，以长绳悬铃达内营，名曰天观，一有所见，即书条，摇铃索报信。又掘地三四丈，埋瓮，使耳聪者卧其上，能闻百十里人言马嘶。亦以铃索达内营，名曰地听，一有所闻，亦如前录报。再远则广布细作，故远近巨细，无不周知。又作连翔阵，人各执喷筒，以毒药煮细沙，晾透，纳筒中。每伍间弩手一排护之。战必抢上风，顺风扬沙，入人目，即迷疼不得开。弩手枪手继之，是杀瞽目也，故易胜。

    Explanation

    132

    Thus, they encircled an area of over three hundred miles, estimating the population at over one hundred thousand. They established a large camp, central, with trusted individuals residing there. Surrounding it were smaller camps for the people. They selected the strong, trained them in military tactics, with orderly movements and formations. Outside the camp, they dug a long moat all around, placing spikes in the moat, covering it with mechanisms, and setting up hidden crossbows. At the four corners of the camp, they erected tall trees, with houses suspended from pulleys at the tops. Holes facing outward were equipped with two telescopes, one for near vision and one for far vision, placed in a tube, which was inserted into the hole, forming a long-distance viewing device capable of seeing people and horses up to a hundred miles away. They stationed literate individuals there, using long ropes with bells to communicate with the inner camp, naming it the "Heavenly Watch." Whenever they saw anything, they would write it down and ring the bell to send a message. They also dug underground pits three to four zhang deep, burying jars, and had individuals with keen hearing lie on top, able to hear people and horses up to a hundred li away. They also used bells and ropes to communicate with the inner camp, naming it the "Earthly Hearing." Whenever they heard anything, they would record it and send a message as before. For even further distances, they widely deployed spies, so that both near and far, large and small matters, were all thoroughly known. They also formed the "Flying Formation," with each person holding a smoke bomb, filled with toxic substances and dried fine sand, placed in the bomb. Each unit had a row of crossbowmen for protection. In battle, they always took the upper hand, releasing smoke with the wind, which entered the enemy's eyes, causing them to be blinded and in pain, unable to open their eyes. Crossbowmen and musketeers followed, effectively blinding the enemy, making victory easy.

    At the time, the defeated bandits regrouped and invited the mountain tribes to launch a large-scale attack. They led the way with cattle, sheep, camels, and horses, followed by earth carts. In an instant, the camp grounds collapsed, and the stored food ignited with rockets and fireballs, creating a thick smoke that filled the sky, killing thousands. The remaining bandits fled the camp, only to be surrounded by the encircling army, leading to their surrender.     135

    This incident occurred during the reign of the Chongzhen Emperor of the Ming dynasty. At that time, the capital, Beijing, was under severe siege by rebel forces, and a call was issued to all directions for military assistance to protect the king. Qin Liangyu, accompanied by her husband, quickly mobilized their troops and set out, with her brother leading the vanguard. They marched with the wind, stirring up dust, and won all their battles, thereby relieving the capital from its state of emergency. The emperor was greatly pleased and summoned Qin Liangyu to the imperial court, intending to bestow on her the title of Marquis. Qin Liangyu declined, saying, "The title of Marquis for a woman, although it has existed in ancient times, does not conform to the norms of the imperial court. If there is no other option, I request that my husband be posthumously honored." The emperor then summoned Qin Liangyu's husband, Ma Sheng, and bestowed upon him the title of Marquis of Pacifying the North, with countless honors and rewards. Qin Liangyu herself was given the titles of Brave Lady of the Village and Great Marshal of Shizhu. After expressing her gratitude, Qin Liangyu left the court, where officials demanded bribes. She told her husband, "The government is in disarray. The emperor's attendants are all sycophantic, greedy, and slanderous, and this situation will not last long. Do not get involved in their troubles." She then resigned on the pretext of an excuse, returned home with her troops in good order, and her descendants continued to hold the hereditary position of local ruler.

    　　某郎中
    　　郎中某，武林人，能忆宿世事。云前生为苏郡庠生，六十无子，家寒教读度日，仅足夫妻餬口而已。自曾祖父母以下三代未葬，恒以为憾。乃发愿每夜焚香一枝，跪告天日，愿减己寿，俾进财百金以葬三代，死亦瞑目。积虔五六年，未能如愿而卒。

    136

    Xiang'an said: Observing the planning of the military governor's wife and Qin Liangyu, the great men of antiquity were no more than this. Unexpectedly, there are such figures among women, it is as if heaven has opened a rare stone. I once read the I Ching and doubted the theory of yin and yang. If yang is dominant over yin, why not say "yang-yin"? Some say that the hexagrams of the I Ching are all inverted, but this still does not resolve my doubts. Now observing these two ladies, I realize that the bright aspect of yin can truly overshadow yang, this is the true explanation of the words "yin" and "yang."

    A certain medical officer,
    A medical officer from Wulin, was able to remember past lives. He said his previous life was a scholar in Suzhou, at sixty years old without a son, living a poor life by teaching, just enough to sustain the couple. His great-grandparents and below, three generations, were not buried, and he always felt regret. So he made a vow to burn an incense stick every night, kneeling to heaven, wishing to shorten his own life to gain a hundred gold pieces to bury the three generations, even in death, he would be at peace. For five or six years of devout practice, unable to fulfill his wish, he died.

    其魂飘然入阴司见阎罗王，王曰：「此孝子也，愿减筭以葬父祖。不知汝父母生前恶业甚多，致汝绝后。汝虽一点诚心，历年不懈，但生平不过安分，无大功德，不足挽回造化。然孝思可敬也。」赐之坐。左右报大孝子到，王命开正门，身出迎之。见一披发尺余，鸠形鹄面之丐，鹑衣百结，水湿淋漓，见王下跪，王扶之起，携手而入，设座生上。王奖不绝口，丐觳觫不安。生甚疑虑，王顾之，谓生曰：「汝疑耶？此君镇江人，生于贫家，自幼失怙，其母携之乞食。至七八岁时，膝行求乞，以养其母。又逾七八年，其母老病不能行，此君负之，哀号于市，人皆怜而济之，必饱其母而后敢自食。如是者十余年，其母病卒。此君求化一席，刨土埋之，投江而死。是一生专行其孝，别无他志。孝为百行先，出于下愚之人，岂不足以感动神明哉？」正议论间，忽见红光照耀，瑞彩缤纷。

    137

    The soul floated into the underworld and appeared before Yama King. The king said, "This is a filial son who wishes to shorten his own life to bury his ancestors. However, your parents had many evil deeds in life, which led to your inability to have descendants. Although you have a sincere heart and have been unwavering for years, your life has been content with your lot, lacking great merit or virtue, and thus unable to reverse fate. Nevertheless, your filial piety is worthy of respect." The king granted him a seat. The attendants reported the arrival of the great filial son, and the king ordered the main gate to be opened, personally greeting him. He saw a beggar with hair hanging down more than a foot, a crow-like figure and crane-like face, wearing ragged clothes soaked through and through. The beggar knelt before the king, who helped him up, took his hand, and led him inside, seating him on a higher platform. The king praised him without ceasing, but the beggar trembled with fear. The soul was very doubtful, and the king turned to him and said, "Are you doubtful? This man is from Zhenjiang, born into a poor family. He lost his father at a young age, and his mother raised him by begging. By the time he was seven or eight years old, he crawled on his knees to beg, supporting his mother. After another seven or eight years, his mother grew old and ill, unable to walk. This man carried her, crying out in the market, and people pitied him, helping him first feed his mother before they would eat themselves. This went on for over a decade until his mother died. The man then begged for a place to rest, dug a grave, buried her, and threw himself into the river and died. He dedicated his entire life to filial piety, with no other aspirations. Filial piety is the foremost among all virtues, even coming from a person of low intelligence, how could this not move the gods?" As they were discussing, suddenly a red light shone, and a myriad of auspicious colors appeared.

    138

    堂上堂下吏卒俱俯伏，朱衣判报圣僧来矣。王亦下堂跪，见五色云自天降，中立一胖大和尚，以手援阎王起而笑曰：「老僧七世修行，尚须过台下。不知何岁西行耳？」王肃容致敬曰：「圣僧根蒂既深，证果不远矣。」和尚曰：「正恐坠落耳。」乃设座公案前。王侍立，和尚命之坐，然后隅坐鞠躬。时生与丐皆避殿下，和尚举目遍观，在群鬼中指曰：「此二孝子也，请来相见。」二人入拜。和尚合十答礼，皆命坐。左右献茶，和尚举杯谓二人曰：「此茶饮之昧性，然不饮则违天条。老僧请以法解之。」命二人擎杯至座前，和尚默诵神咒，茶水自涸，各举空杯对阎王曰：「饮讫矣。」王唯唯。髯判执簿进王曰：「圣僧下降吉时到，请即飞升。」见数鬼卒扶长梯置殿前，王肃和尚登梯，和尚曰：「有缘者，二子可以同登。」王即命判注簿，使二人相随。僧前丐中生后，直上数百级，足力不济，乃坠，囫然一声，已作孩矣。

    138

    In the hall and below, all officials and soldiers knelt in unison, as a red-clothed judge announced the arrival of the saintly monk. The king also descended from the hall and knelt, witnessing a colorful cloud descending from the sky, with a large, fat monk standing in the middle. The monk reached out to help the king stand and smiled, saying, "I have practiced for seven lifetimes, but I still need to pass through the judgment hall. I do not know when I will go west." The king respectfully greeted the monk, saying, "Your roots in Buddhism are deep, and your enlightenment is not far off." The monk replied, "I am just afraid of falling short." He then set up a seat in front of the public bench. The king stood by, and the monk invited him to sit, after which the king bowed at the corner. At this time, the two individuals (生 and 丐) hid behind the hall. The monk looked around and pointed out the two individuals among the ghosts, saying, "These are two filial sons. Please come and meet them." The two individuals entered and bowed. The monk responded with a gesture of respect and invited them to sit. The attendants offered tea, and the monk took a cup and spoke to the two individuals, saying, "This tea, if drunk, would dull your nature, but if not drunk, it would violate the heavenly rules. I will use a method to solve this." He instructed the two individuals to bring the cups to the front. The monk silently recited a magical incantation, and the tea dried up. Each held up an empty cup and said to the king, "We have finished drinking." The king nodded in agreement. The bearded judge held a book and approached the king, saying, "The auspicious time for the saintly monk to descend has arrived. Please ascend immediately." Several ghost soldiers placed a long ladder in front of the hall. The king respectfully invited the monk to climb the ladder. The monk said, "Those with good karma, these two sons can also climb." The king ordered the judge to record this in the book and allowed the two individuals to follow. The monk led, followed by the beggar and the other individual. They climbed hundreds of steps, but the latter's strength failed, and he fell, making a sound, and was reborn as a child.

    139

    开目见本生父母，皆喜曰：「男也。」生觉顶心虚怯，不能言，惟笑啼而已。得乳甘美，果腹。至三岁，顖门合而能言，忆前事了了，如在目前。知鬼神敬孝子，是以一举一动，无不曲体亲心。父母爱如珍宝。前生所读书，不忘只字，五六岁，即理前业，能诗文，称神童。八岁入学，十三举于乡，十七成进士，授礼部主事。父母相继殁，哀毁尽礼，守制三年。二十而娶，入都复职。元日大朝，随班礼毕，皇上退殿。一太监至主事前，问姓名官职，曰：「某亲王有命，请主政公，今夜入府有话。」授以牙牌，曰：「持此以达，门官即不敢阻，得速见也。」主事向不识王，心甚疑之，然不敢拒。

    139

    Upon opening his eyes, the newborn saw his biological parents, who were all delighted and exclaimed, "It's a boy!" The child felt a sense of vulnerability at the top of his head and could not speak, only laughing and crying. He received milk that was sweet and satisfying. By the age of three, his fontanelle had closed and he began to speak, remembering past events clearly as if they were right before him. Knowing that ghosts and spirits respected filial piety, he always acted in a way that pleased his parents. His parents loved him as if he were a precious treasure. He could recall every word he had read in his past life, and by the age of five or six, he could manage his previous studies, composing poetry and prose, and was hailed as a prodigy. At eight, he entered school, passed the local examinations at thirteen, became a Jinshi (imperial scholar) at seventeen, and was appointed as a clerk in the Ministry of Rites. After the deaths of his parents, he observed the three-year mourning period with deep sorrow and adherence to filial piety. At twenty, he married and returned to his official duties in the capital. On New Year's Day, he participated in the court ceremony, and after the rites were completed, the emperor retired from the throne. A eunuch approached the clerk, asking for his name and position, and said, "A prince has a command for you, the Master of Affairs, to come to his residence tonight." He was given a jade tablet and instructed, "Present this to the gatekeeper, who will not dare to obstruct you, and you will be able to see the prince quickly." The clerk had never met the prince before and was quite suspicious, but he could not refuse the summons.

    归宅，晚膳后登王府，以牙牌手版交门官。引入见王，其状貌，即大和尚也。王笑迎曰：「故人犹忆前事乎？」主事再拜曰：「唯不敢忘我王大德。」王赐之坐，曰：「予在殿上，遥睹君貌犹昔，故使人招君话旧。君今虽登仕版，然世事纷扰，不若修行之乐也。余生不食荤，忆前生所作工课，惟默为之，恐骇圣父母听闻耳。然时时惧坠落，不敢稍生妄念，今将回首矣。君何不弃官入道？」主事曰：「固所愿也。但家贫子幼，难摆脱耳。」王曰：「事不难，君记孝丐否？余将使彼助君，不可为外人道，静候时运耳。」主事起，告退，王曰：「君去不必再来，修心为要，无多嘱也。」主事叩谢而出。

    朮芷治痘
    　　痘疮者，父母欲火所结，病在先天。天一生水，故人之五脏，肾先成火，毒伏其中，感时气即发。其有不险者，父母同房时，清心寡欲，不茹荤酒，则毒轻易出。若食有毒之物，而又沉醉，所生子女其毒必重。不见富贵之儿，殇于痘者多，贫贱之子，伤于痘者少乎？若痘出幼年，尚可，成丁婚配后出痘，成者甚鲜。盖先天已伤，不能通达故也。凡医皆执此说。
    　　乡人黄大者，年二十，父母已故，娶有妻室。幼未出痘。是年春间痘症盛行，黄大忽患大热，一身尽疼，入于骨骸，求死不得。七八日间，面现红尖数点，其妻请邻翁视之，曰：「此痘疮也，甚险。」乃延痘科诊之，曰：「阴亏甚矣。必补托而后可，以六味地黄加减。」立方而去。其妻以百钱求邻翁取药，翁曰：「我家潮湿，甚思买苍朮、白芷熏屋，正好乘便。」遂入市择兴旺药肆，投以钱与方并买术、芷二十钱。

    Explanation

    143

    Treatment of Smallpox

    Smallpox is a disease caused by the intense desires of the parents, and it affects the fetus from the very beginning. According to the I Ching, the first element created by heaven is water, and thus, the kidneys are the first organ to form in the fetus, with smallpox toxins latent within them. The disease is triggered by seasonal changes or environmental factors. There are cases where smallpox is not severe, such as when the parents abstain from meat and alcohol and maintain a calm and pure mind during intercourse, making the toxins less harmful. However, if the parents consume toxic substances and indulge in alcohol, the toxins in their children will be more severe. It is observed that wealthy children often die from smallpox, while poor children are less likely to be harmed by it. Smallpox occurring after marriage and childbearing is rare and often fatal, as the body's vital energy is already damaged and cannot recover easily. All doctors adhere to this belief.

    A man named Huang Da, aged twenty, had both parents deceased and was married. He had never had smallpox. That year, smallpox was prevalent in the spring, and Huang Da suddenly fell ill with a high fever, his entire body aching deeply into the bones, and he wished to die but could not. After seven or eight days, several red bumps appeared on his face. His wife asked a neighbor to examine him, who said, "This is smallpox, very dangerous." She then called a doctor, who said, "There is a severe deficiency of yin. Treatment must involve strengthening the body and supporting its functions, using a modified version of the Liu Wei Di Huang Wan." The doctor left after prescribing the medicine. His wife spent a hundred coins to ask the neighbor to fetch the medicine. The neighbor said, "My house is damp, and I very much want to buy mugwort and angelica root to fumigate it, which is convenient for me." He then went to a successful and reputable pharmacy, bought the herbs and the medicine for twenty coins.

    144

    铺伙甚忙，包药之际，以药方误插朮、芷包上。翁不知也，至家，交有方者与黄妻，嘱速煎而进之。黄大服后，即得安眠。翁夜生盆火，开包取朮、芷，则皆药料矣。急往叩门问之，黄妻曰：「已煎服半日，睡甚安，似大见效。」翁不敢言而回。次早往视，一身痘花皆现，光明磊落，且索饭食，神气间如无病者。翁诧异，即代为延医复诊，医曰：「已反逆回顺，非我重用地黄，不能如是神速也。今可不药收功矣。」翁心中抱歉，朝夕在侧，殷懃服侍。果十朝痘尽回，痂渐脱落，壮健如初。

    Explanation

    144

    The shop assistants were very busy, and during the preparation of the medicine, the prescription was mistakenly placed on the package of mugwort (朮) and spikenard (芷). The old man did not know about the mistake. When he arrived home, he handed the package over to someone knowledgeable and his wife, instructing them to boil and administer it quickly. After Huang took the medicine, he fell asleep immediately. That night, the old man lit a fire and opened the package, only to find that it contained medicinal ingredients instead of the herbs he expected. He rushed to knock on the door to ask what had happened. Huang's wife replied, "We have been boiling and administering it for half a day. He is sleeping peacefully and seems to be greatly improved." The old man did not dare to say anything and returned home.

    The next morning, the old man went to see Huang, who had developed a rash all over his body, which looked clear and bright, and he was eating and seemed to be in good spirits. The old man was surprised and immediately asked a doctor to come for a follow-up examination. The doctor said, "The condition has reversed, and without the heavy use of Rehmannia (地黄), it would not have improved so quickly. Now, no further medication is needed." The old man felt sorry and stayed by Huang's side day and night, serving him with great care. Indeed, after ten days, all the rashes had healed, the scabs gradually fell off, and Huang was as strong and healthy as before.

    黄大感甚，乃杀鸡烹肉，备谢礼，请医，并酬邻翁之劳。医持杯大言曰：「非我妙手，恐此症不得回春。老翁阅历多矣，岂不见壮年出痘者十有九死乎？」翁曰：「不然。假如此症误服苍朮、白芷，将何如？」医曰：「一滴入口，早已毙矣。」翁即回家取药曰：「请观此，非先生所开之药乎？」医检之曰：「是也。」翁曰：「是则误矣。以同市两包相混，而黄大所服者实朮、芷也。」医曰：「莫与我争功。我阅书多矣，从无朮、芷发痘之说。此必药肆匆忙，误包两料药，实未给朮、芷也。」翁乃呼黄妻，出药滓示之，固朮、芷也。翁曰：「我非争功，若果朮、芷所愈，有后患否？是以求教。」医摇首支吾，持谢金而去。二人怀疑莫释，遍访时医，皆曰无此情理。或者痘为朮、芷逼引入内，复发无药可疗矣。二人更急矣。

    Huang Da was greatly alarmed, so he killed a chicken, cooked the meat, prepared a gift of thanks, summoned a doctor, and rewarded the old neighbor for his assistance. The doctor, holding a cup, boasted, "Without my skillful hands, this condition might not recover. The old man has much experience; has he not seen that nine out of ten adolescents who contract smallpox die?" The old man replied, "Not so. If this condition was mistakenly treated with aconite and angelica, what would happen?" The doctor said, "If even a drop enters the mouth, death would be instantaneous." The old man then went home to fetch the medicine and said, "Please look at this; isn't it the medicine you prescribed?" The doctor examined it and said, "Yes, it is."
