    时巨室以千金延名医薛生白在邑，二人执香跪门求诊。生白悯其诚，使人诊之。谓黄大曰：「脉甚和平，无疾何治。」翁始以疑质之，生白大笑曰：「是矣，此必黄君祖功宗德，不应绝后，故有此误。若服地黄汤，闷死久矣。时医不知用药之活变，而执古方，冤死者不少。彼意谓有夫妇，必有房事，亏损肾经。故壮年出痘，必先补托。不知夫妇之事，天生天化，互相补益。若以为有房事者必损，则世无八九十岁夫妇偕老之人，而鳏寡孤独，皆千万岁矣。惟好色过度则伤，黄君一夫一妇，人伦之常，复有何损？其痘之郁而不发者，必平日尽力农田，长浸水中，深受湿气，遏不得达，是以痛楚。老翁所市朮、芷必有数两，大剂投之，水气立散，有不畅茂条达者乎？时医何能见及此？我故曰：祖功宗德，鬼神所使也。且黄君脉大而长，不但痘不复发，且享寿无疑。」二人心始释然，喜跃再拜而去。

    乌蛇已癞
    　　蛇之种类伙矣，皆追风药也。内有乌稍蛇一种，最毒。姑苏有曹吏部，由郎中出为粤东潮州府。是邑也，凡幼女，皆蕴癞毒，故及笄，须有人过癞去，方可婚配。女子年十五六，无论贫富，皆在大门外工作，诱外来浮浪子弟交。住弥月，女之父母张灯彩，设筵席，会亲友，以明女癞去，可结亲矣。时浪子亦与宴．事毕，富者酌赠医资送去。多则一年，必发癞死。且能过人，故亲人不敢近。官之好善者，设癞院收养之。

    A Woman with Two Heads and Four Arms

    The varieties of snakes are numerous, all of which can be used as remedies for wind-related ailments. Among them, the black snake (乌稍蛇) is the most venomous. There was a Cao from Suzhou who served as a Ministry of Personnel official and was later appointed to the Chaozhou Prefecture in Guangdong. In this region, all young girls are believed to carry a condition similar to leprosy, so when they reach the age of 15 (of笄), they must undergo a ritual to remove this condition before they can marry. Girls aged 15 or 16, regardless of their wealth, all work outside the main gate to attract idle young men. After a month, the girl's parents set up lanterns and decorations, prepare a feast, and gather relatives and friends to signify that the girl's condition has been removed and she is now eligible to marry. At this time, the young men also attend the feast. After the event, the wealthy provide gifts or donations for medical expenses. If the condition persists for more than a year, the girl will inevitably die from leprosy. Moreover, the condition can be contagious, so close family members are afraid to approach her. Those who are kind-hearted and charitable set up leprosy hospitals to care for them.

    148

    曹太守有弟，已冠，不好学，日事游荡。戚友知此间风俗者，恒诰诫之。介弟初亦不敢犯，但游观而已。一日，至巨宅前，见一女子，国色也，不粉饰而自然，既艳丽而庄重。不禁迷恋，辗转再三，舍之不得。喟然曰：「人生几何，美色难遇，牡丹花下死，较老髦乐甚也。」意乃决。与女交谈，引之入室，两情相得，有终焉之志。无如弥月后，例应分折。其父母见二人情重，不使女知。请介弟前堂大宴，询及家世，方知为太守亲弟。屡奉府县查访綦切，不胜惊骇。但事已如此，不能隐匿，赠以千金，送之回府。太守以乃弟自作之孽，无可奈何，资送回籍，俟死而已。

    Explanation

    148

    Magistrate Cao had a younger brother who, having undergone the cap ceremony, did not take to learning and spent his days wandering aimlessly. Friends who were familiar with the local customs often admonished him. Initially, the younger brother dared not transgress, but he merely wandered around. One day, he came before a grand mansion and saw a woman of extraordinary beauty, naturally unadorned, both graceful and dignified. He could not resist his infatuation, hesitated repeatedly, but could not let her go. He sighed and said, "How long is life, and beautiful women are hard to find. To die under the peony flowers is more enjoyable than being an old man." His mind was thus resolved. He spoke with the woman, led her into the room, and they found mutual affection, with the intention to stay forever. But after a month, it was customary to separate. Their parents saw that the two were deeply attached and did not inform the girl. They invited the younger brother to a grand feast in the main hall, asked about his family background, and only then learned that he was the magistrate's younger brother. He had been repeatedly investigated by the county and prefecture, and could not help but be shocked. But since things had come to this, they could not hide it, so they gave him a thousand gold pieces and sent him back to the magistrate's residence. The magistrate attributed his younger brother's misdeed to his own son, feeling helpless, and provided funds to send him back to his hometown, awaiting his death.

    　　金标客

    Jin Biao Ke
    Jin Biao Ke, surnamed Jin, was registered in Jiahe. He was a person of good virtue, learning martial arts as a child, and could use qi to resist metal weapons. In his prime, he went out to protect others, becoming famous throughout the rivers and lakes, with bandits fearing him upon hearing of him. When he grew old, he had a fortune in his waist, living in Qinghe of Jiangnan, making a living by running boats, and living contentedly without going out anymore.

    夏日，在水阁纳凉，见一舟扬帆而过，篷窗四起，中坐青年公子，外二仆人。回顾舟子，识皆劫贼。顿起怜悯心，疾卷行囊追及之。乞附舟南旋，舟子不纳。公子见其二毛，怜贫老而许之。舟子曰：「人各有心，知其无歹意耶？设有他虞，非我等不预言也。」公子曰：「此老，我三人能备之。毋需尔过虑。」金闻言，一跃登舟，与公子为礼，遂问行踪。公子告以父宰山左，回原籍武林就婚也。与金联乡谊，谈甚洽，以长者呼之，每饭必共。家人心不谓然，见于词色。公子益尊敬之。舟行长淮时，金密谓公子曰：「舟子皆江湖积贼，今当停泊某所，若过此，必逗遛旷野，将行其谋矣。」公子怖甚，曰：「奈何？」金曰：「有老夫在，彼四五后生不足惧也。某今夜与公子易地而寝，看其如何下手！」公子甚疑惧。果舟至闹市竟过。金问之，舟子曰：「风利不得泊也。」公子益惧，夜乃与金潜易卧处。

    The Scholar of Literature

    There was a scholar of literature named Chen, whose family was very poor. He borrowed dozens of gold coins from friends and relatives and went to the capital to take the metropolitan examination. Traveling alone to Wangjiayuan, he hired a carriage with thirty gold coins. The two mules were very strong and well-fed, and the coachman stood with raised eyebrows, chest out, and protruding belly, also very strong and healthy. Chen said, "This place is over a thousand miles from the capital, how could I have so much money to help you? If you cannot proceed, return my original fare, and I will hire another carriage."     While the text was already present, [the person] kicked the pole with one foot, and the two mules could not move an inch. With one hand, [the person] lifted the driver and threw him to the ground, then leapt onto his back, seized the whip, and whipped him hundreds of times. The driver wailed in pain, pleading for mercy. Mr. Chen got off the carriage to plead for leniency, and [the person] released him, allowing Mr. Chen to return to his seat. [The person] then sat on the pole, escorting them back to the main road. [The person] said to the driver, "I am a scholar, but I practice martial arts. Regardless of whether you, one person and two mules, can stop me, it's not remarkable. Look at me using both hands to pull a few carts backward, making them go in reverse." He demonstrated, and indeed, he did so. The driver gasped in amazement, began to fear, and dared not harbor any evil intentions. They accompanied him into the capital, returned the silver borrowed from Mr. Wen, and left. Mr. Chen was deeply moved and said, "Brother, your divine strength is unmatched in the world. Is it innate or through practice?" The person replied, "This is the method of the Yijinjing. The book is available; diligently practice it, and nothing is impossible. People just don't do it." From then on, they became very close and became inseparable friends.

    160

    芗厈曰：此入道之大端也。夫道无所不可。养气则至大至刚；养志则修齐治平；养身则合精气神为正一。可以飞升，可以拔宅。即《易筋经》一书，达摩传为入道基，非仅习勇力也。人配天地，曰三才，其才本广大无伦，故儒家之明德，道家之三宝，释家之本觉、真心，人人共具，专其一而修之，圣贤仙佛，惟人所愿，岂仅勇力乎哉？

    Explanation

    160

    Xiang Yan said: This is the great principle of entering the Dao. The Dao is without limits. Nurturing qi leads to being extremely vast and strong; nurturing one's aspirations leads to self-cultivation, family order, state governance, and world peace; nurturing the body integrates essence, qi, and spirit into the One. One can achieve immortality or supernatural powers. The Muscle/Tendon Changing Classic is a foundational text for entering the Dao, not just for developing physical strength. Humans, matched with heaven and earth, are called the Three Talents, and their talents are inherently vast and unparalleled. The bright virtue of Confucianism, the Three Treasures of Daoism, and the innate enlightenment and true mind of Buddhism are possessed by everyone; one should focus on cultivating one of them. Sages, virtuous men, immortals, and Buddhas are attainable according to one's desire. Is it merely about physical strength?

    161

    何首乌
    　　何首乌，一名能嗣，药中仙品。产山泽者固多，亦有在城市，而其根反得成人形者，以得人之精气多耳。然具人形者必通灵，隐现无恒，人不能得。若得而食之，即仙去，相传已久。
    　　吾邑有张氏姑妇者，夫与子皆诸生，以家贫，教读外出，惟二妇在家操作，女工度日，是以纺纱必夜午方休，每秋月皎洁，时闻院中似有幼孩征逐声。拔关视，则无有。妇与姑谋，后若有所闻，一人仍纺，一人穴窗隙窥之。于是轮流伺隙，妇果见两孩出自墙阴。长不满尺，一男一女，皆赤体，携手至院落中，对月再拜，互相扑跌为戏，妇潜告姑，虑曰：「恐系妖孽之子孙，犯之自肇衅矣。」皆不敢出，然心甚怀疑。

    Explanation

    161

    He Shouwu
    He Shouwu, also known as "Nengsi," is a divine medicine in traditional Chinese medicine. It is commonly found in mountains and marshes, but there are also instances where it grows in cities, and its roots sometimes take on human form due to the accumulation of human essence and energy. However, those that have human form are always spiritually connected, appearing and disappearing without constancy, and cannot be easily obtained by humans. If one were to consume them, they would ascend to immortality, and this has been passed down for a long time.

    In my hometown, there was a mother-in-law and daughter-in-law from the Zhang family. Both the husband and son were students, and because of their poverty, they went out to teach and read, leaving only the two women at home to work, making a living through women's work. As a result, they spun thread until the middle of the night. Every bright and clear autumn moon, they often heard in the courtyard what seemed to be the sounds of young children playing. When they opened the door to look, there was nothing there. The wife and mother-in-law planned that if they heard something later, one person would still spin, while the other would peer through a crack in the window. They took turns waiting for a crack, and the wife indeed saw two children come out from the shadow of the wall. They were not quite a foot long, one boy and one girl, both naked, holding hands to the courtyard, bowing twice facing the moon, and falling and rising together for play. The wife secretly told the mother-in-law, who worried and said, "I fear they are the descendants of evil spirits. Offending them will start trouble." Both dared not go out, but their hearts were very doubtful.

    162

    一日，所亲至，知医博学士也。姑以所疑质之。戚曰：「宅若有妖，何能安居？此必灵药所变。得而蒸食之，当成地仙。」妇笑曰：「渠闻人声即遁，焉能攫取？」曰：「无难，吾闻稻米，天地正气所结，能压宝藏。若由窗隙掷之，得中其身，即不能遁矣。」戚去，妇度院中孩戏之处，至窗隙，约丈余，谅掷米未必适当。乃截竹为筒，撒米其中，以箸卷布催送之。日练其手法，至精熟，复伺于窗隙，二孩来前，妇即以筒米弹之，果中，二孩皆仆，突出擒拿，入手僵直。呼姑举火烛之，类木雕者，眉目如画，气甚芳馥。姑妇相谋，煮饭时于铁锅内蒸之，一次稍软，至五六次，香绵可食。

    Explanation

    162

    One day, a close relative arrived, a learned scholar knowledgeable in medicine. Temporarily, she asked him about her doubts. Her relative said, "If there is a ghost in the house, how can one live there comfortably? This must be a transformation caused by a spiritual medicine. If obtained and steamed for consumption, it would turn one into a local immortal." The woman laughed and said, "It hears human voices and immediately flees; how could it be captured?" He replied, "No difficulty. I have heard that rice, which is the essence of the positive energy of heaven and earth, can suppress treasures. If it is thrown through a window gap and hits its body, it will not be able to flee." After the relative left, the woman measured the place where the children played in the courtyard, near the window gap, about a dozen feet away. She reasoned that throwing rice might not be precise. So, she cut a bamboo tube, filled it with rice, and used chopsticks to roll a cloth to send it. She practiced her technique daily until it became very skilled. She then waited at the window gap, and when the two children came forward, she immediately launched the rice-filled tube at them. It hit them, and both children fell down. She rushed out to capture them, and they were stiff and rigid in her hands. She called her mother-in-law to light a candle, and the two children looked like wooden carvings, with painted eyebrows and eyes, and a very fragrant aroma. The mother-in-law and the woman discussed it, and they decided to steam them in an iron pot while cooking rice. After one steaming, they were slightly soft, and after five or six steamings, they became fragrant and soft enough to eat.

    163

    姑妇各分食一枚，觉鲜美异常，腹果甚，一日不思饮食。夜眠至次日，皆不能起身矣，晌午，门不开，邻姥疑有故，逾垣窥之，见姑妇皆仰卧于床头，面及身俱肿，目开口张，不能言语。邻姥倩人走报，其父子归，不解何由，亦不识何疾，急邀知医之戚诊视。笑曰：「非疾也，日前母所说成形首乌，我曾说以捕法，谅必捕而食之。未识九蒸九晒之制，又不知避忌，误犯铁器，是以有毒。」试以解毒开通之药灌之。至七日，肿消人醒，问之果如医言。起后，强健逾前，累月不思食。其姑年已周甲，发白再黑，齿落重生，枯绉肌肤，皆皮脱而润泽，似二十许人，复生子。其妇年近四旬，转而为二八好女子，连举子女十余。后皆寿一百五六十岁，无疾而终。

    Explanation

    163

    The wife and daughter-in-law each ate one piece of the shaped Polygonum multiflorum (何首乌), finding it unusually delicious. Their stomachs indeed became very full, and they did not think of food for a day. They slept through the night until the next day and could not get up. By noon, the door was still closed, and the neighbor lady suspected something was wrong. She climbed over the wall to look and saw the wife and daughter-in-law lying on their backs at the head of the bed, their faces and bodies all swollen, their eyes open, their mouths wide, and they could not speak. The neighbor lady asked someone to go and report, and the husband and son returned home. They did not understand the cause, nor did they know what disease it was, so they urgently invited a knowledgeable relative who was a doctor to examine them. The doctor smiled and said, "It is not a disease. The mother said the shaped Polygonum multiflorum, and I once said to catch it. They must have caught and eaten it. They did not know the method of nine steams and nine dries, nor did they know the taboos, and they mistakenly used iron utensils, which is why it was toxic." They tried to administer detoxifying and opening drugs to them. After seven days, the swelling subsided, and they woke up. When asked, they confirmed it was as the doctor said. After waking up, they were stronger and healthier than before, and they did not think of food for several months. The mother-in-law, who was already in her sixties, had her white hair turn black again, her fallen teeth regrow, her dry and wrinkled skin shed and become moist and lustrous, resembling someone in their twenties, and she gave birth to a child. The wife, who was nearly forty, transformed into a beautiful woman in her twenties and gave birth to over ten children. Later, they all lived to be over 150 years old and died without any illness.

    164

    芗厈曰：惜乎！得灵药而不知服食之法，仅以延龄，无乃有负仙品。或问制食之法，余日曾考诸文献，当以柳木作桶，承以砂甑，用桑木火，先武后文，九蒸九晒，以竹刀剖作九顿食，可以绝粒入山矣。或笑曰：能得者不能制，能制者，必不能得，徒虚语耳。

    Explanation

    164

    芗厈曰：Alas! Having obtained the elixir but not knowing the method of consumption, one can only extend life, which surely falls short of the status of an immortal. Someone asked about the method of preparation, and I replied that I had examined the literature, and it should be done by making a bucket from willow wood, supporting it with a sand steamer, using mulberry wood fire, first vigorous and then gentle, nine steams and nine dries, and cutting into nine servings with a bamboo knife, which can lead to abstaining from food and entering the mountains. Another person laughed and said: Those who can obtain cannot prepare, and those who can prepare cannot obtain; it is just empty words.

    165

    第四卷

    　　一技养生
    　　吾乡有锺生者，业医。无人延请，偃蹇不堪。乃赴豫投亲戚之出仕者。其戚系闲曹，又未补缺，锺依之餬口而已。六月间，豫抚太夫人疾急，医皆束手。属员来见，必问有南医否，其戚以锺对。中丞命急召之，其戚谆嘱小心，锺唯唯而去。中丞延入卧室，见窗户皆闭，大生炉火，热不可耐。太夫人犹衣棉，且覆以棉衾。诊之，无脉。出谓中丞曰：「太夫人阳伏于内，阴见于外。当此大暑之时，必先去火开窗，并去棉衾，则脉必复。脉复乃可定也。」中丞曰：「前医无言及此者，先生高明。」乃从之。未几，太夫人索饮，中丞大悦曰：「我母不言，已二日矣，今依先生法，竟大苏醒。」复请锺诊视之，得脉，以藿香正气汤饮之，立痊。太夫人悦，命留在署，欲官之。为之报捐未入流，奏留豫省，充文巡捕。中丞言听计从，因此获财无算。

    Explanation

    165

    Translation:

    Fourth Chapter

    A Skill in Nurturing Life

    In my hometown, there was a man named Zhong who practiced medicine. Without anyone to call upon him, he felt dejected and unable to bear it. He then traveled to Henan to seek out a relative who had entered official service. His relative was in a low-ranking and inactive department, and had not yet filled a vacancy. Zhong relied on him merely to earn a living. In June, the governor's mother-in-law fell gravely ill, and all the doctors were at a loss. When subordinates came to see, they always asked if there was a southern doctor available, and his relative mentioned Zhong. The vice-governor ordered him to be summoned urgently, and his relative earnestly instructed him to be careful. Zhong replied in agreement and left. The vice-governor invited him into the bedroom, where he saw that the windows were all closed, and a large fire was burning, making the room unbearably hot. The governor's mother-in-law was still wearing cotton clothes and covered with a cotton quilt. After examining her, Zhong found no pulse. He came out and said to the vice-governor, "The governor's mother-in-law has yang energy suppressed internally and yin energy manifested externally. At this time of great heat, one must first remove the fire and open the windows, and take off the cotton quilt. Only then will the pulse return, and only then can the condition be stabilized." The vice-governor said, "None of the previous doctors mentioned this, showing how insightful you are." He then followed Zhong's advice. Soon after, the governor's mother-in-law asked for water, and the vice-governor was greatly pleased, saying, "My mother hasn't spoken for two days now, but following your method, she has finally regained consciousness." He then asked Zhong to examine her again, and upon finding the pulse, he administered the formula Huoxiang Zhengqi Tang to her, and she was immediately cured. The governor's mother-in-law was delighted and ordered him to stay in the office, intending to appoint him. They reported his donation without being in the official hierarchy, petitioned to keep him in Henan province, and appointed him as a civil patrol officer. The vice-governor followed his words and advice completely, and as a result, he gained countless amounts of wealth.

    166

    又张生系鹾商子，一无所长，惟好口腹。广搜古今食谱而准酌之，烹调甚精。未几父死业败，室人交谪，暂避武林，寓吕祖阁。阁前树木茂盛，有亭纳凉甚适。阁之左有大宅，系候补太守公馆，其仆从暇即来亭内坐谈，以是识张。数日间，闻太守盛怒，鞭扑家人，骂詈无已。其仆亦有时来，皆楚囚相对，非复从前畅快矣。张偶询之，一仆告曰：「主人蜀之富族，纳资得官。所好者精馔，有得意庖人偕来，日前中暑而死。主命我辈觅人，不如意则挞举荐者。连挞多人，皆不敢引进矣。又詈我等无良心，必欲饿死主人也，故嚷嚷不绝。不意偌大郡城，寻不出一善庖者。我辈命该绝矣。」同辈皆咨嗟叹息。张微哂曰：「我以为有大事也，故如此盛怒。

    Explanation

    166

    Zhang, the son of a salt merchant, had no special skills or talents, but he loved food. He widely collected ancient and modern recipes, carefully considering and adjusting them, and his cooking was very refined. Not long after, his father died and the business went bankrupt, and his wife and family blamed him. He temporarily fled to Wulin, lodging at Lüzu Pavilion. The trees in front of the pavilion were lush and dense, and there was a pavilion where one could cool off very comfortably. To the left of the pavilion was a large mansion, the residence of a deputy magistrate. His servants would come to the pavilion to chat during their leisure time, and thus Zhang became acquainted with them. Within a few days, Zhang heard that the magistrate was very angry, beating his family members and continuously cursing and scolding them. His servants would sometimes come, looking at each other like prisoners from Chu, no longer as carefree as before. Zhang casually asked them, and one servant replied, "The master is a wealthy family from Sichuan who obtained an official position by paying a fee. He likes fine cuisine and brought along a skilled cook, but the cook recently died of heatstroke. The master ordered us to find someone, and if we don't find a suitable person, he will beat the one who recommended us. He has beaten many people, and none of them dared to recommend anyone. He also cursed us for lacking a conscience, saying he wants to starve the master to death, so he continues to shout and complain. Unexpectingly, in such a large city, we cannot find one skilled cook. Our fate is sealed." The other servants all sighed and lamented. Zhang smiled slightly and said, "I thought there was a major event, so he is so furious."

    区区者，何地无之，君等诚不善觅耳。」仆曰：「然则先生能之乎？」张曰：「未识汝主果知味否？」众仆皆喜曰：「我等姑耐一顿皮鞭，请试为之。」乃具应用之物，交张，成四簋。夕飧进之，其香始升，不觉触鼻。太守曰：「何来此味？」试尝而甘之，大啖饱食。呼仆问所从来。仆告之故，立命传见。张曰：「我非庖人，因图馆寓此，行将归矣。岂为人作厨下媪哉？」仆复命。太守曰：「客何能，欲修金若干？肯为我庖人指点，我必延之。汝等善为我词，不可失此人也。」仆又往商，张曰：「汝主必欲留我，岁修三百金，亲来聘请，为司账房，兼督庖厨可也。」众仆惟恐失之，急为办行李衣装复命。太守往拜，订交，一一如约，相得甚欢。未几，太守得缺，张为司总，加修至千金。因此起家。

    167

    A humble person like me, there is no place without such a person, but you are not good at finding such a person. The servant said, "Then can the master do it?" Zhang replied, "I do not know if your master truly appreciates the taste." All the servants were delighted and said, "We will just endure a beating, please try it." They prepared the necessary ingredients and handed them to Zhang, who made four bowls. At the evening meal, the fragrance began to rise, unconsciously touching the nose. The magistrate said, "Where does this flavor come from?" He tried it and found it sweet, eating heartily and becoming full. He called the servant and asked where it came from. The servant explained the reason, and the magistrate immediately ordered him to be summoned. Zhang said, "I am not a cook, I am staying here temporarily, and I am about to leave. How could I serve as a kitchen maid?" The servant reported back. The magistrate said, "What skills does the guest have, and how much salary do you want? If you are willing to instruct my cooks, I will certainly hire you. You must speak well for me, and do not lose this person." The servant went back to negotiate, and Zhang said, "Your master must want to keep me, offering 300 gold coins annually, personally inviting me to be the accountant, and also overseeing the kitchen." All the servants were afraid of losing him, so they quickly prepared his luggage and clothing and reported back. The magistrate went to pay respects, established a friendship, and everything was as agreed, and they were very happy with each other. After a short time, the magistrate received a vacancy, and Zhang was appointed as the head, with the salary increased to 1,000 gold coins. Thus, he established a family.

    168

    又有妇人善哭者，无端发声，闻者泪下。南俗富贵之家，凡有丧吊，客来不绝，内帏须终日哭。主妇力不逮，或荐此妇代哭，能日夜不绝声。吊者闻其哀甚，佥称主妇孝。于是有丧之家争延之，通邑无二人。故鲜暇日，亦得小康。

    Explanation

    168

    In the southern regions, there was a woman skilled in weeping who could cry without any apparent reason, moving those who heard her to tears. In wealthy and noble families of the south, whenever there was a funeral or condolence, guests would keep arriving, and the women in the inner chambers would be required to cry all day. If the mistress was unable to cry continuously, she might recommend this woman to cry on her behalf, as she could cry without ceasing day and night. Those who came to mourn were deeply moved by her crying and praised the mistress for her apparent filial piety. Thus, families with funerals competed to invite her, and she was the only one of her kind in the city. Consequently, she had few idle days but still managed to live comfortably.

    芗厈曰：人既不能上达，必习一长一技，以为仰事俯育之资。否则，妄想求财，我不知渠何所藉。或曰：前三人，亦命应如此。不然，饱学秀才，埋没在蒙馆中者，不知凡几。一长一技，更何足道哉？余曰：如君言，误人不浅，若无所凭借而待命，天其雨金雨粟乎？非所以励中人也。
    　　昔有袜匠，业甚兴隆，晚年得子，爱如珍宝。年将及冠，犹不使学事业。亲友皆劝之，匠曰：「有命存也。」故人皆戏呼之曰「袜公子」。时有推五星者，曰张铁口，名卓卓。匠使推其子命，铁口曰：「此大富造也。行年三十，家资五百万。我在贵邑推命多矣，无出其右者。」书单与之。匠大悦，归使其妻，以锦作囊，纳单其中，悬于其子胸前曰：「无忘发财之年。」且以夸示亲友，益任其怠惰矣。为其子完姻后，匠夫妇相继亡。其子不能自立，所遗袜肆，为其伙抵盗净尽，渐至夫妇相携行乞。

    芗厈曰：人既不能上达，必习一长一技，以为仰事俯育之资。否则，妄想求财，我不知渠何所藉。或曰：前三人，亦命应如此。不然，饱学秀才，埋没在蒙馆中者，不知凡几。一长一技，更何足道哉？余曰：如君言，误人不浅，若无所凭借而待命，天其雨金雨粟乎？非所以励中人也。

    The Master said: Since people cannot attain higher understanding, they must acquire at least one skill or trade to provide for the support of their parents and the upbringing of their children. Otherwise, to foolishly seek wealth, I do not know what he relies on. Someone said: The first three people were also destined to be like this. Otherwise, there are countless well-learned scholars who are buried in private schools. One skill or trade, how much more need it be mentioned? I say: If what you say is true, you greatly mislead people. If one waits for fate without any support, will heaven rain gold and grain? This is not the way to encourage the average person.

    昔有袜匠，业甚兴隆，晚年得子，爱如珍宝。年将及冠，犹不使学事业。亲友皆劝之，匠曰：「有命存也。」故人皆戏呼之曰「袜公子」。时有推五星者，曰张铁口，名卓卓。匠使推其子命，铁口曰：「此大富造也。行年三十，家资五百万。我在贵邑推命多矣，无出其右者。」书单与之。匠大悦，归使其妻，以锦作囊，纳单其中，悬于其子胸前曰：「无忘发财之年。」且以夸示亲友，益任其怠惰矣。为其子完姻后，匠夫妇相继亡。其子不能自立，所遗袜肆，为其伙抵盗净尽，渐至夫妇相携行乞。

    Once there was a sock maker whose business was very prosperous. He had a son late in life and loved him like a treasure. When the son was about to reach adulthood, the father still did not allow him to learn a profession. Relatives and friends all advised him, but the father said, "It is due to fate." Therefore, people would jokingly call the son "Sock Prince." At that time, there was a fortune-teller named Zhang Tiekou, who was very famous. The father asked him to predict his son's fate, and Zhang said, "This is a great wealth maker. At the age of thirty, his family wealth will be five million. I have predicted many fates in this town, and none surpass this." He wrote down the prediction and gave it to the father. The father was very pleased and told his wife to make a silk pouch, put the prediction inside, and hang it on his son's chest, saying, "Do not forget the year of wealth."     六壬神课
    　　吾乡张君，鹾商子也。幼多病，故不甚读书，然敏甚，其慧解书旨，皆能领悟。及冠，自觉气禀甚弱，不愿婚娶。一日，在朋友案头见《大六壬》书，悦之，求教。友曰：「我虽知此，不甚精。」遂以大略指示之。张携归学习，不忍释手，复购求他本，以为揣摹。闻有秘本，不惜重价，不畏远道，务罗而致之。不售者，亲往手录。是以其书盈室，多人所不经见者。研精十载，忽大悟曰：「道不远人，非书所能该。」进束书不观，亦不肯为人决事。有时自露其机，则无不中。忽谓兄嫂曰：「此宅住不得矣，速往某亲戚家借寓，犹可及也。

    Liu Ren Divination

    Mr. Zhang, a salt merchant's son from my hometown, was often ill as a child and therefore did not read much. However, he was very quick-witted and could understand the essence of books. Upon reaching adulthood, he felt his constitution was very weak and did not wish to marry. One day, he saw the Da Liu Ren (Great Liu Ren) book on his friend's desk, was delighted by it, and asked to learn. His friend said, "I know this, but not very well." He then roughly explained it to him. Mr. Zhang took it back to study, could not let go of it, and bought other copies to study and emulate. Hearing of secret editions, he did not hesitate to pay high prices, did not fear long journeys, and determined to obtain them. Those not for sale, he personally went to copy them by hand. Therefore, his room was filled with books, many of which were unseen by others. After studying diligently for ten years, he suddenly had a great realization: "The way is not far from people, not something that books can encompass." He no longer looked at books and also refused to make decisions for others. Sometimes he revealed his insights, and they were always accurate. Suddenly, he told his brother and sister-in-law, "This house cannot be lived in anymore, hurry to a relative's house to stay temporarily, still in time."

    」兄曰：「宅乃祖遗，居此百余年，丰衣足食，人口平安，有何不美，而欲依亲戚家，不为人非笑耶？且迁宅不易，汝勿多言。」再三恳之，兄嫂执不可，张乃哀求其母曰：「十日不迁，儿为大不孝子。必见责于天而受祸也。」其母夙爱怜之，见惶迫之状，出于至诚，谕长子迁居。迫于母命，往见其戚假宅。戚果非笑之。然其家宅广人稀，乐亲戚之情话，允之。张君迫促速移，上下皆有怨言，若不闻也，督催益急。至九日，母尚在旧宅督理，张突负而趋，言勿惊老母者再。甫至戚家，喘息未定，人报左邻火发，延及张宅，顷刻荡然。而张氏之器用财贿无伤也。然后怨者德之。母与兄曰：「何不先言？」张曰：「天机不可预泄，然与先言何异耶？」

    Brother said, "This house is the inheritance of our ancestors, and we have lived here for over a hundred years, enjoying ample clothing and food, with the family members living in peace and safety. What is not good about it, and why do you want to rely on relatives' homes, which would not be criticized by others? Moreover, moving the house is not easy, so do not talk too much." Despite repeated pleas, the eldest brother and his wife insisted it was not possible. Zhang then pleaded with his mother, saying, "If we do not move within ten days, I will be a great unfilial son. I will surely be blamed by heaven and suffer misfortune." His mother, who had always loved and pitied him, saw his state of anxiety and urgency, which was out of utmost sincerity, and instructed the eldest son to move. Under the pressure of his mother's command, Zhang went to see his relatives and asked to stay at their home. The relatives indeed criticized him, but their house was spacious and had few people, so he enjoyed the intimate conversations with relatives and agreed to it. Zhang urged everyone to move quickly, and everyone, from top to bottom, had complaints, but he ignored them and urged them more urgently. By the ninth day, the mother was still at the old house overseeing the move, and Zhang suddenly carried her and hurriedly went, repeatedly saying not to frighten the old mother. As soon as he arrived at the relatives' home, he was still breathing heavily, and someone reported that the neighbor's house on the left was on fire, which spread to Zhang's house in a moment, and everything was destroyed. But Zhang's household items and wealth were unharmed. Then those who had complained were grateful. The mother and the eldest brother asked, "Why didn't you speak earlier?" Zhang said, "The heavenly secret cannot be revealed in advance, but what is the difference from speaking earlier?"

    Not long after, Zhang fell ill, and his condition worsened daily.     　　妖人邢大
    　　燕人邢大，幼失怙恃。年十七，艳丽过好女，因无事业，偃蹇不堪。里有洪大者，家小康。有龙阳之癖，亦无父母妻子。途遇邢，目逆而送之曰：「此天下尤物，可遇而不可求者。」尾至其家，见隤垣败室，虚寂无人，入门唁之。邢见洪来，羞涩之态，亦若女子之初见良人者。洪讯得困苦状，不胜怜悯曰：「弟若肯随至家，我能温饱之。」邢本无能，腆然随去。洪为置鲜衣，给美食，抚养周至，邢实心感。

    A strange person named Xing Da, a man from Yan, lost his parents at a young age. At seventeen, he was more beautiful than a good woman.     A Man Named Liu Liu

    Once there was a man named Liu Liu, who was also a handsome fellow. Hong and Liu Liu became sworn brothers, and Hong often brought Liu Liu home to meet his sister, Xing. When they met, Hong would say, "This is my sister." Liu Liu found Xing to be beautiful and fell in love with her. Hong had romantic intentions toward Xing, but Xing refused. Therefore, every time Liu Liu saw Xing, she would greet him with a formal bow and then leave, leaving Liu Liu with no recourse. When Hong was on his deathbed, Liu Liu proposed marriage to Xing with a substantial dowry. Hong and Xing discussed the matter, saying, "I am too sick to recover. Now that you have been living as a woman for some time, your appearance and demeanor are that of a beautiful lady. We originally planned to marry, but you abandoned me halfway through. If you continue to pretend to be a man, you cannot remain faithful to me. If you return to your male identity, you will lose the life you have built as a woman, and without knowing the ways of a man, you will likely starve to death, and I will be responsible for your fate. Even if you have no resentment, I will not find peace in the afterlife. It is better for you to marry Liu Liu. I can use the dowry to properly prepare for my funeral, and you will also find a suitable place in life."

    The Playful Judgment of Xiang Yan:

    Upon investigation, it is found that Xing possesses the elegance of the Song Dynasty, while Hong harbors the heart of Wei Ling. Sharing my remaining peach, the affection is harmonious as if we were united in marriage; in return for his cutting off his sleeve, why not allow us to share the same bed forever? If one temporarily removes their hat and robes to don a hairstyle, such occurrences may happen from time to time; but to permanently discard one's attire and adopt a feminine identity, such a thing is rare in ancient times. Creating new laws for a reckless youth should result in divine punishment; allowing a former favorite to return to their previous state and indulge in extraordinary emotions. As for Liu Liu, who has clearly distinguished between male and female, he should unleash a thunderous fury, yet how could he end up swapping genders and pursuing the ability to turn the sky and rain upside down? He is a man, and I am a man; male and female are complementary and equal. Actions have consequences, and what one does to others will come back to them, with rewards and punishments reciprocating. From now on, if one hides in the women's quarters, the law can still be avoided; but to boldly display unusual behavior in public, such actions are unforgivable. Those who deviate from the norm should be treated as heretics and executed by hanging; those who follow should be assigned to serve as slaves and sent to a remote and undesirable place. This is the judgment.

    补明武宗遗事(三则)
    　　正德二年丁卯秋，大比之年，士子云集。星卜之流，皆在前门营趁。有相士自命许（名负）、管（名辂）之能，凡朝官微服而来，一见即能指其现居品级，系何出身，历试无误，是以就相者众。帝知之，亦微服在人丛中观听。时八月初八日午刻，突一士人吼奔而来，扯扭相士曰：「汝误我功名，当与汝性命相搏。」众为排解不开。帝使卫士分之，入问何如此急急。相士曰：「是人前数日来问功名，我以今科解元许彼，自不入场，反赖我误之，真书呆也。」士人曰：「因汝以元许我，亲朋预作贺筵，饮入醉乡，家人唤醒入场，门已闭矣。

    Supplementing the Lost Tales of Emperor Wu of the Ming Dynasty (Three Anecdotes)
    In the autumn of the second year of the Zhengde era (1507), the year of the imperial examinations, scholars gathered in large numbers. Fortune-tellers and astrologers were all present at the front gate, seeking to profit from the crowd. There was a fortune-teller who claimed to possess the abilities of Xu (Fù) and Guan (Lù), famous fortune-tellers of the past. Whenever officials came incognito, he could immediately identify their current rank, their background, and their past experiences without error, which is why so many sought his services. The emperor, aware of this, also came incognito to observe the scene. On the eighth day of the eighth month at noon, a sudden commotion occurred as a scholar rushed forward, grabbing and twisting the fortune-teller and shouting, "You have ruined my chances of success! I will fight you to the death for this!" The crowd tried to intervene but could not resolve the dispute. The emperor ordered his guards to separate them and asked the scholar why he was so agitated. The fortune-teller explained, "This man came here a few days ago to ask about his prospects. I told him he would be the top scorer in this year's examination. He didn't show up, and now he blames me for his failure—what a bookworm!" The scholar replied, "Because you told me I would be the top scorer, my friends and relatives prepared a celebratory banquet. I drank myself into a stupor, and when my family woke me up to enter the examination hall, the gate was already closed."

    岂有场外解元哉？非汝误我而谁？」二人争执不休，帝曰：「无哗，使有人送渠入场，不得发解，汝认何罚？」相士曰：「挖我眸子去。」帝曰：「言出无悔。」即取案上纸笔书条，钤以身佩小玺，命卫士送去。帝谓相士曰：「半月后，来验汝言也。」相士知机，唯唯而遁。当卫士送士人至场外，传鼓称圣旨降，门官揭封去锁，内即传点开门，偕士人直入。至公堂，知贡举各官跪接，卫士面南宣读毕，即去复命。御史捡卷，恭送士人入号。内外哄传皇帝送朋友进场，主考亦留心阅卷，见其文亦尚稳妥，与各官公议皆曰：「此公既为当今识拔，不可作第二人，以拂上意。」竟中解元。试官复命，力奖其文才出众，贺帝得人。帝大笑曰：「命也，命也。」盖帝本欲使入场而不取，以难相士。因豹房新得美人，恋色而忘后命。今竟发解，益觉相士可异。着锦衣卫追寻，杳不知其所之矣。

    In the year of Wu's imperial examination, the emperor also wore a sword on his waist, dressed in the attire of a warrior, and roamed the marketplace. At the time, the emperor reviewed the case and ordered the interrogation of the accused in the imperial court. Han Lao cried out his innocence, and the emperor smiled and said, "You truly have a great injustice." The emperor asked who had presided over this case, and the Minister of Rites replied with the name of a certain Magistrate. The emperor ordered the guards to remove Han Lao's restraints and pointed to the Magistrate, saying, "I am the killer. You forced someone to confess falsely, and there are countless unjust and excessive cases in prison. Now I will use you as a substitute, and I will slightly appease the anger of the many wronged souls." The Magistrate defended himself by saying that the murder weapon came from Han Lao and was not without evidence. The emperor ordered the scabbard to be brought, and it fit perfectly, so the Magistrate confessed. Han Lao was then released and rewarded with a hundred gold pieces. The emperor said, "This compensates for your expenses." Furthermore, the emperor ordered that this year's executions be suspended and that capable Censors be selected to form a special commission named "Xu Xing" (恤刑). They were to travel to various provinces to review cases and confirm them before reporting approval, and indeed, many wrongful convictions were overturned.

    芗厈曰：观上三则，游戏中确有主裁，但好行小慧，为儒尚且不可，况九五之尊耶？今之读史者，直以帝比之桀纣，无乃过甚。当初谥曰武宗毅皇帝，毅者果决之谓，可见遇事实能决断，非尽阿谀可知矣。
    　
    　　通州吏目
    　　乾隆间，纯皇帝东巡，直隶各官，照例备供给。光天化日之中，诸凡顺遂，惟此差最难均平。盖随驾官员，皆循情理，独太监一项，或重支，或冒支，或以好作歹，挠搅不休。意在饮食之外，其内廷供奉，有执事监，名二十八他他者，俱在御前行走，皆得用人也。其时支应局总理，系通州剌史，协理者，即其吏目，发放一切酒筵，及例支饭食，皆按照旧章，井井有条。内监亦照例支讫矣。忽有十余人云自他他处来，索食甚侈。

Initially, he was posthumously given the title Emperor Wu of the Resolute, "resolute" being the term for decisiveness, showing that when faced with situations, he could make decisive judgments, not fully understood by flattery alone.

    Tongzhou Clerical Official
    During the reign of Emperor Qianlong, the pure emperor toured the east, the officials of Zhili Province, as usual, prepared supplies. In the bright daylight, everything went smoothly, except for this task, which was the hardest to distribute fairly. The officials accompanying the emperor all followed the rules, but the eunuchs, on the other hand, sometimes overclaimed, sometimes falsely claimed, or acted improperly, causing endless trouble. Beyond the food and drink, the inner court had attendants, known as the Twenty-Eight "Ta Ta," who all walked before the emperor and could use people. At that time, the head of the supply department was the governor of Tongzhou, and the assistant was the clerical official, who distributed all the banquets and regular meals according to the old rules, everything was well-organized. The eunuchs also received their allotted supplies according to the established rules. Suddenly, more than ten people claimed to come from the "Ta Ta" and demanded an excessive amount of food.

    The Medical Monk of Jinshan Temple

    A scholar-official from Zhejiang, accompanied by friends, was traveling to the capital for the imperial examinations. When the boat reached Suzhou, the scholar-official fell ill. His companions summoned a carriage to take him to the home of the famous physician Ye Tianshi for treatment. After examining him for a long time, Ye said, "Your illness is due to a cold, and one medicine will cure it. But where are you going?" The scholar-official replied that he was going to the metropolitan examination. Ye said, "Sir, you should rest. Once you leave the boat and go ashore, you will certainly contract diabetes, which cannot be cured, and you will not live more than a month. The pulse signs are already present. Return home quickly; there is still time to prepare for the afterlife." He then prescribed medicine for him and instructed his disciples to record it in the medical casebook. The scholar-official returned to the boat, weeping in distress, and decided to return home. His companions said, "This is the physician's way of scaring people to make money. Besides, Ye is just a contemporary physician and certainly not a divine being; why should you be so concerned?" The next day, the scholar-official took the medicine and indeed recovered. His companions encouraged him even more, and he continued northward, but his heart was filled with sorrow. When the boat reached the river mouth, the wind was against them, and they could not cross. The companions suggested visiting Jinshan Temple. Outside the temple gate, there was a sign for a medical monk. The scholar-official visited the meditation room, and the monk examined him, saying, "Where are you going, sir?" The scholar-official replied that he was going for the imperial examinations. The monk frowned and said, "I fear it is too late."

    此去登陆，消渴即发，寿不过月，奈何远行耶？」孝廉泣下曰：「诚如叶天士言矣。」僧曰：「天土言何？」孝廉曰：「无药可救。」僧曰：「谬哉，药如不能救病，圣贤何必留此一道？」孝廉觉其语有因，跽而请救。僧援之曰：「君登陆时，王家营所有者，秋梨也。以后车满载，渴即以梨代茶，饥则蒸梨作膳。约此物食过百觔，即无恙。焉得云无药可救，误人性命耶。」孝廉再拜而退。行抵清河，舍舟登陆，果渴病大作矣。如僧言，饮食必以梨，至都平服如故。入闱不售，感僧活命恩，回至金山，以二十金及都中方物为谢。僧收物而却其金曰：「居士过苏城时，再见叶君，令其诊视。如云无疾，即以前言质之。彼如问治疗之人，即以老僧告之，胜于厚惠也。

If medicine cannot cure diseases, why would sages and virtuous men have left such a path?" The scholar felt that the monk's words had merit and knelt to ask for help. The monk grasped his hand and said, "When you disembark, the only thing available at Wangjiayang is autumn pears. After that, load your carriage with them. When thirsty, use the pears as tea; when hungry, steam the pears to make a meal. If you consume about one hundred pounds of this, you will be fine. How can one say there is no cure, misleading people's lives?" The scholar bowed twice and then left. Upon reaching Qinghe, he disembarked, and indeed, the symptoms of diabetes worsened. Following the monk's advice, he used pears for both thirst and hunger, and upon arriving in the capital, he was as healthy as before. He failed in the imperial examinations and, grateful for the monk's life-saving kindness, returned to Jinshan to offer twenty gold pieces and local delicacies as thanks. The monk accepted the gifts but declined the gold, saying, "When you pass through Suzhou, visit Ye Jun again and have him examine you. If he says there is no illness, verify my previous advice. If he asks about the healer, mention the old monk, as it is more valuable than a generous gift."

    　　张廉访
    　　津门档子班主，以钱十余缗，买张姓童子，貌俊而性敏。教之歌，不数月，观听者莫不叫绝。但张故旧家子，父母俱没，为堂兄所掠卖，身习贱业，心中不甘。然年仅十二，不能逋逃也。售班至正定郡，寓土地祠，夜梦锦衣绣裳天使降，从者呼土地接天符，见殿内老翁伏地听命。使者曰：「帝命布疫，授一册一囊，命散药祠中，以收数内之人。」翁叩首曰：「小神庙内，寓张臬使，不应遭殃，何以安顿？」天使曰：「速引之出，而后从事可也。」言毕，冉冉腾云去。

    Zhang Lianfang, the head of a performing troupe in Tianjin, bought a handsome and intelligent boy named Zhang with several strings of cash. The old man pointed out the way, and they ran with great effort. At dawn, they entered a city, and when asked, the people said it was Ling County. Exhausted, Zhang could not go further and lay down at the gate of a large house. Not long after, an old man came out and saw the child tiredly sleeping, looking very healthy and vigorous. He was moved to pity him. He woke the child up and asked where he came from. Zhang knelt and wept, saying, "I am a man named Zhang from Tianjin. Both my parents have passed away. My elder brother wanted to sell me to join a troupe, out of fear, I fled and begged my way here. If the honorable person shows compassion, I am willing to be a servant."

    201

    」翁曰：「儿与老夫同姓，既有志不愿作档班，岂可为僮仆？速从我来，有以处子。」呼其子出，曰：「此儿有志向上，后必有为。汝其子之。」其子曰：「此人来历不明，且已行丐，儿不愿有此下贱子也。」翁怒曰：「汝不欲耶，我子之，汝其弟之。」乃引入室，见其爱妾曰：「汝素日以无子为戚，今为汝得一佳儿矣。」命张拜为亲母，妾乐而抚之。翁使入学读书，既勤且敏，五年而学成。文笔清灵，一试入泮，年仅十七。翁为之娶妇分家，亲子得其六，螟蛉得其四。乃兄敢怒而不敢言。

    Explanation

    201

    The old man said, "The child shares the same surname as me. Having already resolved not to become a servant, how could he be made a servant? Come quickly with me, I have a plan for you." He called his son out and said, "This child is ambitious and will surely achieve something in the future. You should adopt him as your own." His son replied, "This person's background is unclear, and he has already been begging. I do not want to have such a lowly child." The old man became angry and said, "If you do not want him, I will adopt him, and you will be his brother." He then brought him into the room and introduced him to his beloved concubine, saying, "You have always been troubled by not having a son, now I have found you a fine son." He ordered the child to kneel and address her as his mother, and the concubine happily took care of him. The old man sent him to school to study, and he was both diligent and quick-witted, completing his studies in five years. His writing was clear and elegant, and he passed the imperial examination at the age of seventeen. The old man arranged for him to marry and set up a household, giving him six of his own children and four adopted ones. His elder brother dared to be angry but did not dare to speak out.

    202

    未几翁卒，乃兄以异姓乱宗告逐。幸父党及张之同学诸生，辩非异姓，系其父爱继。官怒其兄曰：「汝父尸骨未寒，即欲逐其爱子，以不孝论。」欲重责之。张为哀求，官以张情，断令各安其业。张知日久必不见容，随携受分之物，奉嗣母入都。时前明中叶，大珰王振用事，张以赂结。珰谕张，使以张名贡入成均，肄业期满，选得中州某县丞，益媚事珰，不十年，官至廉访使。值土木之变，王振死，失所依，忆昔土地奏臬使之言，知官止于是矣。引疾归，置业津门，优游林下，又十余年而卒。
    　　芗厈曰：惜乎，张廉访之为人，虽脱其身，究不能脱档子气，故媚事大珰，以奔竞功名。若有贤父兄教之，得为正人君子，既命应廉访，终必至此地位，益为后人所景仰，岂仅为档子出色耶？

    Explanation

    202

    Not long after the old man died, Zhang's brother accused him of disrupting the family lineage by marrying into another clan and demanded his expulsion. Fortunately, Zhang's father's relatives and fellow students came to his aid, arguing that Zhang was not of a different surname and was actually the father's beloved adopted son. The official became angry with Zhang's brother, saying, "Your father's body has not yet turned to dust, and you are already trying to expel his beloved son, which is akin to filial impiety." The official wanted to severely punish the brother. Zhang pleaded on behalf of his brother, and the official, considering Zhang's plea, decided to let everyone return to their respective occupations. Zhang realized he would eventually be expelled and thus took what was given to him and accompanied his stepmother to the capital. During the middle period of the previous Ming dynasty, the powerful eunuch Wang Zhen held sway. Zhang bribed Wang Zhen, who instructed Zhang to enter the Imperial Academy under his name. After completing his studies, Zhang was selected as a county magistrate in a certain county in Central China. He further flattered Wang Zhen and within ten years rose to the position of Censorate Inspector. During the Tumu Crisis, Wang Zhen died, leaving Zhang without support. Zhang recalled the words of the land official who had advised him about the limits of his position. He feigned illness to return home, established a residence in Tianjin, lived a leisurely life in retirement, and passed away after more than ten years.

    Xiang Yan commented: It is a pity that Zhang, the Censorate Inspector, despite rising to a high position, could not escape the influence of his lowly origins. Therefore, he flattered the eunuch to achieve fame and fortune. If Zhang had been taught by virtuous parents and brothers, he could have become a virtuous and upright person, and his eventual rise to the position of Censorate Inspector would have been even more admirable. How could he have been merely outstanding among those of low status?

    某少君
    　　少君某，年十七，能诗文而未遇，翩翩美少年也。父以科甲铨得四川县令，少君随任。行至羊肠阪，马逸，颠落崖下，身糜而魂出，随风飘荡，瞬息数千里，求止不得。忽堕于山东历城县村落间，初死男尸壳中，大叫曰：「跌死我也。」见妇与童围绕身旁者，皆止哭曰：「苏矣。」一老媪曰：「气绝逾日，如何得醒？」随有二三父老近身细审曰：「气暖身和，复生无疑。」一家庆幸，频闻欢乐声。媪前抚之曰：「我儿何云跌死，曷为我言之。」少君睁目曰：「汝何人，敢儿我？」父老笑曰：「渠虽少苏，神尚未完。此汝母，如何不识？」又指一丑妇曰：「此汝妻。」指一村童曰：「此汝子，皆识否？」少君起坐曰：「谬甚！谬甚！我某公子，随父莅任。行蜀道上，堕马，被风吹至此。

    A Young Gentleman

    A young gentleman named Meng, aged seventeen, was skilled in poetry and prose but had not yet achieved recognition; he was a graceful and handsome youth. His father obtained the position of county magistrate in Sichuan through the imperial examination system, and Meng accompanied him. Traveling to the winding and difficult mountain pass known as Yangchangban, the horse ran away, and Meng fell off the cliff, his body destroyed and soul departed, drifting with the wind for thousands of miles in an instant, unable to find a place to rest. Suddenly, he found himself in a village in Licheng County, Shandong, inside the shell of a recently deceased male body. He shouted loudly, "I fell and died!" The woman and children around him all stopped crying and said, "He has revived!" An old woman remarked, "His breath had ceased for more than a day; how could he have woken up?" A few elder men approached to examine him closely and said, "His breath is warm and his body is harmonious; there is no doubt that he has revived." The whole family rejoiced, and joyful sounds were frequently heard. The old woman gently touched him and asked, "My son, how could you say you fell and died? Why don't you tell me?" Meng opened his eyes and said, "Who are you, dare to call me your son?" The elder men laughed and said, "He has slightly revived, but his spirit is not yet fully restored. This is your mother; how could you not recognize her?" They then pointed to an unattractive woman and said, "This is your wife," and to a village boy and said, "This is your son. Do you recognize them all?" Meng sat up and said, "How absurd! How absurd! I am the son of someone, traveling with my father to take up his post. Traveling on the road to Sichuan, I fell off my horse and was blown by the wind to this place."

    204

    并未娶妻，焉得有子？且我母乃诰命孺人，村妪何得冒认？」父老曰：「休呓语，汝不信，可以镜自照。」少君对镜，四十余岁之麻胡也。不禁扑镜大哭曰：「还我本来面目，我愿死，不愿生矣。」父老粲然皆笑，老媪曰：「谅我儿初醒，神尚模糊，诸公勿扰之，儿静养数日，自然复原。」众散去，少君拥衾，垂首丧气，无如饥肠作辘辘声，丑妇以半规糠饼饲之，粗粝难食，勉强吞咽，泪涔涔下。丑妇曰：「我与阿姑守君十余日，已绝粮三四日，仅食槐皮野菜耳。以君初复，需调养，忍耻向邻人乞得此饼，亦大人情。君犹以为不足耶？」少君大声叱之出。目睹败屋三椽，土炕上所拥者，破衾败絮蓝缕衣裤一堆，厨灶亦在房中，气息秽不可耐。因思居厦屋，役奴仆，衣罗绮，食膏粱，判若天渊。怦怦懊恼，求死不得。至晚妻儿皆来就宿，少君又大叱之，闻老媪唤其妇与孙去。

    Explanation

    204

    Since he has not married, how could he have a son? And my mother is a high-ranking lady, how could a village woman claim such a title?" The elders said, "Stop your nonsense. If you don't believe us, look in the mirror." The young master looked in the mirror and saw a disheveled man in his forties. He could not help but hit the mirror and cried out, "Restore my original appearance. I wish to die rather than live." The elders laughed heartily, and the old woman said, "My son just woke up and his mind is still fuzzy. Please do not disturb him. Let him rest for a few days, and he will naturally recover." After the crowd dispersed, the young master hugged his quilt, hung his head in dejection, but his empty stomach growled. The ugly woman gave him a half-circular cake made of bran and grits, which was coarse and difficult to eat. He swallowed it勉强, tears flowing continuously. The ugly woman said, "I and your mother have been taking care of you for over ten days. We have been without food for three to four days, eating only wild vegetables and tree bark. Since you just recovered, you need to rest and recuperate. I endured shame to beg for this cake from our neighbors, which is also a gesture of goodwill. Do you still think it's not enough?" The young master shouted at her to leave. He saw a dilapidated house with three beams, a pile of tattered bedding and clothes on the earthen kang, and the kitchen was also inside the same room. The air was foul and unbearable. He thought of living in a grand house, having servants, wearing fine clothes, and eating rich food, which was as different as heaven and earth. He felt agitated and annoyed, wishing to die but unable to do so. By evening, his wife and children came to stay for the night, and the young master shouted at them again, hearing the old woman call her daughter-in-law and grandson to leave.

    205

    次日，邻翁来殷懃问候曰：「吾与君至交也，闻君病小痊，性情大变，亲母妻子，视若寇仇，恐乡党不能容此不孝不义之人也。将来亲戚不齿，邻里不顾，君又贫困，何以仰事俯育以终乃身乎？用敢奉劝。」少君泣曰：「承翁美意，请辨我语言，是足下好友之音乎？」翁曰：「人是音非，吾固知君借尸返魂也。今既为某人矣，得不为某人之事乎？譬如仕官，本督抚也，降为杂职，能不安杂职之分而从其政乎？君即舍此而就尊公，面目既非，纵怜而育之，他人必不相容。」少君思其言中理，曰：「翁所教良是。后将若何？」翁曰：「母其母，子其子，仍营趁以自食其力，承此一家，以了此躯而已。」少君曰：「我前生读书作文，曾应童试，营趁之事，一无所能，奈何？」翁曰：「能如是乎。请为君游扬闾里，以训童蒙。亦自食其力之一道也。

    Explanation

    205

    The next day, the elderly neighbor came with sincere greetings and said, "I have been a close friend of yours, and I hear that your illness has slightly improved, but your character has greatly changed. You now regard your mother, wife, and children as enemies, and I fear that the village will not be able to tolerate such an ungrateful and unjust person. In the future, your relatives will hold you in contempt, and your neighbors will ignore you. You are also poor; how can you support your parents and raise your children to live out your life? I dare to offer my advice." The younger man wept and said, "I appreciate your kind intentions, please clarify my words. Is this the voice of your good friend?" The old man replied, "The person is the same, but the voice is different. I know you have been reborn. Now that you are this person, can you not act as this person should? It is like being an official; originally a governor or provincial inspector, but now reduced to a minor official, can one not act according to the duties of a minor official? If you abandon this situation and return to your father, your appearance will be different, and even if they feel pity and take care of you, others will definitely not tolerate it." The younger man thought his words were reasonable and said, "Your teachings are indeed correct. What should I do afterward?" The old man said, "Be the mother to your mother, the son to your son, continue to earn a living to support yourself, and take care of this family to complete this life." The younger man said, "In my past life, I read and wrote essays, and even took the children's examination, but I am completely incapable of earning a living. What should I do?" The old man said, "Can you do that? Please allow me to teach children in the neighborhood. It is also a way to earn one's own living."

    206

    」少君起谢之。翁为布告乡党，人素知某为佣保，目不识丁，忽闻一病而能诗文，远近好奇之士，咸来共语。少君引经据典，侃侃而谈，众皆悦服，从游者甚众。所得修脯，以养一家，绰有余裕。但少君自授徒后，借居古庙，竟不归家。母来谈论，格格不入，妻子更不顾而问矣。然得温饱，皆乐而安之。未几，赴试，旋入学为名诸生。有客入蜀，少君作禀告乃翁。大令奇其事，寄资作札，招之使去。少君前生本行三，因其聪敏俊秀，父母偏爱之。上有两兄，皆不得意。后闻其堕马死，父母衰恸而两兄窃喜。今又闻其来也，皆惧。及相晤，其貌不扬，父甚狐疑，两兄直叱为妄冒，母亦不认。少君历举幼时游戏事，及父母秘密之言，委曲道达。父虽垂怜，而母与两兄决意逐之。父知必不见容，私与千金，遣归山左，家以小康。谈者曰：此人现在，后不知作何结局矣。

    Explanation

    206

    少君起身致谢。老翁在乡里传播了消息，人们原本只知道某人是个佣工，目不识丁，突然听说他因病痊愈后能写诗作文，远近的好奇人士都纷纷前来与他交谈。少君引用经典，侃侃而谈，众人无不心悦诚服，跟随他学习的人很多。他所获得的学费足以养活一家人，绰绰有余。然而，少君自从开始教授学生后，便借住在古庙中，不再回家。母亲前来与他交谈，但双方格格不入，妻子更是不闻不问。尽管如此，他们还是得到了温饱，都感到快乐和满足。不久，少君参加考试，很快便成为有名的学生。有客人前往四川，少君写信禀告他的父亲。那位大令对这件事感到非常惊奇，寄送钱财并写信邀请少君离开。少君前世本是家中的第三个儿子，因为聪明俊秀，受到父母的偏爱。他有两个哥哥，都不如意。后来听说少君因马失前蹄而死，父母悲痛欲绝，两个哥哥却暗自欢喜。如今又听说少君回来了，他们都感到害怕。见面时，少君相貌平平，父亲非常怀疑，两个哥哥直接斥责他是冒充的，母亲也不承认他。少君历数童年游戏的事迹，以及父母的秘密话语，详细地讲述。父亲虽然怜悯他，但母亲和两个哥哥坚决要赶他走。父亲知道他们必定不会接纳他，便私下给了他一千金，让他返回山东，家境因此变得小康。人们议论说：此人现在如何，将来又会有什么结局呢？

    207

    或曰：「异哉，少君之一跌，既未入幽冥，又不经神判，以翩翩佳公子，顿变而为窭人，何异于膴仕之投荒者。造化弄人至此极矣。」芗厈曰：「此不弟之显罚也。观其后之不见容于乃兄，即可见前之乃兄受侮不少。若使再世得报，人皆不知。直以现身作法，以示鉴于人伦。谚云，一失足成千古恨，再回头已百年身。为少君诵矣。」

    Explanation

    207

    Someone said: "Strange indeed! Young Master's fall, neither entering the underworld nor undergoing divine judgment, transformed the graceful young nobleman into a poor man. How is this different from a wealthy official being exiled? Fate has played with people to this extreme."

    Xiang Yan said: "This is a clear punishment for a younger brother. Seeing how he was not accepted by his elder brother, one can see that his elder brother was greatly humiliated. If he were to seek revenge in another life, no one would know. It is better to live and serve as an example, to show a lesson in human relationships. The saying goes, 'One misstep can lead to regret for a thousand years, and turning back will make you feel like you have lived a hundred lives.' This is for Young Master to reflect upon."

    许宗伯
    　　吾乡许大宗伯，讳汝霖。幼失怙恃，终鲜兄弟，室如悬罄，地无立锥。依寺僧训蒙度日，每闻僧作法事归，必聚论人家字画。有云堂幅好者，有云单条佳者，有云横披更妙者，有云楹联出色者，争论不一。间有戚友延僧，宅中实无字画，而论者如故。公大疑，访诸其徒。徒哂曰：「彼所论非真字画，凡请持经之家，妇女不避。我等得以纵观，归而各诩目力，以隐语评之。所云堂幅者，其家正妻，横披者妾，单条者女，楹联者婢也。我不敢在师前隐讳，然师亦不可为外人道也。」公深恨之而无如何。嗣应试，屡冠童子军，苦不得售。年将而立，无与论婚者。

    Explanation

    208

    A Man of Letters

    Mr. Xu, the Grand Secretary of our hometown, whose courtesy name was Rulin, lost his parents at a young age and had no brothers. His house was as empty as a suspended bell, and he had no land to stand on. He relied on a temple monk to teach him basic literacy for a living. Every time the monk returned from performing religious rituals, they would always gather to discuss the paintings and calligraphy of others. Someone would say that a scroll was good, someone would say that a hanging scroll was excellent, someone would say that a horizontal hanging scroll was even more wonderful, and someone would say that a couplet was outstanding. There were no consistent opinions. Sometimes relatives and friends would invite the monk, and there were no paintings or calligraphy in the house, but the discussion continued as before. Mr. Xu was greatly puzzled and asked his disciples. The disciples laughed and said, "What they were discussing was not actual paintings or calligraphy. Families that invited monks to hold scriptures did not avoid them. We were able to observe everything, and upon returning, we boasted about our eyesight, using coded language to evaluate them. The scroll referred to the main wife of the family, the horizontal hanging scroll referred to a concubine, the hanging scroll referred to a daughter, and the couplet referred to a servant. We dare not hide this from our master, but the master should not tell outsiders either." Mr. Xu deeply resented this but could do nothing about it. Later, he took the examination and often won the top position in the children's examination, but he struggled to pass the higher examinations. By the age of thirty, no one wanted to discuss marriage with him.

    209

    乡有葭莩亲，以耕读为业，时全家患疫，惟一女无恙。戚翁静卧床，中夜，闻众鬼议曰：「明日许宗伯来视疾，我曹避何处？」一鬼曰：「翁床下大瓮，聚处其中，亦可暂避一时耳。」皆应曰可。是日，公闻戚病，果来探视。翁见公，大悦，使其女奉以馔甚丰。公不安欲去。翁跃起曰：「有事烦君，看老夫薄面，万不可辞。」公食毕，请所事，翁曰：「请以纸，朱书『大宗伯封』四字，封老夫床下瓮口，举而投诸河，即感盛德矣。」公不解其意，笑从之，为弃瓮归。病者果痊愈。翁益喜，遣媒以女订婚。年齿皆长，急须聘娶。翁为公作大布衣冠，草草成礼。

    Explanation

    209

    In a village, there lived a distant relative who engaged in farming and reading. One day, the entire family fell ill with an epidemic, except for one daughter who remained unharmed. The old man, lying quietly in bed, heard the ghosts discussing at midnight: "Tomorrow, the Master of the Imperial Academy Xu Zongbo will come to visit the illness. Where should we hide?" One ghost replied, "Under the old man's bed is a large jar. We can gather inside it and temporarily hide for a while." All agreed that it was possible.

    The next day, Xu Zongbo heard that the relative was ill and came to visit. The old man saw Xu Zongbo and was delighted, ordering his daughter to serve a very abundant meal. Xu Zongbo felt uneasy and wanted to leave. The old man suddenly jumped up and said, "There is something I need your help with. For the sake of my old face, you must not refuse."

    After finishing the meal, Xu Zongbo asked what the matter was. The old man said, "Please write the four characters 'Grand Master of the Imperial Academy' in red ink on a piece of paper, seal the mouth of the large jar under my bed, lift it, and throw it into the river. Then you will have shown your great kindness."

    Xu Zongbo was puzzled but followed the instructions, leaving the jar in the river. The sick person indeed recovered. The old man was even more delighted and sent a matchmaker to arrange a marriage for his daughter. Both of their ages were advanced, and they urgently needed to arrange the marriage. The old man prepared a simple robe and hat for Xu Zongbo, and they hastily completed the wedding ceremony.

    210

    公无力备花烛，代以二油灯。其夫人恒曰：「妾每见取妇家，必彩舆、鼓乐、鸣炮，君今一事不备，岂非妾命累君耶？」公曰：「卿今羡此不得，恐异日闻之生厌耳。」夫人曰：「妾乐此不疲，何厌之有？」未几，公入泮，将应秋闱，无力买舟，惟趁夜航之便，行百里，不过数十钱。然无卧具者，例不准趁船。公谋诸僧，曰：「盍以敝毡裹两破蒲团，用充卧具，谁敢拒之。」公如法，趁船赴省。停泊时，舟子举其具掷岸上树间。公亦不顾，入茶肆，旋有驿卒乘骑至，亦系马树下。马饥，见破毡内有草，蹄而食之。群哗曰：「许爷行李被马吃矣。」公亦大笑而去。

    Explanation

    210

    The man had no means to prepare the wedding candles, so he substituted them with two oil lamps. His wife often said, "Whenever I see the wedding party of the bride's family, they always have decorated sedan chairs, music, and firecrackers. You have not prepared any of these things now. Isn't it because of my fate that you are burdened?" The man replied, "You cannot envy this now, but I fear that one day you will grow tired of hearing about it." The wife said, "I enjoy this without tiring, why would there be any weariness?" Soon after, the man passed the local examination and was about to take the provincial examination. He had no means to afford a boat, so he only took advantage of the night ferry, traveling a hundred miles for just a few dozen coins. However, those without bedding were not allowed to board the ship by rule. The man suggested to the monks, "Why don't we use old felt wrapped around two broken zafus as bedding? Who would dare refuse?" The man followed this suggestion and boarded the ship to go to the provincial capital. When the ship was moored, the boatman threw the bedding onto a tree on the shore. The man paid no attention and went into a teahouse. Soon after, a postal official arrived on horseback and also tied his horse to a tree. The horse was hungry and saw grass inside the old felt, trotted up and ate it. The crowd shouted, "The official's luggage has been eaten by the horse." The man also laughed and left.

    211

    后举孝廉，捷南宫，入词林，转春坊，由卿贰，外转方伯，旋晋中丞。中丞官廨限于地，横而长，上房距鼓亭炮台密迩，早晚鼓吹鸣炮，夫人不得安眠，谓公曰：「日日鼓乐，未免喧阗，盍命稍停乎？」公笑曰：「卿昔求之不得，今果厌烦耶？我所以日日为此者，非自鸣得意，所以补卿昔日之不足耳。今既足矣，从此收声，不仅稍停而已。」旋内召为大宗伯，妻封一品夫人。公卒时，遗教子孙，永不许延僧作佛事，违者以不孝论，实有憾于字画之说也。
    　　芗厈曰：许公未达时，可谓君子固穷。吾乡人至今称物之不堪者，曰「许老爷铺盖」。又曰：「许老爷鼓吹补你。」竟成谚语。至其文集，为国初名家政绩，足以上动圣明。不但能言之者少，即知之者亦稀，风俗之陋耶？

    Explanation

    211

    After being recommended as a孝廉, he successfully passed the imperial examinations, entered the imperial academy, and was later promoted to positions in the imperial court, high-ranking officials, provincial governors, and finally to the central government official. The residence of the central government official was limited in space, being long and narrow, with the main house very close to the drum tower and cannon platform. The daily sounds of music and cannon fire prevented the wife from sleeping, and she told the official, "The daily music and drumming are too noisy. Why not stop them for a while?" The official smiled and said, "You could not have it before, so now you are annoyed? I play the music and drumming every day not out of self-satisfaction, but to compensate for what you lacked in the past. Now that you have it, stop them completely, not just for a while." He was soon summoned to a high-ranking position as the chief official of rituals, and his wife was granted the title of First-Rank Lady. When the official died, he left instructions to his descendants, forbidding them from inviting monks for Buddhist rituals, with disobedience considered filial impiety. He had reservations about the idea of "字画" (calligraphy and painting).

    Xiang Yan said: "When Xu Gong was not yet successful, he could be called a gentleman who remained steadfast in poverty. People in his hometown still use the phrase 'Xu Lao Ye's bedding' to describe something of poor quality. They also say, 'Xu Lao Ye's music compensates for you.' These have become common sayings. As for his literary works, they are considered important contributions to the early Ming dynasty and could move the wise ruler. Few can articulate or understand their significance, and is this a sign of cultural decline?"

    212

    巧令(三则)
    　　有幕客攫其居停误征已免钱粮印簿，讹控者，状已上达，簿未呈堂。宪司咸以此人铁据在握，难以理断，其能者，不过私与往还，问其所欲，图赎其簿，销之而已。此人索数千金，不得丝毫缺。或云，即予千金，倘抱赃出首，中人亦连累无涯矣。皆窘于计。宪司会议时，有巧令在侧微笑。诘之，令曰：「若交职，三日办矣。」宪欣然委之，令携卷回，不动声色。至第三日，上下皆曰：「限期已到，尚未佥票，得毋误乎？」令曰：「予几忘之。」乃出，升公座，唤三班役来前曰：「有善斗殴者否？」众皆骇，莫敢应，一强项者出曰：「役能之。」令喜曰：「汝能，必知我意。今某处有幕客某寓，汝往生事激之斗。但许自伤，勿许伤人，受伤即来鸣冤，汝知之乎？」役曰唯。

    Explanation

    212

    A Clever Official (Three Tales)

    A guest (幕客) had seized the landlord's mistakenly collected tax exemption registration book (攫其居停误征已免钱粮印簿) and falsely accused someone (讹控者). The complaint had been submitted (状已上达), but the document had not yet been presented to the court (簿未呈堂). The constitutional officials (宪司) all believed that the person had solid proof (铁据在握) and found it difficult to resolve the case. The most capable officials could only meet privately (私与往还) with the person, ask what he wanted (问其所欲), and try to redeem the document and destroy it (图赎其簿，销之而已). The person demanded several thousand gold coins (索数千金), and if he were to confess and turn over the stolen goods (倘抱赃出首), the middle person would also be implicated without limit (中人亦连累无涯矣). All were in a difficult situation (皆窘于计).

    During the conference of the constitutional officials, there was a clever official (巧令) smiling. They questioned him, and he said, "If you give me the task, I can handle it in three days (若交职，三日办矣)." The constitutional officials gladly entrusted him with the case (宪欣然委之), and he carried the case file back without showing any emotion (令携卷回，不动声色). On the third day, everyone above and below said, "The deadline has passed, but the ticket has not yet been issued (限期已到，尚未佥票). Is it not a mistake (得毋误乎)?" The official replied, "I almost forgot (予几忘之)." He then ascended the official seat (升公座) and called the three ranks of officials forward (唤三班役来前曰), saying, "Is there a good fighter (有善斗殴者否)?" Everyone was startled (众皆骇), and none dared to respond (莫敢应). A strong-willed person came out (一强项者出曰) and said, "The official can do it (役能之)." The official was pleased (令喜曰) and said, "If you can, you must understand my intention (汝能，必知我意). Now there is a guest in a certain place (今某处有幕客某寓). Go and provoke a fight (汝往生事激之斗). Allow only self-injury, not injury to others (但许自伤，勿许伤人). If injured, come and complain (受伤即来鸣冤). Do you understand (汝知之乎)?" The official replied, "Yes (役曰唯)."

    213

    即赴客寓，向其人大呼曰：「汝从某县来，我载汝至此，今已逾月，所欠车价若干，速给我，不能再待矣。」客大怒曰：「我来时仆夫非汝，何来恶棍，敢肆讹诈！」役詈不已，客推之出，役即自伤其首回，县令未退堂，即呼冤入跪。正验伤，客亦衣冠至，以棍徒凭空讹诈具禀。役与争辩，令曰：「无哗，此易辨耳。汝既载客来，客行李若干，汝必知之。」令逐－报明核对，役不能知，妄报数物。客大笑，称令贤明。

    Explanation

    213

    The official immediately went to the guest's residence and shouted at him, saying, "You came from a certain county, I transported you here, it has been over a month, how much do you owe for the carriage fare? Give it to me quickly, I cannot wait any longer!" The guest became very angry and said, "When I came, the driver was not you, what kind of ruffian are you, daring to extort money?" The official kept cursing, and the guest pushed him out. The official immediately injured his own head and returned. The county magistrate had not yet left the court when the official called for a complaint and entered to kneel. While examining the injury, the guest also came in formal attire and filed a report accusing the ruffian of extorting money out of thin air. The official argued back, but the magistrate said, "Be quiet, this is easy to determine. Since you transported the guest here, how many items of the guest's luggage do you know?" The magistrate asked each item to be reported and verified, but the official could not know and falsely reported several items. The guest laughed and praised the magistrate as wise.

    214

    令问之，曰：「所报全非，自愿书单呈验。」令即饬书，带役数人往客寓，将行李捡来，当堂查验，与所书单无异。于行箧中搜得印簿，曰：「此系官文，何得私自携取？本应治罪，念汝尚属斯文，姑全颜面。」命取火焚之。客争曰：「案已上控，簿不可焚。」时人多手快，已成灰烬。令大笑曰：「汝肯讹人，无怪人来讹汝。天道好还，汝知之乎？第我治下，不容奸险之徒，即备文递回原籍可也。」客知据已毁，无能为，隐忍吞声而去。令即缴卷销案，宪司优奖之。

    Explanation

    214

    The magistrate asked him, and he replied, "The report was entirely false, and I willingly submitted a list for verification." The magistrate immediately ordered the clerk to take several officials to the guesthouse, where they collected his luggage and inspected it on the spot. Everything matched the submitted list. In his luggage, they found a seal book, and the magistrate said, "This is an official document. How could you take it privately? You should be punished according to the law, but considering you are still a scholar, I will save your face." He then ordered it to be burned with fire. The guest protested, "The case has already been reported to a higher authority. The book cannot be burned." But by the time he finished speaking, the document was already ashes. The magistrate laughed and said, "If you dare to deceive others, it's no wonder others deceive you. The way of heaven is to return things to their proper place. Do you know this? But in my jurisdiction, there is no room for deceitful and cunning people. You may be sent back to your hometown with a written notice." The guest knew the evidence was destroyed and could do nothing, so he silently bore the humiliation and left. The magistrate immediately submitted the report and closed the case, and the higher authority praised him highly.

    215

    有刘姓者，孤独少年，入赘李老家。李以其稚弱无能，虐之。刘不堪，潜投仕宦为仆，得主宠眷。数年，积金四百余，辞归，与其妻谋置产业。妻乃炫述于父母，李老生心，欣然设宴，为婿洗尘。誉而醉之，且曰：「汝妻年幼，交以多金，恐不胜任。况汝须外出谋事，以少妇居守，得无穿窬之虑乎？盍交老夫，权为收藏，可以无虑。」刘唯唯，出金点交，八宝十六件也。次日，刘酒醒而悔，亟向李老索银。李曰：「汝贫如丐，寄食我家，邻里咸知，焉得多金寄顿？不思为汝育妻恩，反肆讹耶？」其女助婿争论，李老大怒曰：「女生外向，真不可与处矣。」逐其夫妇出诸大门之外。刘冤忿兴讼，以妻为证。县令曰：「汝物无凭，妻不可以为证。汝妻父曰，女生外向，此言诚然。我不能直汝，毋干犯义之责也。」挥之退。刘素稔巧令名，往陈其苦，令曰：「隔境无能为力。」刘曰：「天下贤使君，惟有老爷，若不肯治理，则无官能明此狱矣。

    Explanation

    215

    A Man Named Liu

    There was a man named Liu, a lonely young man who entered his wife's family to live and work. His father-in-law, Li, mistreated him because he was young and weak. Liu could no longer endure the abuse and secretly took up service in a wealthy household as a servant, where he gained the favor of the master. After several years, he accumulated four hundred or more in silver and returned home, planning with his wife to establish a business. His wife boasted about this to her parents, and Li grew suspicious. He happily arranged a banquet to welcome his son-in-law and, while praising him, got him drunk and said, "Your wife is still young, and you've given her a large sum of money. She might not be able to manage it. Besides, you need to go out and seek your fortune, leaving a young wife to stay behind. Isn't there a risk of theft? Why not give the money to me to keep for safekeeping, so you won't have to worry?" Liu nodded in agreement and handed over the silver, which consisted of eight treasures in sixteen pieces. The next day, after waking up from the drink, Liu regretted his decision and urgently asked Li to return the silver. Li replied, "You're as poor as a beggar, living off our family, and the neighbors all know. How could you have so much money to entrust to me? Don't you think about the kindness of raising your wife, and instead make false claims?" His daughter supported her husband's argument, and Li became furious, saying, "Women are naturally inclined to be unfaithful, truly, they cannot be trusted." He then expelled the couple from the main gate. Liu filed a lawsuit out of resentment, using his wife as a witness. The magistrate said, "You have no proof of your claim, and your wife cannot be a witness. Your wife's father said that women are naturally unfaithful, and that is true. I cannot rule in your favor, or I would be risking a breach of duty." He dismissed them. Liu, known for his cleverness, went to present his case to a higher authority, and the magistrate said, "From afar, I cannot help. Liu replied, "The most virtuous magistrate in the world is only you. If you refuse to handle this case, no other official can clarify it."

    216

    」哀之切，令笑曰：「若必欲余明此讼，须暂禁囹圄，汝愿之否？」刘曰：「果能明此，虽刀杖加身，亦甘承受，况暂禁耶？」令即梏收之。乃移文县令曰：「日者获大盗张三，据供劫得某事主家银四百余两，若干锭件，寄顿贵县某村大窝主李老家，希即委员带捕，查起赃银，连窝主李老解质」云云。县令见系盗劫重情，即身自查抄，人赃并获，解交此令。乃涂刘面，衣以囚衣，械系于堂。呼李老诘之曰：「此囚供在某家劫银四百余两，八宝十六件，寄汝家，今所起赃数相符。

    Explanation

    216

    The magistrate, deeply sorrowful, smiled and said, "If you insist that I clarify this case, you must temporarily imprison him in jail. Are you willing?" Liu replied, "If you can indeed clarify this, even if beaten with a whip or rod, I will willingly endure it, much less a temporary imprisonment." The magistrate then handcuffed and detained him. He sent a letter to the county magistrate saying, "Yesterday, we captured a notorious bandit named Zhang San. According to his confession, he stole over 400 taels of silver and several ingots from a certain victim's home, and left the stolen goods with a notorious gang leader named Li Laohu in a village in your county. Please send officials immediately to capture and investigate the stolen goods, along with the gang leader Li Laohu, to be brought to trial." The county magistrate, seeing the serious nature of the theft, personally conducted the search and seizure, capturing both the person and the stolen goods, and handed them over to this magistrate. The magistrate then painted Liu's face, dressed him in prison clothes, and chained him in the courtroom. He called Li Laohu and questioned him, saying, "This prisoner confessed to stealing over 400 taels of silver and sixteen valuable items from a certain victim's home, and left them with you. The amount of stolen goods found matches the confession."

    汝为盗窝，罪干枭首，据实陈明，勿自庸三木也。」李老呼冤曰：「此银实系小人之婿刘某寄存者，闻其得自随官，是否属实，请拘刘某与张三质之，以明小人之冤。」令笑曰：「若见刘某，汝又将图赖矣。」李老曰：「与其冤诛，莫若明心。召刘某与张三质对，可见小人不知情，庶望一线生路，奚肯贪财舍命耶？」令曰：「若然，则刘某在是矣。」乃释其桎梏，使涤面易服相见。李大惭无词。令乃给还刘银，而薄责李曰：「余为留翁婿情也。」刘感激涕零而去，李亦从此悔过矣。

    Explanation

    217

    You are the elderly Li, accused of being a den of thieves and facing decapitation. You plead your innocence, claiming that the silver in question belongs to your son-in-law Li D, who obtained it from an official. You request that Li D and Zhang San be brought to confront you to clear your name. The magistrate, however, seems to suspect you of fabricating the case against Li D. You argue that it is better to be honest and face the truth rather than risk wrongful execution. The magistrate then releases Li D from his chains, has him wash his face and change clothes, and summons him to meet you. Li Da is ashamed and has no words to say. The magistrate returns the silver to Li D and lightly reprimands Li Da, explaining that he is sparing him out of respect for the father-son-in-law relationship. Li D is deeply grateful and sheds tears as he leaves, and Li Da repents from then on.

    Here is the final translation of the source text:

    You are the elderly Li, accused of being a den of thieves and facing decapitation. You plead your innocence, claiming that the silver in question belongs to your son-in-law Li D, who obtained it from an official. You request that Li D and Zhang San be brought to confront you to clear your name. The magistrate, however, seems to suspect you of fabricating the case against Li D. You argue that it is better to be honest and face the truth rather than risk wrongful execution. The magistrate then releases Li D from his chains, has him wash his face and change clothes, and summons him to meet you. Li Da is ashamed and has no words to say. The magistrate returns the silver to Li D and lightly reprimands Li Da, explaining that he is sparing him out of respect for the father-son-in-law relationship. Li D is deeply grateful and sheds tears as he leaves, and Li Da repents from then on.

    218

    某县尉与其大令有隙，面和而心违。一日在令账房闲话，见几上有入钱簿，内书某季收陋规若干，某役手，某案收钱若干，不一而足。尉俟令回首时，潜藏而退。令送客回，不见此簿，知入尉手矣。所载赃私累累，必受其讹，惶恐之至。函致巧令商之，复书曰：「慎勿言，见尉时谈笑如恒，若无事然，饬库书取银数百两，备文批解杂税，封贮账房柜内。签差翌日起解，夜于墙上钻穴而入，取回内署。次日即呼尉带捕来验，云是夜被窃杂税银若干，公文一角，入钱总簿一本。申明宪司，渠敢自露乎？」令如法行之，旋即通报，自请处分。尉知其心而不敢言，恐干重咎，将所藏之私簿暗毁矣。
    　　芗厈曰：彼诈而吾诈之，强中更有强中手。书曰：「诪张为幻。」至此，令人不可测而可笑。盖人情欺愚而畏智，是故惧讼者，讼即随之。若烛其奸又操其胜具，将不战而胜矣。

    Explanation

    218

    A county magistrate and his superior official had a conflict, though they appeared harmonious on the surface but harbored resentment inwardly. One day, while chatting idly in the superior's office, the magistrate noticed a ledger on the table, which recorded various irregular fees collected during certain seasons, handled by certain officials, and amounts collected from specific cases, with numerous entries. When the superior turned his head, the magistrate secretly took the ledger and withdrew. After sending off his guests, the superior noticed the ledger was missing and realized it must be in the hands of the magistrate. The ledger contained numerous records of corruption and illegal gains, and the superior knew he would be implicated if the truth came out, causing him great anxiety. He wrote to a clever official for advice, and the response said: "Be careful not to speak. When you see the magistrate, act as if nothing has happened, and continue to talk and laugh as usual. Instruct the clerk to withdraw several hundred taels of silver, prepare a document to explain the collection of miscellaneous taxes, and seal it in the office cabinet. The next day, send an officer to escort the silver away. At night, the officer should dig a hole in the wall to retrieve the ledger and bring it back to the inner office. The following day, summon the magistrate and the officer to inspect the ledger, claiming that the silver collected for miscellaneous taxes was stolen during the night, along with a piece of official document and a copy of the ledger. Report this to the judicial authorities; how could the magistrate dare to expose himself?" The superior followed the advice, promptly reported the incident, and requested punishment for himself. The magistrate, knowing the superior's intentions but fearing severe consequences, secretly destroyed the private ledger he had hidden.

    The commentator, Xiang Yan, remarked: "He deceives, and I deceive him in return; even stronger hands exist within strength." The Book of Documents says: "To deceive and create illusions." To this point, the situation is both unpredictable and laughable. People deceive the foolish and fear the wise; therefore, those who fear lawsuits will be followed by lawsuits. If one exposes the deceit and holds the winning tools, one will win without fighting.
